1601 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. English


1-99-3465


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


334 Ill. App. 3d 156; 778 N.E.2d 218; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 895; 268 Ill. Dec. 232



September 27, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal From The Circuit Court Of Cook County. Honorable Edward M. Fiala, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and cause remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) that dismissed as frivolous and patently without merit a petition for postconviction relief from his convictions of armed robbery and attempted murder of police officers, in which he also challenged the legality of the sentences imposed on him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-defendant were both tried on charges arising out of a bar hold-up in the course of which defendant was wounded in a shoot-out with police, but only defendant was convicted. The appellate court reviewed de novo defendant's claims of ineffective trial and appellate counsel, but found that trial counsel was not ineffective in making strategic decisions regarding the calling of witnesses, and that appellate counsel was not ineffective in failing to raise an issue of sufficiency of the evidence where the amount and quality of the evidence against defendant and his co-defendant were quite distinct. At the time defendant was sentenced, however, the sentencing ranges in effect for attempted murder of a police officer had been amended by Ill. Pub. Act 88-680 (effective 1995), which was subsequently held unconstitutional. Even though the sentences imposed on defendant would have been legal under pre-existing law, there was no telling how the change in ranges might have affected his sentences, so they were void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of the petition for relief from the convictions, but vacated the sentences imposed on the attempted murder counts, and remanded for resentencing.

 

1602 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jackson


No. 1-00-1803


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


333 Ill. App. 3d 962; 777 N.E.2d 626; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 873; 267 Ill. Dec. 823



September 24, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 30, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 20529. Honorable Michael P. Toomin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; mittimus corrected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of home invasion, two counts of armed robbery, and two counts of first degree murder, and sentenced him to concurrent sentences of natural life for the murder counts and concurrent 30-year prison terms for the armed robbery counts. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another barged into the home of the victims, robbed them and shot them. Although the State proceeded under a theory of accountability at trial, defendant was also charged with felony murder. The jury was instructed on felony murder and the prosecutor argued felony murder as an alternative theory. Thus, the appellate court found the evidence sufficient under either theory. Felony murder applied as an alternative theory to accountability because it was charged in the indictment, argued by the State at trial, and included in the jury instructions. Next, the prosecutor did not make improper remarks about the victims' children, misstate the law of accountability, or misstate the evidence. Isolated comments that the victims would miss milestones in their children's lives was not reversible error as they were not a material factor leading to defendant's conviction. Also, the prosecutor was permitted to give examples illustrating the application of the law to the facts, and correctly stated the law. Finally, Apprendi did not apply as, when imposing the natural life sentence, the trial court did not increase the penalty for first degree murder beyond the statutory maximum.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. Additionally, it was directed that mittimus be corrected.

 

1603 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Young


No. 1-00-3525


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


334 Ill. App. 3d 785; 779 N.E.2d 293; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 866; 268 Ill. Dec. 679



September 23, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied November 1, 2002. Released for Publication December 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 98 CR 22437. The Honorable Henry R. Simmons, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed and case was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), entered a judgment revoking defendant's probation and sentencing him to a prison term. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two stolen vehicle crimes. He pled guilty to both charges. He was approved to participate in residential treatment and was placed on probation. He was then arrested on a separate charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle. Shortly thereafter, the State petitioned for violation of probation and warrant alleging the possession of the stolen motor vehicle charge, failure to report to his probation department, and failure to comply with residential treatment rules. After a hearing, defendant stipulated that he previously had been convicted on two criminal charges. Defendant's probation was then revoked. He was sentenced to time in prison, with credit given to him for time he had already served. After the revocation was ordered, the appellate court found that defendant's prior sentence of probation was not void as the trial court had the discretion to sentence him to probation so he could be treated for drug abuse. It also found the mandatory sentencing scheme allowing for enhanced punishment based on prior convictions was permitted based on a narrow Apprendi exception, and that a remand was required to impose the correct credit for time served.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed and the case was remanded with directions.

 

1604 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Peshak


1-01-2455


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


333 Ill. App. 3d 1052; 777 N.E.2d 554; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 865; 267 Ill. Dec. 751



September 20, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 30, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Janice Bierman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of three counts of reckless homicide and two counts of aggravated driving under the influence of alcohol. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to a four-year prison term on the reckless homicide convictions and a concurrent three-year term on the aggravated driving under the influence of alcohol convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the reckless homicide statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/9-3(b) (West 2000), was unconstitutional because it created a mandatory presumption of recklessness. The appellate court held that the language of § 9-3(b) did not equate to a mandatory presumption of recklessness. Defendant also contended that the State failed to prove him guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held that the evidence showing defendant's blood alcohol concentration to be 0.13 three hours after the accident was sufficient to establish that he drove under the influence of alcohol. The appellate court also noted that the evidence was not so unreasonable, improbable, or so unsatisfactory as to warrant a reversal of the reckless homicide conviction. Defendant next argued that the trial court erred in failing to provide an interpreter for a witness. The appellate court held that due process did not require the presence of an interpreter since the witness gave appropriate responses to questions. Finally, as for the alleged violation of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 412(a)(ii), the appellate court held that the issue had been waived by defense counsel's failure to object at trial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

1605 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Trettenero v. Police Pension Fund


No. 2-01-0544


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 792; 776 N.E.2d 840; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 819; 267 Ill. Dec. 468



September 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 17, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 00--MRK--226. Honorable Michael J. Colwell, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant disability pension recipient sought review in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) of the decision of appellee pension fund board of trustees terminating her pension. The trial court affirmed the board's decision, and the recipient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The recipient was granted a nonduty police disability pension. The appellate court held the fact that she had to provide three medical evaluations to be found eligible for a pension, under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-115 (West 2000), and her pension could be terminated based on one evaluation, under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/3-116 (West 2000), did not violate due process, as she had an adequate hearing, or equal protection, as the legislature's treatment of potential disability pensioners and pension recipients was a rational distinction that served the legitimate goal of ensuring the pension fund's integrity. It was unnecessary to construe § 3-116 to require three evaluations, as its language was clear. Exclusion of the recipient's evidence of her mental state was not unconstitutional, as she had an adequate opportunity to offer evidence on this subject. If the exclusion was otherwise error, the error was harmless. The manifest weight of the evidence supported termination of her pension, as the pension board could choose which medical evidence to credit. The physician whose evaluation did not favor the recipient was not biased.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1606 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hill


Nos. 2-01-0522 & 2-01-0523 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 783; 776 N.E.2d 828; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 792; 267 Ill. Dec. 456



September 4, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 17, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 00--CM--1199. No. 00--CM--775. Honorable Donald H. Geiger, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a dancer and a nightclub employee, appealed from a judgment of the Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting them, respectively, of prostitution and soliciting for a prostitute.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were arrested for prostitution-related offenses after an undercover officer entered the nightclub where they worked and one defendant took money from the officer in exchange for the performance of a private erotic dance by the other defendant, in the course of which the officer's genital area was fondled through clothing. On appeal of their convictions, defendants argued that the statutory definition of prostitution, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11-14(a) (West 2000), was vague and overbroad. The appellate court held that the erotic dancing in question was not protected by the First Amendment, because it went beyond expressive dancing to physical touching. It was not vague, either. It was perfectly clear from the plain language, which prohibited any touching of sex organs for purposes of sexual arousal or gratification, that it reached touching through clothing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

 

1607 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Smith


No. 1-00-1204


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


333 Ill. App. 3d 622; 776 N.E.2d 781; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 757; 267 Ill. Dec. 409



August 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Robert Bertucci, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and cause was remanded for new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) of first-degree murder and attempted armed robbery. Defendant was sentenced to 50 years' imprisonment for first-degree murder and 30 years' concurrent imprisonment for attempted armed robbery. Defendant's motion for a new trial and supplemental motion for a new trial were denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another man robbed, shot, and killed a woman when she answered her apartment door, while an accomplice waited outside in a car. The police received conflicting information from witnesses and sources as to who was responsible for the crimes. On appeal, the court found that: (1) based on the repeated questioning of defendant at a police station, including the requestioning of defendant by one of the same detectives after defendant's assertion of his right to remain silent, defendant's statement that he was afraid, defendant's detention for over 60 hours preceding his first admission, and the lack of normal sleeping conditions, defendant's confession was not voluntary, and the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to suppress his confession; (2) 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/115-10.4 (West 2000) was not unconstitutionally vague; (3) the admission of a dead man's testimony before a grand jury violated defendant's Sixth Amendment right of confrontation; (4) the evidence was sufficient to prove defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt; and (5) on retrial, photographs of the victim after the shooting should not be shown to the jury.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1608 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brazee


No. 2-01-0332


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 43; 775 N.E.2d 652; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 766; 266 Ill. Dec. 812



August 21, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 98--CF--2536. Honorable Frederick J. Kapala, Judge, Presiding.
 People v. Brazee, 316 Ill. App. 3d 1230, 250 Ill. Dec. 430, 738 N.E.2d 646, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 839 (2d Dist. 2000).



DISPOSITION: Prior decision of this court vacated; judgment of trial court modified in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to sexual assault and was sentenced to 11 years. The appellate court vacated the judgment and remanded the cause with directions that defendant be sentenced to time served under the Illinois Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/1-1 et seq. (West 1996). The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) sentenced defendant accordingly, but ruled he stood convicted of a criminal offense. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that, when a court entered a disposition under the Act, pursuant to 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 405/5-4(6)(c)(ii), the resultant judgment constituted an adjudication of delinquency under the Act. The State argued § 5-4(6)(c)(ii), pertained only to sentencing and that the minor still stood convicted of a criminal offense. The appellate court concluded that, when the charge or charges enumerated in § 5- 4(6)(a) were resolved in the minor's favor, he or she was no longer excluded from the definition of delinquent minor. Thus, the appellate court concluded, by validating the criminal prosecution and verdict, § 5-4(6)(c)(ii) eliminated the need to retry a defendant in a formal delinquency hearing. The State also argued that, even if defendant was correct on the merits, he forfeited review by failing to file a motion to withdraw his guilty plea in the trial court. The appellate court disagreed, noting that defendant was not convicted of an offense mandating criminal prosecution under § 5-4(6)(a), and therefore the trial court had no statutory authority to enter the conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was modified by entering an adjudication of delinquency. Defendant's conviction for criminal sexual assault was vacated.

 

1609 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Townsend


No. 2-01-0222


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 375; 775 N.E.2d 262; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 768; 266 Ill. Dec. 700



August 21, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 92-CF-228. Honorable Raymond J. McKoski, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder and attempted murder. Defendant was sentenced to consecutive sentences of 55 years' imprisonment for murder and 30 years' imprisonment for attempted murder. The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences. The supreme court denied defendant's petition for leave to appeal. The Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) denied defendant's postconviction petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that the court of appeals should remand the cause so that defendant could allege facts in his petition that established that his delay in filing the petition was not due to his own culpable negligence. In reaching the conclusion that defendant's postconviction petition was properly dismissed and that this cause should not have been remanded for defendant to allege a lack of culpable negligence, the court of appeals noted that a cause need not be remanded where defendant has not alleged, in the trial court, a lack of culpable negligence. The court of appeals examined 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122/2.1(a)(2) (West 2000) and found that it provided that the court could dismiss a postconviction petition, if the claims of a defendant, sentenced to imprisonment, were frivolous or patently without merit.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's postconviction petition was affirmed.

 

1610 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ottinger (In re Ottinger)


NO. 4-01-0904


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 114; 775 N.E.2d 203; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 705; 266 Ill. Dec. 641


June 19, 2002, Argued  
August 14, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 18, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 99MR14. Honorable Elizabeth A. Robb, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) dismissing his petition for conditional release and granting the State's motion for a finding of no probable cause under the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/1 to 99 (West 2000), after a hearing, and a review of the examinations of defendant by defendant's psychologist and the State's psychologist.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's contention that it was plain error to fail to appoint neutral examiners was rejected, as was his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel for failure to object to the appointment. A hearing on discharge was not required because the trial court determined there was not probable cause to believe that defendant was no longer a sexually violent person. The procedure employed by the trial court comported with § 65(b)(1) ( 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 207/65(b)(1) (West 2000)) and was not equivalent to entry of summary judgment. Defendant failed to show that it was not substantially probable that he would engage in acts of sexual violence if conditionally released. The trial court did not abuse its discretion by determining that defendant was not entitled to a full hearing on conditional release or discharge. The Act did not violate defendant's right to due process. Defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel for failure to make a constitutional challenge to the Act lacked merit. Defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel for failing to ensure that defendant's psychologist filed a timely report, as any error did not prejudice defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1611 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brunt


No. 1-00-2744


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 974; 775 N.E.2d 11; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 712; 266 Ill. Dec. 449



August 14, 2002, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dennis Porter, Judge Presiding.
Court of appeals' prior opinion: People v. Brunt, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 202 (Ill. App. Ct. Mar. 27, 2002).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' prior opinion was modified upon denial of rehearing and trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and vacated, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which dismissed his post-conviction petition without an evidentiary hearing for being untimely, as well as being frivolous and patently without merit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued on appeal, inter alia, that under Apprendi, his consecutive sentences for murder and attempted murder were unconstitutional, and that one of the convictions for armed robbery must be vacated since a criminal defendant could not be convicted of both felony murder and the underlying predicate felony. The appellate court agreed with the trial court's determination that defendant failed to raise the gist of a constitutional claim and thus the trial court properly dismissed his postconviction petition. In addition, the appellate court advised that sentences which ran consecutively to each other were not converted into a single sentence, and because consecutive sentences remained distinct, there was no Apprendi conflict inasmuch as Apprendi only addressed sentences for individual crimes. Therefore, the appellate court found that defendant's sentences did not violate Apprendi. However, the appellate court noted that the State conceded that defendant's conviction and sentence on the armed robbery count was improper and should be vacated.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the dismissal of the petition for postconviction relief. However, the appellate court vacated defendant's conviction and sentence on the count of the indictment alleging armed robbery.

 

1612 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Diggs v. Snyder


NO. 5-01-0634


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 189; 775 N.E.2d 40; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 702; 266 Ill. Dec. 478; 116 A.L.R.5th 687



August 13, 2002, Order Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Motion to Publish Granted August 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Randolph County. No. 01-MR-31. Honorable William A. Schuwerk, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Randolph County (Illinois) dismissing the inmate's complaint that was filed under the Illinois Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 35/1 et seq., against defendant Illinois Department of Corrections employees.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed that he was improperly ticketed for gang or unauthorized organization activity when correctional officers seized an Islam-related pamphlet that condemned all correctional officers. This condemnation included a pledge that was signed by some inmates. The inmate sought a declaration that the employees' actions violated the Illinois Religious Freedom Restoration Act, 775 Ill. Comp. Stat. 35/1 et seq. The appellate court found that the inmate failed to show that the seizure placed a substantial burden on his free exercise of religion. The inmate did not show that possession of the pamphlet was required by the basic tenets of Islam. Furthermore, the Muslim chaplain said that the pamphlet was not condoned or disseminated by his office. Even if the seizure of the pamphlet was a burden on the inmate's practice of Islam, the seizure was lawful, because the pamphlet's inflammatory language could have been construed as a threat to the prison's security. Finally, it was the inmate's burden, not the department's, to submit the pamphlet for approval, or the inmate had to run the risk of being ticketed for possession of it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1613 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Toia v. People


No. 1-00-3999


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


333 Ill. App. 3d 523; 776 N.E.2d 599; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 699; 267 Ill. Dec. 227



August 12, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. Y2-663-369. The Honorable Joseph Urso, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed from an order of the Cook County Circuit Court denying expungement of the record of his drunk driving conviction. He challenged the constitutionality of two amended statutes that prohibited the expungement of his records.


OVERVIEW: At the time petitioner was convicted of drunk driving, Illinois statutes permitted him to petition for expungement of his criminal record five years after completing probation. During the five-year waiting period, however, the Illinois legislature enacted Ill. Pub. Act 89-637, which amended both 20 Ill. Comp. Stat. 2630/5 and 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-6-3.1 to preclude expungement in the case of drunk driving convictions. Petitioner argued that these amendments violated the federal and Illinois prohibitions against ex post facto laws contained in U.S. Const. art. I, § 9, and Ill. Const. art. I, § 16. The appellate court held, first, that there was no question that the plain language of the statute prohibited the expungement of petitioner's record. It went on to consider whether the amendments unconstitutionally created a new offense or increased petitioner's punishment. By analogy to constitutional case law involving sex offender registration and notification laws, the appellate court concluded that, even though the ban on expungement was clearly intended to have a deterrent effect, its primary aim was not punitive, but the protection of the public, so it was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying relief.

 

1614 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Flowers


Nos. 3-01-0083 through 3-01-0085 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 60; 775 N.E.2d 96; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 669; 266 Ill. Dec. 534



August 5, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 13, 2002.
Appeal granted by People v. Flowers, 202 Ill. 2d 629, 787 N.E.2d 161, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 2000, 272 Ill. Dec. 346 (2002)
Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Flowers, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2278 (Ill., Nov. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Nos. 98-CF-1503, 98-CF-1623 and 98-CF-1741. Honorable Stephen D. White, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to an agreement in which the State would recommend four-year concurrent prison sentences, defendant pled guilty to seven counts of forgery in three consolidated cases. The Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, rejected the recommendation, sentenced her to concurrent five-year terms of imprisonment, and ordered her to pay restitution and costs. Her motion to reconsider sentence was denied. She appealed.


OVERVIEW: Before accepting her plea, the trial judge told defendant that he would not be bound by the State's sentencing recommendation, and that she could receive up to 3 consecutive sentences of 10 years' imprisonment. He did not admonish her that she could be ordered to pay restitution. The State argued the appellate court lacked jurisdiction to hear defendant's appeal, as she failed to comply with Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d) by not filing a motion to withdraw her guilty plea. The appellate court disagreed. As the trial judge did not sentence defendant within the terms of the plea agreement, defendant was not obliged to file a motion to withdraw the plea, but properly filed the motion to reconsider the sentence under Rule 604(d). Defendant's untimely filing of her motion to reconsider, in violation of Rule 604(d), did not deprive the appellate court of jurisdiction. As the trial court failed to admonish defendant she could be required to pay restitution, its restitution order was improper. Finally, the order that the department of correction (DOC) withhold 50 percent of defendant's prison wages for court costs was unauthorized by statute and therefore void.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated those parts of the order that required defendant to pay restitution and the DOC to withhold 50 percent of the defendant's income to pay restitution and court costs, but affirmed the remainder of the trial court's order.

 

1615 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Fedanzo v. City of Chi.


1-01-0582


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


333 Ill. App. 3d 339; 775 N.E.2d 26; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 754; 266 Ill. Dec. 464



August 2, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied July 30, 2002. Modified Opinion August 2, 2002. Released for Publication September 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presiding.
Court of appeals' prior opinion: Fedanzo v. City of Chicago, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 413 (Ill. App. Ct. May 24, 2002).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' prior opinion was replaced and trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former public employee of defendant city appealed from an order of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), denying his petition for writ of certiorari for review of a decision of defendant personnel board terminating his employment for failure to reside in the city.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked as a unionized electrical mechanic at a large regional airport located within the city. Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 2-152-340 (1990) required city employees to live in the city. On a tip, city personnel investigators conducted surveillance both at the city apartment where the employee claimed to live and at the suburban home of his family. The personnel board determined that he violated the ordinance and lied to investigators, and it discharged him. The appellate court upheld the action. Even though the airport in question received funding from federal and airline sources, it was still the city airport, and the residency rule had a rational relationship to the civic welfare, so it was not unconstitutional. Furthermore, the board's determination was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The record did not indicate that the employee was threatened with discharge if he failed to testify, which would have violated the collective bargaining agreement. Finally, the exclusionary rule did not necessarily apply in non-criminal settings. In the instant case, the benefit of excluding the evidence would have outweighed the likely social costs.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of review.

People v. Outlaw


No. 1-01-2555


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT


2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 674

Writ of certiorari denied Outlaw v. Illinois, 537 U.S. 1122, 123 S. Ct. 858, 154 L. Ed. 2d 804, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 94 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 76 C 2091. Honorable Diane Gordon Cannon, Judge Presiding.
People v. Outlaw, 311 Ill. App. 3d 1069, 766 N.E.2d 689, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 1749, 262 Ill. Dec. 769 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2000)
People v. Outlaw, 329 Ill. App. 3d 1232, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 3805 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2002)
People v. Outlaw, 75 Ill. App. 3d 626, 394 N.E.2d 541, 1979 Ill. App. LEXIS 3122, 31 Ill. Dec. 339 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1979)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissing as frivolous and patently without merit his successive pro se petition for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was sentenced to two concurrent terms of 150 to 300 years after his conviction of two murders. A quarter-century after the affirmance of his conviction and sentence, in one of a series of post-conviction petitions, he argued that his indeterminate sentences violated the rule of Apprendi, in that a jury had not determined precisely what his sentence should be. The appellate court held that Illinois case law had long established that an indeterminate sentence was to be treated as a life sentence, and that life sentences were well within the statutory range for murder. Thus, defendant's sentences did not expose him to a greater possible punishment than authorized by the jury's verdict, and there had been no Apprendi violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

1618 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Wakeland v. City of Urbana


NO. 4-01-0991


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 1131; 776 N.E.2d 1194; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 647; 267 Ill. Dec. 543



July 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified On Denial of Rehearing September 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 95C1453. Honorable Ann A. Einhorn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners filed an action against defendant City of Urbana (Illinois), seeking a judgment that a city ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to them. Defendant adjacent landowners filed a petition to intervene. The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) granted the adjacent landowners' petition to intervene and following a bench trial, the court entered judgment in favor of the city. The landowners appealed.


OVERVIEW: Two people bought three lots on a street in Urbana, Illinois, when the lots were zoned for multi-family residential use. Four years later, the city passed an ordinance that changed the zoning on the lots to single family residential use. Although the landowners were offered $ 150,000 for their lots after the zoning change and could have sold the lots at a profit, they claimed the properties were worth more than $ 150,000 and sued seeking a declaration that the ordinance was unconstitutional as applied to them. The appellate court reviewed the criteria set down by the Supreme Court of Illinois in prior decisions and held that (1) the landowners did not have a right to count on an indefinite continuation of the multi-family residential use zoning classification; (2) because the landowners had not applied for a building permit or made substantial expenditures on their lots, they had no vested interest in the multi-family residential use zoning classification; and (3) although property located within two blocks of the landowners' lots was zoned for multi-family residential use, the city had a valid reason for down-zoning lots on the street where the landowners' lots were located.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Graves


No. 3-00-0953


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


332 Ill. App. 3d 685; 773 N.E.2d 1243; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 611; 266 Ill. Dec. 173



July 22, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for publication August 26, 2002.
Appeal granted by People v. Graves, 202 Ill. 2d 631, 787 N.E.2d 162, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1929 (2002)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by People v. Graves, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1423 (Ill., Sept. 18, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 13th Judicial Circuit, Bureau County, Illinois. No. 98-CF-62. Honorable Scott Madson Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the Circuit Court for the 13th Judicial Circuit, Bureau County, Illinois, which convicted him, after he pled guilty, to the unauthorized theft of currency in excess of $ 10,000 but less than $ 100,000. The trial court sentenced defendant to 12 years' imprisonment and ordered him to pay $ 20,000 in restitution.


OVERVIEW: The victims of defendant's crime were 71 and 93 years old. Before defendant entered his plea, the trial judge admonished him of the rights he would forego by pleading guilty. The judge also explained the sentencing range for a Class 2 felony and informed defendant he was eligible for an extended sentence due to the victims' ages. Ordinarily, defendant would have been sentenced according to the Class 2 felony sentencing range of three to seven years with the possibility of probation under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3(b)(1) (1998). However, because of the ages of the victims, he was sentenced pursuant to § 5-5-3.2(b)(4)(ii), which carried a sentencing range of a mandatory 7 to 14 years, with no possibility of probation. The appellate court held the penalties for unauthorized theft and theft by deception similarly violated the proportionate penalties clause of Ill. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 11, since they required the same elements, yet carried significantly different penalties. Defendant failed to include the issue of the propriety of the restitution order in his motions. Thus, he waived the issue.


OUTCOME: The trial court's extended term sentence was unconstitutional as applied and was vacated. The penalties for unauthorized theft and theft by deception were unconstitutionally disproportionate. The trial court's restitution order with the suggestion that payment be re-directed was affirmed if appropriate. The matter was remanded for proper sentencing.

U.S.G. Italian Marketcaffe v. City of Chi.


No. 1-00-3294


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 1008; 775 N.E.2d 47; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 607; 266 Ill. Dec. 485



July 19, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 4, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 L 050208. The Honorable Thomas P. Quinn, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and director of revenue, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff restaurants, where the restaurants claimed that the city's litter tax ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 3-43-010 et seq., violated state law, violated Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970), and was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: The litter tax ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 3-43-010 et seq., was passed in an effort to control the amount of litter resulting from carry-out food. The ordinance imposed a tax on the sale of food prepared for immediate consumption by a place for eating, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 3-43-020 (2000). A place for eating was defined as a business engaged in the sale of food at retail, where the business provided for on-premises consumption of the food it sold, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 3-43-010(A)(5) (2000). The ordinance exempted food that was not carry-out food, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 3-43-030(A) (2000). 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-42-5 (West 1998) authorized the city to tax places for eating. Because the ordinance taxed places for eating under § 11-42-5, the appellate court found it did not violate 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-11-6a (West 1998). The ordinance violated the uniformity clause, Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2, as it did not bear a reasonable relationship to its object. It taxed items that were not likely to cause litter, food sold for on-premises consumption, while not taxing other items that were likely to cause litter, food sold by carry-out-only businesses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. McCormick


NO. 4-00-0214


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


332 Ill. App. 3d 491; 774 N.E.2d 392; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 600; 266 Ill. Dec. 286



July 17, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 15, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 00CF44. Honorable Donald D. Bernardi, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, vacated, in part, and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for making a harassing call. Defendant's motion to dismiss was denied. Defendant was found guilty and sentenced to three years' imprisonment, ordered to pay $ 270 in restitution, and assessed a $ 20 fine under § 10(c) of the Illinois Victims Assistance Act, codified at 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 240/10(c) (West 2000). The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) denied defendant's motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that § 2(b)(5) of the Communications Act, codified at 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-8(b)(5), violated his constitutional right to equal protection; § 2(b)(5) violated the proportionate penalties clause, Ill. Const. art. I, § 11; the trial court had no statutory authority to order restitution for the parking tickets; and only the court, not the circuit clerk, had authority to impose the fine. The appellate court upheld that the legislature's classification of burglary as a forcible felony since there was a reasonable argument in favor of the classification. The appellate court found no violation of the proportionate penalties clause since the offenses pointed to by defendant were similar and contained many of the same elements, and the language of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-8 (West 2000) included in its definition of forcible felonies a clause to include any felony involving the use or threat of force or violence. In vacating the restitution order, the appellate court noted that such an order was plain error since a damages award was inappropriate where the claimant's own illegal acts resulted in the claimed damages.


OUTCOME: The trial court's orders that defendant pay restitution and a fine were vacated. In all other respects defendant's sentence was affirmed.

People v. James

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting him on jury verdict of criminal sexual assault of a child.

Coyne v. Osf Healthcare Sys.


No. 3-01-0982


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


332 Ill. App. 3d 717; 773 N.E.2d 732; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 595; 265 Ill. Dec. 968


December 31, 2001, Assigned; April 10, 2002, Submitted  
July 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 19, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the Tenth Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 01-L-228. Honorable John A. Barra, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee patient filed a negligence action against a medical center and named appellant doctor as a respondent in discovery, pursuant to 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-402 (1998). The doctor filed a motion to quash the summons that was served on him, but the Circuit Court of the Tenth Judicial Circuit, Peoria County (Illinois), denied his motion. The doctor appealed.


OVERVIEW: A patient sued a medical center and named a doctor who worked as a medical resident at the medical center, but who had since left Illinois and established a medical practice in another state, as a respondent in discovery. The doctor filed a motion to quash the summons that was served on him, arguing that, as he no longer resided in Illinois, the trial court lacked personal jurisdiction over him. The appellate court held that: (1) 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-402 (1998) allowed the patient to name the doctor as a respondent in discovery for the purpose of securing discovery and required the doctor to respond to discovery in the same manner as though he had been named as a defendant; and (2) because the patient's action against the doctor arose from the doctor's employment with the medical center in Illinois, the doctor had sufficient minimum contacts with Illinois to satisfy traditional notions of fair play and substantial justice under the United States Constitution.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Vasquez


Nos. 1-00-0805 & 1-00-1083 Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 269; 772 N.E.2d 922; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 539; 265 Ill. Dec. 551



June 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 7, 2002. Released for Publication August 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 C660853, No. 99 C6-60854 (Cons.). Honorable George M. Morrissey, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and case was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pled guilty to two counts of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and was sentenced by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to serve two concurrent extended nine-year terms of imprisonment based on a prior conviction, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that where the trial court failed to admonish defendant as to the nature of the charges and failed to inform him of the maximum and minimum sentences prescribed by law, the trial court erred under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402. The trial court failed to inform defendant: (1) of the minimum and maximum sentences that he was eligible to receive, (2) that he could receive an extended-term sentence, and (3) that he would be required to submit to a 10-year period of supervision following his incarceration. This was improper. The trial court's responsibility under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402 was not negated by the fact that defendant had negotiated a plea agreement with the State. Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402 required the trial court to spell out to defendant the maximum and minimum sentences prescribed by law.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was reversed and the trial court was ordered to allow defendant to withdraw his guilty pleas, vacate his conviction and sentence, and permit defendant to plead anew.

Allen v. Woodfield Chevrolet


No. 1-01-3131


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 605; 773 N.E.2d 1145; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 543; 266 Ill. Dec. 75



June 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 20, 2002. Released for Publication September 4, 2002.
Rehearing denied by, 08/20/2002
Appeal granted by Allen v. Woodfield Chevrolet, Inc., 202 Ill. 2d 597, 787 N.E.2d 154, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 2078 (2002)
Affirmed by Allen v. Woodfield Chevrolet, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1493 (Ill., Oct. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CH 16228. Honorable Dorothy Kirie Kinnaird, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff purchasers sued defendants, auto dealership and collection service, seeking damages in connection with the purchase of a vehicle. Count II of the complaint sought a declaratory judgment that certain provisions of the Illinois Consumer Fraud and Deceptive Business Practices Act were unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered judgment for the dealership on count II, and the purchasers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the 1993 and 1996 amendments, Ill. Pub. Act 87-1140 and Ill. Pub. Act 89-144, to section 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/10a violated Illinois' constitutional prohibition against special legislation. Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970) prohibited legislation which arbitrarily discriminated in favor of a select group. The amendments in question imposed penalties on both consumers and car dealers for refusing to settle cases, and limited the ability of the consumer to receive punitive damages and added a notice requirement. The amendments were urged because the legislature perceived that in cases involving new and used car dealers the availability of punitive damages and awards of attorney fees encouraged consumers to file lawsuits rather than attempting to work out a settlement. The appellate court held that in the present case there was not enough evidence that a perceived crisis existed in the auto dealership industry to require the measures. Moreover, even if the appellate court were to assume that the problem existed, there was no basis for distinguishing between fraud committed by auto dealers and others who defrauded consumers.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting a dealership's motion for judgment on the pleadings as to count II of the complaint was reversed. The denial of the purchasers' motion for judgment on the pleadings was reversed and remanded to the trial court for the entry of an order granting judgment on the pleadings on count II for the purchasers, and for further proceedings.

People v. Johnson


No. 1-00-1305


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 81; 773 N.E.2d 155; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 545; 265 Ill. Dec. 793



June 28, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 15781. Honorable John Moran, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Case was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant challenged the dismissal of his petition for relief pursuant to the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. Defendant had pleaded guilty to delivery of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that since defendant could attack a judgment at any time when he had not been properly admonished pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(b), defendant's claim had not been procedurally defaulted, and therefore there was no issue of waiver. The circuit court's failure to give any admonishments as to defendant's appellate rights failed both the completeness and the accuracy requirements of due process. When a defendant was not given Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 605(b) admonishments and subsequently failed to file a motion to withdraw his plea of guilty, the cause should be remanded for further proceedings. When a trial judge failed to provide the proper Rule 605(b) admonishments and defendant failed to follow Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 604(d), the cause had to be remanded to the trial court so that defendant could be given the correct admonishments and allowed the opportunity to withdraw his guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The appellate court remanded the case for defendant to be admonished so that he would have an opportunity to file an amended motion to withdraw his plea of guilty if he desired.

People v. Daniels


1-97-4354


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 198; 773 N.E.2d 119; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 549; 265 Ill. Dec. 757



June 28, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:  [***1] THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.

UNPUBLISHED IN PART PURSUANT TO SUPREME COURT RULE 23.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication August 12, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Daniels v. Illinois, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 1826 (U.S. Mar. 3, 2003).
Appeal denied by People v. Daniels, 201 Ill. 2d 583, 786 N.E.2d 189, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1628 (2002)
Appeal denied by People v. Daniels, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 49 (Ill., Feb. 5, 2003)
Writ of certiorari denied Daniels v. Illinois, 155 L. Ed. 2d 204, 123 S. Ct. 1363, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 1826 (U.S., 2003)
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Daniels, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 793 (Ill., June 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph J. Urso, Judge Presiding.
People v. Daniels, 272 Ill. App. 3d 325, 650 N.E.2d 224, 1994 Ill. App. LEXIS 1526 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1994)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting her, at her second trial, of murdering her boyfriend. She argued that the trial court erred in failing to hold a hearing on her motions to suppress, in quashing her subpoenas, in not allowing her medical records to be taken to the jury room, and imposing an extended term sentence.


OVERVIEW: When defendant and her brothers were questioned in the murder of her boyfriend, the interrogation took place at Area 2, a police district in Chicago, Illinois, in which officers were later determined to have routinely tortured suspects during the time period in question. At defendant's retrial, she sought to re-open the issue of denial of her motions to suppress evidence, but the appellate court held that the first ruling was the law of the case, because it was clear that the original judge had considered all the constitutional issues that defendant sought to raise in her second attempt. Subpoenas regarding incidences of torture in Area 2 were properly quashed, because defendant had never raised the issue of her brothers' torture before, and never claimed that she had been tortured. Since defendant failed to lay a foundation regarding the medical records indicating that the victim had abused her, they could not have been admitted in evidence or taken into the jury room. Since defendant's appeal was heard in an appellate district that applied the Apprendi rule to extended term sentences for heinous or brutal crimes, her 80-year sentence was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction, but vacated defendant's sentence and remanded for resentencing.

City of Chi. v. Taylor


No. 1-01-0414


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 583; 774 N.E.2d 22; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 550; 266 Ill. Dec. 244



June 28, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 16, 2002. Released for Publication September 4, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 MC1 318256. Honorable Mark Ballard Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant criminal pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to unlawful discharge of a firearm, possession of a firearm without a Firearm Owners Identification Card, and possession of an unregistered firearm. Plaintiff city moved to confiscate and destroy his firearms, and the criminal's father petitioned for return of one of them. The trial court granted the father's petition, and the city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father loaned the criminal a shotgun. The appellate court held Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 8-20-040 (1999), requiring its registration, and Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 8-20-220 (1999), requiring its destruction, were permissible exercises of home rule powers not contrary to Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6, as they concerned the city's interest in reducing firearm-related deaths and were not preempted. The ordinance allowed possession of a registered firearm, so it did not violate Ill. Const. art. I, § 22, allowing people to bear arms. The right to bear arms was not fundamental, so the correct due process analysis of the ordinance was the rational basis test, and it was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest in regulating firearms and lawfully applied to property lent by an innocent owner to an unlawful user. When the unregistered shotgun entered the city, it was contraband per se, subject to confiscation and destruction. The ordinance appropriately exempted non-resident owners, and its definition of antique firearms was neither arbitrary nor capricious. It clearly stated when the shotgun had to be registered.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order directing release of the shotgun was reversed.

Appeal denied by People v. Carter, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 58 (Ill., Feb. 5, 2003)
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Carter, 204 Ill. 2d 666, 790 N.E.2d 377, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 795, 274 Ill. Dec. 1 (2003)
Different results reached on reconsideration by People v. Carter, 346 Ill. App. 3d 1173, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 2723 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CR 32391. Honorable Stanley J. Sacks, Judge Presiding.
People v. Carter, 311 Ill. App. 3d 1066, 766 N.E.2d 687, 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 1664, 262 Ill. Dec. 767 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2000)



DISPOSITION: Post-conviction court's judgment was affirmed, in part, vacated, in part, and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of second-degree murder. He was denied leave to appeal and filed a pro se petition under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. The trial court denied the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that defendant's notice of appeal was timely filed. The record indicated that defendant's notice of appeal, which was mailed from the correctional center, had to have been mailed either on or prior to the cut-off date of November 10, 2000. A case holding that any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum, other than the fact of a prior conviction, had to be submitted to a jury and proven beyond a reasonable doubt applied retroactively to defendant's timely filed postconviction petition. The cause was remanded to the circuit court for imposition of a nonextended-term sentence for a second degree murder.


OUTCOME: The judgment regarding defendant's conviction was affirmed, the extended-term sentence of 28 years was vacated, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court for imposition of a nonextended-term sentence for second degree murder.

 

1630 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nolan


Nos. 1-99-0846 & 1-99-4197


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 215; 773 N.E.2d 105; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 555; 265 Ill. Dec. 743



June 28, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Robert Bertucci, Judge Presding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in separate trials, convicted defendants of criminal drug conspiracy, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/405.1, and sentenced defendants accordingly. Defendants appealed the judgments.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that the trial court erred in summarily granting the State's motion for substitution of a judge and other errors. Defendants maintained that the judge to which the case was initially assigned mistakenly believed that it had no choice but to grant the motion and failed to realize its authority to inquire into the actual grounds for the motion. Defendants argued that, because the State's motion was prompted by the original judge's willingness to entertain a defense motion for a bond reduction, the motion should not have been granted. The appellate court held that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/114-5(a) allowed the State to move for substitution of a judge without inquiry by the court. The one exception to this rule was where it appeared that such motions were being used to thwart the chief judge of a circuit court's exercise of independent assignment authority. Defendants did not allege that the prosecution employed such a tactic. The appellate court further held the original judge's indication that he intended to hear a motion to reduce bond was not a substantial ruling that would have precluded the State from exercising its right to automatic substitution of judge.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

In re County Collector


No. 1-00-2499


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


332 Ill. App. 3d 277; 774 N.E.2d 832; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 559; 266 Ill. Dec. 393



June 28, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE FRANCIS BARTH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, sustained 5 of 25 objections filed by appellee taxpayers challenging the legality of certain property taxes levied by the appellant city. The city appealed the trial court's order and the taxpayers cross-appealed the pretrial dismissal of one of their objections.


OVERVIEW: The city contested, inter alia, the trial court's ruling on two objections which claimed that the city (1) unlawfully underestimated revenue for the library maintenance and operation fund; and (2) overestimated the loss in collections for the debt service funds and the public building commission fund. The appellate court held that the transcript showed that the trial court sustained the objection regarding the library maintenance fund based on a pattern of historical underestimation. However, no testimony showed that the city had certainty in regard to the estimate prior to the 1989 appropriations ordinance, and the objection could not be sustained, and while there was testimony that the city had used a five percent estimate for loss of collections for decades, the record showed that the city had relied on financial reports and estimated a rate consistent with the rates shown therein. The increases in second year collections were insufficient to sustain a tax objection. The trial court also erred in dismissing the taxpayers' objection that the city illegally diverted surplus funds for another purpose, because material questions of fact remained regarding the objection.


OUTCOME: That part of the trial court's judgment which sustained the objections as to the underestimation of revenue and overestimation of the loss in collections, and which dismissed the objection as to illegal diversion of funds, was reversed. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed, and the case was remanded.

A.G. Edwards v. Sec'y of State


NO. 5-00-0525


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 1101; 772 N.E.2d 362; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 869; 265 Ill. Dec. 324



June 27, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 00-MR-117. Honorable John M. Goodwin, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, securities salesmen and securities dealer, moved the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) to quash subpoenas by appellant state securities department for the production of personal banking information of the salesmen. The department moved to enforce the subpoenas. The trial court granted appellees' motion and denied that of the department, and the department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The department said it needed the salesmen's personal banking information as their office kept no "business" account into which their commissions were deposited before disbursement to them. The appellate court held the salesmen were not required by 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/8(I)(1), (I)(3) (West 2000), or Ill. Admin. Code tit. 14, § 130.825(c)(1) (2000) to preserve personal banking information, nor did 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/11(D)(1) (West 2000) allow the department to audit such information from them. The documents the department sought were irrelevant to a routine audit. In balancing the department's need for official intrusion, under the Securities Law, 815 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1 et seq., against the salesmen's constitutionally protected interests, the subpoenas violated the salesmen's privacy rights, absent an indicia of fraud. Some bank accounts were held jointly with spouses. Some information sought was available from the dealer's home office, but the department did not seek the information there. Creating a "business" account at the salesmen's office would not lessen an opportunity for fraud or provide greater information to the department.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Allen (in Re Allen)


No. 2-00-1379


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 996; 772 N.E.2d 354; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 528; 265 Ill. Dec. 316



June 25, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 99--MR--690. Honorable Christopher C. Starck, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent convicted sex offender appealed from a judgment of the Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) granting the State's petition, pursuant to the Illinois Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/1 et seq., to commit the offender to the custody of a state agency, after a jury determined that he was likely to re-offend.


OVERVIEW: Over the years, the offender had been convicted of several sex offenses against children, most of them involving his young daughter. Although the State of Illinois had not initially petitioned for his classification as a sexually violent person subject to commitment when the offender was first eligible for mandatory supervised release, it filed a petition when his release was revoked for further molestations. The appellate court held that the petition was timely, because the 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/15(b)(2) time limit for filing a petition did not specify a particular release date as the single date near which a petition had to be filed. That court also held that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/25(e), which provided for appointment of a medical expert for an indigent sex offender, did not violate the offender's due process guarantees, even though the State had the resources to pay many experts. Finally, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence of the offender's prior sex offenses, because it was critical to the jury's determination of whether he was likely to re-offend.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Pinkonsly


No. 2-99-1060


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 984; 772 N.E.2d 855; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 620; 265 Ill. Dec. 484



June 20, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied July 22, 2002. Released for Publication July 22, 2002.
Rehearing denied by, 07/22/2002
Appeal granted by, 12/05/2002
Appeal denied by People v. Pinkonsly, 202 Ill. 2d 648, 787 N.E.2d 165, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1937, 272 Ill. Dec. 350 (2002)
Reversed by People v. Pinkonsly, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2281 (Ill., Nov. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. Nos. 89-CF-916, 90-CF-451. Honorable Ward S. Arnold and Susan Fayette Hutchinson, Judges, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and vacated, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his conviction for unlawful delivery of a controlled substance and narcotics racketeering, for which he was sentenced to concurrent terms of 30 years' imprisonment, was affirmed on appeal, defendant petitioned the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) to reduce his sentence. The trial court denied his petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought review of his sentence more than six years after he was sentenced. The appellate court held the State waived the issue of timeliness by not raising it in the trial court. The statutory elements of his narcotics racketeering conviction were implicitly contained in his unlawful-delivery-of-cocaine convictions, rendering the unlawful-delivery-of-cocaine counts lesser-included offenses. His convictions of, and sentences for, unlawful delivery of a controlled substance had to be vacated, and his counsel was ineffective for not raising the issue in his petition to reduce his sentence, under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1401 (West 1998), as he would have prevailed on the issue. Defendant could not show he was prejudiced by counsel's failure to raise the trial court's failure to state the basis for his extended term sentence for narcotics racketeering, and there was a basis in the record for finding an aggravating factor justifying defendant's sentence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences for unlawful delivery of cocaine were vacated. His conviction and sentence for narcotics racketeering were affirmed.

People v. Simmons


No. 2-00-0695


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 416; 770 N.E.2d 1271; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 503; 264 Ill. Dec. 575



June 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 12, 2002. Vacated, Appeal denied: People v. Simmons, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 29 (Ill. Feb. 5, 2003).
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Simmons, 783 N.E.2d 32, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 29 (Ill., 2003)
Vacated by, Substituted opinion at People v. Simmons, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 977 (Ill. App. Ct., July 29, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 95-CF-698. Honorable Richard W. Vidal, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Simmons, 297 Ill. App. 3d 1133, 737 N.E.2d 714, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 4799 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, Illinois, convicted defendant of first-degree murder. The trial court sentenced him to 80 years' imprisonment, and denied his motion to reconsider his sentence. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant quarreled with, then fatally shot, the victim. In imposing extended-term sentencing, the trial court noted his substantial criminal history, the execution-style manner in which he shot the helpless and wounded victim in the back of the head, and found "brutal and heinous" behavior indicative of wanton cruelty. Defendant claimed that prosecutorial misconduct and ineffective assistance of counsel deprived him of a fair trial. The instant court held that as the prosecutor's remarks were reasonable inferences based on the evidence, defendant suffered no prejudice. Defendant failed to show a reasonable probability that the outcome of his trial would have been different had defense counsel objected to any comments made during the prosecutor's closing argument. The trial court's "brutal or heinous" finding did not create a new or independent crime, but was merely an aggravating circumstance. Since defendant's sentence was not beyond the maximum authorized by statute, there was no "sentence enhancement," and defendant's Apprendi claim failed. In imposing sentence, the trial court considered the statutory factors, and the instant court would not disturb the sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Avant


NO. 4-00-0183


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 144; 771 N.E.2d 420; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 827; 264 Ill. Dec. 716



June 17, 2002, Decided  
June 17, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 99CF701. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.
Court of appeals' prior opinion: People v. Avant, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 459, (Ill. App. Ct. 4th Dist. June 20, 2001).



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' prior opinion was replaced and trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of a controlled substance in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) and argued that: (1) the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence and (2) his conviction should be reversed because it was based, in part, on a police laboratory report admitted into evidence pursuant to a statute which the Supreme Court of Illinois declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by an officer walking the same section of a street several days in a row in a high drug activity area. The officer stopped defendant and asked if he had any illegal substances and defendant handed over a bag of crack cocaine. At the time he approached defendant, the officer had not observed defendant committing a crime and defendant did not appear about to commit a crime. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because it was obtained in an illegal seizure in violation of the Fourth Amendment. The trial court erred by denying defendant's motion to suppress because despite the fact that the officer had observed defendant's behavior for two to three days and knew the area to be a high drug-trafficking area, circumstances were not sufficient to make a Terry stop. Because the only evidence of defendant's crime was to be suppressed, the court reversed defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

Myers v. Mundelein College


Nos. 1-99-3190 and 1-99-4129, Consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


331 Ill. App. 3d 710; 771 N.E.2d 1113; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 468; 265 Ill. Dec. 154



June 11, 2002, Decided  
June 11, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 23, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Nos. 96 CH 1100, 99 CH 9232. Honorables Michael B. Getty and Albert Green, Judges Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) arising from breach of contract claims brought by three plaintiff faculty members against defendant college, two faculty members argued on appeal that the dismissal of their declaratory judgment action was in error. The third faculty member challenged the denial of her motion in the original chancery action for additional relief under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-701(c).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found the two faculty members were entitled to future damages under Illinois law, but the issue was not solely resolvable through a declaratory judgment. The court could not make a finding on the effect of another case on the claims for damages unless and until the issue was raised by the college. Whether the faculty members were entitled to posttrial damages did not turn solely on an interpretation of the other case, but on an analysis of the rule that damages for breach of contract beyond the date of trial were barred as speculative. The term "future damages" was imprecise. 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-701(c) empowered the trial court to assess money damages based on the trial court's earlier declaration that a defendant breached the tenure contract. The third faculty member's motion for additional relief under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-701(c) was compensable in a traditional action at law, as the faculty member had more than one remedy, and selecting one of them was not a bar to another remedy as the remedies were not inconsistent and the other party materially changed position in reliance on the manifestation.


OUTCOME: The cases were reversed and remanded with directions that they be transferred to the law division.

People v. Roberts

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant previously convicted of burglary appealed from an order of the Winnebago County Circuit Court (Illinois) denying his 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-4.1 petition for a new sentencing hearing. On appeal, he also sought relief from the judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was not present when he was convicted of burglary and sentenced as a prior felon, pursuant to former 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-3(c)(8). He originally sought relief from his sentence and the underlying conviction on grounds that he was unavailable, within the meaning of 725 Ill. Comp. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Boylan v. Matejka


No. 2-01-0787


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 96; 770 N.E.2d 1266; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 506; 264 Ill. Dec. 570



June 11, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 00--MR--919. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought an Illinois veteran grant exempting him from paying tuition at state-controlled colleges, universities, and community colleges. Defendant commission denied the application. The applicant sought judicial review of the commission's decision. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) upheld the commission's decision. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The applicant sought a veteran grant after he received a general discharge, under honorable conditions, from the United States Navy due to, among other things, his refusal to take an anthrax vaccine. On appeal from the denial of his application, the applicant argued that the trial court erroneously upheld the commission's determination that he was ineligible for an Illinois veteran grant because he was not honorably discharged. The appellate court agreed with the commission that 110 Ill. Comp. Stat. 947/40 (1998) did not permit the applicant to receive an Illinois veteran grant because his discharge was other than honorable. The appellate court noted that 32 C.F.R. § 724.109(a) (2002), distinguished honorable discharge from general discharges, and that the language of 110 Ill. Comp. Stat. 947/40 (1998) was clear in stating that an applicant must have received an honorable discharge in order to be eligible for the Illinois veteran grant. As for the applicant's argument that the court should have considered the reason underlying his discharge, the appellate court held that it was not the court's function to do so.


OUTCOME: The denial of the applicant's request for an Illinois veteran grant was upheld.

Mefford v. White

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 8, 2002.

DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Sangamon County (Illinois), entered a judgment affirming defendant secretary of state's denial of plaintiff applicant's request for a driver's license after the applicant refused to provide his social security number on his application, citing his religious beliefs. The applicant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The applicant's father helped the applicant obtain a social security number when the applicant was very young. When he was older, he applied to the secretary of state for a state driver's license. He supplied all personal information required by the applicable Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat.
