Admin Code tit. 92, § 1030.63, he requested relief from having to submit his social security number based on the religious beliefs he had developed. The secretary of state issued a final decision that denied his application after it was determined that neither the statute nor the rule allowed him to obtain a license without providing that number. The trial court affirmed. After it did so, the appellate court found neither the statute nor administrative rule violated his state or federal constitutional rights to free exercise of his religion. It found the statute and rule were neutral laws generally applicable to all driver's license applicants and only incidentally affected his particular religious practices.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Redwood v. Lierman


NO. 4-01-0612


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 1073; 772 N.E.2d 803; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 871; 265 Ill. Dec. 432



June 7, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 99LM243. Honorable Holly F. Clemons, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from a judgment of the Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) that dismissed their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 complaint against defendants, the village and local officials, for alleged Fourth and Fourteenth Amendment violations in towing a van from their driveway under a nuisance ordinance dealing with inoperable motor vehicles.


OVERVIEW: The village's ordinance, aimed at preventing the nuisance of inoperable motor vehicles stored indefinitely in plain sight on private property, provided for a system of notice and hearing before a vehicle could be towed pursuant to the ordinance. The property owners were repairing the brakes on a van used in their contracting business when they received a notice under the ordinance. They explained the situation, received an extension, and fixed the van before the deadline. Nonetheless, at the direction of certain officials, deputies entered their property and towed the van. When it was retrieved from the impoundment facility, the owners' tools were missing. The appellate court held that for purposes of federal civil rights liability, the owners did not state a claim against the village, since the ordinance as written was proper, or against the sheriff or the mayor, since they were not individually involved, but that the individual officials who decided to tow the van could be liable for Fourth Amendment violations, since there was a warrantless seizure from the curtilage of the home, although not for Fourteenth Amendment notice violations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal as to the action against the village and against certain officials in their official capacities, and as to all the Fourteenth Amendment claims, but reversed it as to the Fourth Amendment claims against those officials sued as individuals, and remanded the matter for further proceedings on those claims.

People v. Botruff


No. 3-01-0223


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 486; 771 N.E.2d 570; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 471; 264 Ill. Dec. 866


October 15, 2001, Assigned; November 8, 2001, Submitted  
June 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 16, 2002.
Appeal granted by People v. Botruff, 201 Ill. 2d 579, 786 N.E.2d 188, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1503, 271 Ill. Dec. 930 (2002)
Reversed by People v. Botruff, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 1019 (Ill., Sept. 23, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Warren County, Illinois. No. 99-MR-3. Honorable Ronald C. Tenold, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 9th Judicial Circuit Court, Warren County, Illinois, conducted a probable cause hearing concerning appellant inmate's commitment to the Department of Human Services under the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/1 et seq. The trial court denied the inmate's request for an independent evaluator, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate was statutorily prohibited, by 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/65(b)(1), from being present at the probable cause hearing conducted to determine if facts existed to warrant a hearing on the issue of whether he remained a sexually violent person. The appellate court held, while 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/55(a) provided the trial court "may" appoint a qualified expert to examine the inmate, at the time of his reexamination, that was subject to the rights conferred in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/25(e) to have such an expert appointed upon request. Under the Due Process Clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, the inmate had to be allowed to be heard at a meaningful time and in a meaningful manner. The probable cause hearing held under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/65(b)(1) was such a meaningful time, but disallowing the inmate's presence at that hearing, where he could only be present by counsel, was not a meaningful manner, for due process purposes, and the provision of § 65(b)(1) prohibiting the inmate's personal presence at the hearing was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

Prato v. Vallas


No. 1-01-0964


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


331 Ill. App. 3d 852; 771 N.E.2d 1053; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 451; 265 Ill. Dec. 94



May 31, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 23, 2002.
Appeal denied by Prato v. Vallas, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1438 (Ill., Oct. 2, 2002)
Motion denied by Prato v. Vallas, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 3693 (U.S., May 19, 2003)
Request denied by Prato v. Vallas, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 4577 (U.S., June 9, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE DOROTHY K. KINNAIRD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school principal appealed from that part of a judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) that dismissed her petition for administrative review of a decision of defendant school board and its superintendent, terminating her employment for cause. She argued that the decision was against the manifest weight of the evidence and that the statute under which the board acted, 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/34-85, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A school principal somehow accessed confidential test scores of children in surrounding schools, and invited them to apply to her school's magnet program. This caused friction and scandal. She took adverse employment action against teachers who cooperated with the investigation. Although her local school council continued to support her, her contract was terminated by the school board after a hearing. The appellate court reviewed the board's action, rather than the trial court's affirmance of the action, and upheld it. There was ample evidence in the record supporting the impropriety of the principal's conduct and her knowledge that the conduct was wrong; therefore, it fell within the exception in 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/34-85 that permitted the board to find her conduct irremediable, and therefore a firing offense, because she knew all along that it was wrong. Because the statutory procedure provided the principal with notice and an opportunity to explain herself (which she failed to do), it did not violate the due process guarantees of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

Lara v. Hyundai Motor Am.


No. 2-01-0250


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 53; 770 N.E.2d 721; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 446; 264 Ill. Dec. 416; 47 U.C.C. Rep. Serv. 2d (Callaghan) 1379



May 29, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 00--AR--202. Honorable Timothy R. Gill, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff consumer filed an action against defendant car manufacturer alleging breach of written limited warranty and breach of merchantability under the Magnuson-Moss Warranty-Federal Trade Commission Improvement Act, 15 U.S.C.S. § 2301 et seq. The Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) granted the car manufacturer partial summary judgment on the breach of warranty count. The consumer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The instant action arose after a vehicle purchased by the consumer failed to be properly repaired after being brought in for repairs on 14 occasions. On appeal, the consumer argued that the Act did not permit the car manufacturer to require the return of the vehicle as a condition to any remedy for a breach of the express warranty. She further argued that, although the warranty limited her potential remedies to the repair or replacement of defective parts, the limitation was ineffective because it was inconspicuous and the exclusive remedy failed of its essential purpose. Therefore, the consumer contended, incidental and consequential damages were available as a remedy. The appellate court concluded that the new vehicle limited warranty was not a full warranty under the Act because it did not permit the consumer to elect a replacement of the vehicle or a refund as a remedy for a warranty breach. Therefore, the car manufacturer could not demand the return of the vehicle. Finally, the appellate court noted that summary judgment was erroneously granted on the express warranty count because a factual question existed as to whether the consumer received the benefit of her bargain.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

People v. Ruppenthal


No. 1-01-1231


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


331 Ill. App. 3d 916; 771 N.E.2d 1002; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 410; 265 Ill. Dec. 43



May 24, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied July 2, 2002. Released for Publication July 23, 2002.
Rehearing denied by, Petition for certiorari filed at, 07/02/2002
Appeal denied by People v. Ruppenthal, 201 Ill. 2d 604, 786 N.E.2d 196, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1617 (2002)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by RUPPENTHAL, STEPHEN v. ILLINOIS, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5529 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Carol Kipperman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting him of indecent solicitation of a child in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-6. He argued that the statute was an unconstitutional limitation of his freedom of speech and that territorial jurisdiction was absent because the solicitation took place via computer, from California.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was located in California when, believing himself to be communicating with a 15-year-old girl in Illinois via the Internet, he solicited sex with her. He was actually corresponding with a middle-aged sheriff's deputy. Defendant was arrested when he arrived in Illinois with the announced intent of consummating the relationship, and was convicted of soliciting sex with a child. He attacked the constitutionality of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-6, but the appellate court upheld the statute as a reasonable limitation on defendant's freedom of expression, given the State's obligation to protect children. It noted, further, that defendant would never have been arrested if he had not acted on the plan he had proposed. An actual child did not have to be involved in order to commit the crime of solicitation, but someone had to be solicited. The fact that the target was in Illinois was sufficient to give Illinois courts territorial jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction.

Fedanzo v. City of Chicago


1-01-0582


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 413



May 24, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT. As Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing August 2, 2002. Opinion replaced: Fedanzo v. City of Chicago, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 754 (Ill. App. Ct. Aug. 2, 2002). Opinion withdrawn by order of the court: Fedanzo v. City of Chicago, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 661 (Ill. App. Ct. July 31, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John K. Madden, Judge Presidng.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee filed a petition for a writ of certiorari in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) seeking review of the decision made by defendants, the Personnel Board of the City of Chicago (Illinois) and the City of Chicago (Illinois) to terminate him from his employment. The circuit court denied the petition and the employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee, who worked for the city at an airport, was terminated from his employment after the city investigated a claim that he did not reside in the city. A hearing officer sustained that decision and the employee sought judicial review. The appellate court held that (1) the employee failed to meet his burden of showing that the city's residency requirement was unconstitutional as it applied to people who worked at the airport; (2) evidence which showed that the employee was not seen at a residence which his father owned in the city when investigators conducted surveillance at that residence but was seen on 26 out of 29 occasions at a house outside the city limits where his wife and children lived, that someone else occupied the residence in the city, and that the employee had spent money to improve the residence outside the city was sufficient to sustain the hearing officer's determination that the employee did not reside in the city; and (3) the hearing officer did not abuse his discretion by refusing the employee's motion to suppress evidence that was allegedly seized in violation of his rights.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Jones v. Indus. Comm'n


No. 3-01-0154WC


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT, INDUSTRIAL COMMISSION DIVISION


335 Ill. App. 3d 340; 780 N.E.2d 697; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 382; 269 Ill. Dec. 225



May 15, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County. No. 00-MR-189, Consolidated. Honorable Ronald Taber, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner police officers or firefighters appealed from a Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) affirmation of the decision of appellee industrial commission that it had no jurisdiction over their claims under 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/22-307 and dismissal of their causes of action. Respondent city cross-appealed from the portion of the trial court's order reversing the commission's order as to one petitioner.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found the commission did not err in finding that it had no jurisdiction. The version of 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/22-307 in effect at the time of the petitioners' injuries was unambiguous that an injured firefighter or police officer could not pursue any common law or statutory remedies against his municipal employer except for those provided by ordinance enacted pursuant to 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/22-306. Petitioners had misplaced reliance on the city's jurisdiction stipulation in the case of one petitioner, and it was of no benefit. Review of the amendment of 40 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/22-307 revealed nothing to indicate an express intent on the part of the legislature that previously barred claims be revived. The contested laws were not unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that, in the case of one petitioner, the city had made a knowing and binding election to proceed under the Workers' Compensation Act (Act), 820 Ill. Comp. Stat. 305/1 et seq. The city's actions could not confer subject matter jurisdiction where it was absent. The trial court erred in entering judgment on the one petitioner's behalf.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed as to all claimants except one petitioner and was reversed as to the one petitioner.

Hanna v. City of Chi.


No. 1-00-2181


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


331 Ill. App. 3d 295; 771 N.E.2d 13; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 369; 264 Ill. Dec. 609



May 14, 2002, Decided  
May 14, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 2, 2002.
Appeal denied by Hanna v. City of Chicago, 201 Ill. 2d 566, 786 N.E.2d 183, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 994, 271 Ill. Dec. 925 (2002)
Related proceeding at Hanna v. City of Chicago, 354 Ill. App. 3d 1156, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 6510 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)
Appeal after remand at Hanna v. City of Chicago, 382 Ill. App. 3d 672, 887 N.E.2d 856, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 383, 320 Ill. Dec. 712 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 CH 8311. Honorable Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, reversed, in part, and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sued appellee city in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for a declaratory judgment and injunctive and other relief regarding the downzoning of the owner's property. The trial court granted the city's motion to dismiss, and the owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner's property was downzoned by its inclusion in a special district. The appellate court held the applicable level of scrutiny in his facial challenge to the zoning ordinance was whether the legislation bore a substantial relationship to the public health, safety or welfare or was arbitrary, irrational and capricious. The owner's allegations that (1) the district was a hodgepodge of zoning uses surrounded by commercial uses; (2) his property values were substantially diminished; (3) the rezoning did not benefit the general health, safety or morals; (4) an extreme hardship was imposed on him due to an uncompensated taking of his property; and (5) the subject property had been zoned "as is" for over 40 years, adequately pled a constitutional violation. The owner also adequately alleged improper spot zoning. The city's alleged failure to follow the special district amendment could not be reviewed. On remand, the owner had to give notice to all property owners within 250 feet of the district. He did not have to exhaust local remedies as he sought to invalidate the entire special district. He sufficiently alleged irreparable injury.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment dismissing the owner's claim that the city did not comply with the special district amendment was affirmed. Otherwise, the trial court's judgment was reversed, and the matter was remanded.

People v. Kelley


No. 1-00-0764


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


331 Ill. App. 3d 253; 770 N.E.2d 1130; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 367; 264 Ill. Dec. 434



May 13, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 2, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Kelley, 203 Ill. 2d 558, 788 N.E.2d 732, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 497, 273 Ill. Dec. 141 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Kelley v. McCann, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 43083 (N.D. Ill., June 14, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Leo E. Holt, Judge Presiding.

DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), denied defendant's motion for postconviction relief in a case where he was convicted following a bench trial of first-degree murder, attempted first-degree murder, and armed violence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A woman was sitting in her car with her three-year-old son, her father, and her brother. She saw defendant "throw gang signs" at her. The woman started to drive away. Defendant fired a gun. The son was shot in the back of the head and soon died. The father was shot twice in the arm and had to be hospitalized for three days. Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder for the killing and attempted first-degree murder for the wounding. The trial court imposed an extended-term sentence for the first-degree murder and a consecutive sentence for the attempted first-degree murder. Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. After his postconviction relief petition was denied, the appellate court found the extended-term and consecutive sentences were properly imposed. It found any violation of Apprendi was harmless because no dispute existed but that the murder victim was three years old and the jury would have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt even had it been asked to determine the victim's age. It also found the attempted first-degree murder allowed for consecutive sentencing pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a) (1994).


OUTCOME: The judgments imposing extended-term and consecutive sentences were affirmed. Also, the State's request for costs in defending the appeal was granted.

People v. Terry


NO. 4-00-0435


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


329 Ill. App. 3d 1104; 769 N.E.2d 559; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 375; 264 Ill. Dec. 57



May 13, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 99CF2038. Honorable John G. Townsend, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with unlawful possession of a stolen vehicle in violation of § 4-103(a)(1) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, codified at 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-103(a)(1), (b) (1998). The Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) found defendant guilty and sentenced him to 24 months' probation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued his conviction must be reversed because 1998 Ill. Laws 1307, violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d). Defendant argued that 1998 Ill. Laws 1307, included unrelated subjects such as the insanity defense and drug asset forfeiture proceedings. The appellate court held that the purported subject of 1998 Ill. Laws 1307, on involving the criminal law, was a legitimate subject for single subject purposes. Defendant also argued the amendments to the Illinois Drug Asset Forfeiture Procedure Act were not related to criminal law, and thus, the single subject clause was thereby violated. The appellate court disagreed, finding that defendant failed to meet his burden of demonstrating any of the provisions of 1998 Ill. Laws 1307, bear no natural and logical connection to the single subject relating to the criminal justice system.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Taher


No. 1-01-0048


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 1007; 769 N.E.2d 1021; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 326; 264 Ill. Dec. 184



May 3, 2002, Decided  
May 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 18, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 00 MC5 006008. The Honorable Daniel Welter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction of domestic battery in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-3.2(a)(2).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-3.2(a)(2) provided a person of ordinary intelligence with a reasonable opportunity to distinguish between lawful and unlawful conduct so that he or she could act accordingly. 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-3.2(a)(2) provided defendant with sufficient notice that his conduct was prohibited. 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-3.2(a)(2) was constitutional as applied to defendant. The conduct prohibited by 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-3.2(a)(2) was not protected by the First Amendment. The overbreadth doctrine only applied when First Amendment expressive rights were implicated. Since the statute at bar did not infringe on a constitutionally protected right, it was not unconstitutionally broad. After reviewing defendant's wife's testimony, the trial court could have concluded that defendant was guilty of domestic battery. The issue of whether the trial court erred when it entered and continued the order of protection was moot, as defendant was granted supervised visitation. There was no error that denied defendant a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

People v. Jones


Nos. 2-00-1214 & 2-01-0177 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


329 Ill. App. 3d 470; 769 N.E.2d 540; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 332; 264 Ill. Dec. 38



May 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 31, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 98--CF--399 98--CF--1701. Honorable Ann Brackley Jorgensen Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal from judgments of the Du Page County Circuit Court (Illinois), defendant appealed from her natural life sentence imposed pursuant to her guilty plea to first-degree murder and from denial of her motion to dismiss, on double jeopardy grounds, her prosecution for an earlier attempted murder of the same victim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant faced charges of attempted first-degree murder of her husband and first-degree murder of him, which occurred a few months after the attempt. In a plea bargain to avoid the death penalty she pled guilty to first-degree murder, but specifically did not plead to the facts underlying the attempt charge. The sentencing court found that the murder was aggravated by its heinousness and brutality, and sentenced defendant to natural life in prison pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(b). The appellate court held that the sentence did not violate the rule of Apprendi because by her agreement to a natural life sentence at the plea colloquy, a natural life term became the statutory maximum sentence. Defendant also argued her continuing prosecution for attempted murder violated her double jeopardy guarantees, but the appellate court held that jeopardy had never attached on that charge, because counsel explicitly excluded the factual basis for that charge from defendant's guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both judgments.

Thompson v. Vill. of Newark


No. 2-01-0542


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


329 Ill. App. 3d 536; 768 N.E.2d 856; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 333; 263 Ill. Dec. 775



May 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 31, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kendall County. No. 00--MR--12. Honorable James R. Edwards, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners sued defendant village, seeking a declaratory judgment that a village ordinance assessing developmental impact fees for school construction was not authorized by statute and was unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Kendall County, Illinois, granted summary judgment for the village. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance authorized the village to impose school impact fees on new development within the village. Before they could receive a permit to build a home on their property, the owners were obliged to pay almost $ 4,000 in impact fees. Their suit alleged that the ordinance was authorized by neither the Illinois Constitution nor state statute, that it violated the equal protection clauses of the federal and state constitutions, and that was an uncompensated "taking" in violation of the federal and state constitutions. The appellate court held that authorization, if any, for the ordinance was provided by 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-12-5 (2000). Under that statute, a municipality could implement a comprehensive plan for the municipality's future development. But that statute was concerned with such traditional planning concepts as the location, width, course, and surfacing of public streets and the size of lots to be used for residential purposes. It could not be read to also authorize a municipality to collect revenue to undertake massive capital improvements. As the ordinance was not authorized by state statute, the appellate court did not reach the constitutional arguments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

People v. Tenney


No. 2-00-0199


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


329 Ill. App. 3d 430; 769 N.E.2d 528; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 315; 264 Ill. Dec. 26


June 25, 2001, Submitted; May 24, 2001, Assigned  
April 29, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2002.
Rehearing denied by, 05/23/2002
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Tenney, 799 N.E.2d 678, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2301, 278 Ill. Dec. 813 (Ill., 2003)
On reconsideration by People v. Tenney, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 367 (Ill. App. Ct., Apr. 5, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 95-CF-902. Honorable Donald C. Hudson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction affirmed; sentence vacated and and cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Kane County, Illinois, found defendant guilty of first-degree murder; he was sentenced to life imprisonment. He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's accomplice testified that while he and defendant were burglarizing a home he heard a shot and saw the bleeding victim, and that defendant told him his gun had jammed and ordered him to shoot the victim again, which he did. He admitted to being addicted to several drugs, and to the leniency shown him by the State for his testimony. The appellate court held that as the testimony was in part corroborated by other evidence, including one of the murder weapons found in defendant's possession, the evidence was sufficient to convict. The trial court did not err in refusing to allow defendant to question the venire about their experiences with friends or family suffering from substance abuse, as it did not prohibit him from questioning them about their views regarding alcohol and drugs. However, the life sentence was invalid under Apprendi. Since the maximum statutory penalty for first-degree murder was 60 years' imprisonment, and the State conceded that there was insufficient evidence to find defendant eligible for the death penalty, in order to obtain a life sentence the State was obliged to prove to the jury beyond a reasonable doubt the factors of brutality and heinousness.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed, but the cause was remanded for a new sentencing hearing.

People v. Hancock


NO. 4-01-0678


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


329 Ill. App. 3d 367; 771 N.E.2d 459; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 314; 264 Ill. Dec. 755



April 23, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 28, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Hancock, 201 Ill. 2d 589, 786 N.E.2d 191, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1176, 271 Ill. Dec. 933 (2002)
Appeal denied by People v. Hancock, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2315 (Ill., Dec. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 00CF1597. Honorable John R. DeLaMar, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his commitment by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois) after he was found to be a sexually dangerous person pursuant to Illinois' Sexually Dangerous Persons Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 205/0.01 through 12 (2000). Defendant asserted several errors including constitutionality of the Act and juror instructions.


OVERVIEW: Two psychiatrists diagnosed defendant as suffering from a number of mental disorders, including pedophilia and voyeurism with a history of exhibitionism. Both agreed that defendant was a sexually dangerous person with a propensity for committing acts of sexual assault against children. Two police officers stated defendant admitted committing the underlying crimes, as well as confessing a number of other sex-related offenses over a period of several years. The appellate court held the nature of defendant's psychiatric diagnosis, and the severity of the mental abnormality itself, was sufficient to distinguish defendant from the dangerous but typical recidivist convicted in an ordinary criminal case. There was no issue as to whether defendant committed as least one act of or attempt at sexual assault or sexual molestation. Defendant's remaining contentions were without merit. In particular, his proposed instruction was a misstatement of the law. He was allowed to cross-examine the testifying psychiatrist concerning whether he would commit sex-related acts in the future. The prior acts showed his propensity to commit criminal acts in pursuit of his sexual urges.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Jamesson


No. 2-00-0480


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


329 Ill. App. 3d 446; 768 N.E.2d 817; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 324; 263 Ill. Dec. 736


March 8, 2001, Submitted; August 1, 2001, Assigned  
April 23, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99-CM-5198. Honorable Mark W. Dwyer, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Du Page County Circuit Court convicting him, after a trial to the bench, of unlawful contact with a gang member in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/25-1.1. He argued on appeal that the statute was unconstitutional and that the evidence was insufficient to convict him.


OVERVIEW: When defendant pled guilty to a drug offense, a condition of his supervision was that he have no contact with several named persons or any other known gang members. Two days later a police gang specialist saw him with one of the named persons and another gang member, so he was prosecuted for knowingly having contact with gang members while under a sentencing order forbidding it, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/25-1.1. Defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statute, but the appeals court agreed that it was neither overbroad, because it limited defendant's freedom of association only to the extent of illegal association, nor vague, because it was clear exactly what conduct was prohibited, and the statute contained a scienter element. Defendant also challenged the sufficiency of the evidence that the association to which the prohibited persons belonged was a street gang, but the court held that the trial court, as trier of fact, reasonably relied on the expert evidence of the police gang specialist.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Armstrong


No. 2-99-0352


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


329 Ill. App. 3d 150; 769 N.E.2d 77; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 302; 263 Ill. Dec. 875



April 18, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 24, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Carroll County. No. 96--CF--25. Honorable Richard E. DeMoss, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was vacated, in part, reversed, in part, and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court convicted defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault and other crimes. On direct appeal, the appellate court affirmed. Defendant filed a petition pursuant to the Post-Conviction Hearing Act. The trial court dismissed the petition, and defendant appealed. The appellate court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and vacated in part. The Illinois Supreme Court directed the appellate court to vacate and reconsider the case.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the dismissal was erroneous because he stated valid claims that: (1) he was denied the effective assistance of trial counsel; and (2) his conviction of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child was void because the statute creating the offense was unconstitutional. The State confessed error on the second issue. Defendant asked the appellate court to reverse the summary dismissal of his petition and remand the cause so that the trial court may appoint counsel for defendant and conduct further proceedings on the petition as a whole, including his claim that his trial counsel was ineffective. The appellate court held that partial summary dismissals were not permitted under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act. The Act spoke solely in terms of the petition itself being frivolous or patently without merit, and the Act mandated that if the petition was not dismissed, then the trial court was required to order the petition docketed. The appellate court held this doctrine required the entire petition to be advanced to the second stage of the postconviction process.


OUTCOME: The conviction of predatory criminal sexual assault was vacated, and the denial of postconviction relief was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

Arangold Corp. v. Zehnder


No. 1-01-1371


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 781; 768 N.E.2d 391; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 266; 263 Ill. Dec. 631



April 12, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 2002.
Affirmed by Arangold Corp. v. Zehnder, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 460 (Ill., Mar. 20, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 L 51215 (formerly 95 L 50989). Honorable John A. Ward, Judge Presiding.
Arangold Corp. v. Zehnder, 187 Ill. 2d 341, 718 N.E.2d 191, 1999 Ill. LEXIS 955 (1999)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendants-appellees' motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff cigar company filed a four-count complaint challenging the validity of the Tobacco Products Act of 1995, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 143/10-1 et seq. Defendants, the state department of revenue and its director and the state treasurer, filed a motion for summary judgment. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the motion and upheld the constitutionality of the Act. The company appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The Act imposed a tax on tobacco products other than cigarettes, such as cigars, and allocated the revenues to the Illinois Long-Term Care Provider Fund, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 143/10-10. The appellate court held the Act did not violate the due process clauses of the Illinois and federal Constitutions. The appellate court found the Act met the rational basis test. The State had a legitimate interest in preserving the health of its citizens. The Act's taxation of tobacco products was rationally related to those interests, as the Illinois General Assembly could have believed that cigars and other tobacco products caused any number of health problems and that those problems required care in long-term health care facilities. The appellate court held it was rational to formulate a tax requiring people who imposed costs on society to pay some of those costs. The appellate court held the Act did not violate Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2. The fact the tax was imposed specifically to fund nursing home care for the poor did not violate uniformity requirements, as the general assembly could fairly have found a connection between tobacco products and long-term care for the poor.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Nationwide Gen. Ins. Co. v. Shapo


NO. 4-01-0524


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 1028; 767 N.E.2d 936; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 263; 263 Ill. Dec. 210



April 10, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. Nos. 00MR5, 00MR6, 00MR7, 00MR8, 00MR9, 00MR10, 00MR11, 00MR12, 00MR129, 00MR166, 00MR506, 00MR566, 00MR584, 00MR592, 00MR593, 00MR594, 00MR597, 00MR598, 00MR690, 00MR826, 00MR827, 00MR852, 01MR23, 01MR82, 01MR180, 01MR182, 01MR202, 01MR203, 01MR204. Honorable Thomas R. Appleton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Sangamon County (Illinois), denied plaintiff foreign companies' motion to reconsider and entered judgment dismissing their consolidated complaints for administrative review that they filed after defendants, state insurance agency, director, and counsel, notified the foreign companies that the director had no statutory authority to allow refunds of privilege taxes the foreign companies had paid. The foreign companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: The foreign companies were incorporated under the laws of states other than Illinois. As foreign companies, they were subject to an annual tax of two percent of net taxable premium income, imposed by 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/409 (1996), for the privilege of doing business in Illinois. However, the state supreme court found that statute was unconstitutional. The foreign companies relied on that holding and the tax refund statute of 215 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/412(1) (1996) to request refunds of privilege taxes paid over the refund period allowed in § 5/412(1), six years. The state insurance agency, director, and counsel notified them that the director had no statutory authority to allow the refunds. After the trial court denied administrative review, the appellate court found the foreign companies relied on § 5/412(1)'s provision that a refund was permitted where the director erroneously interpreted a statute to collect a tax. However, it found the fact that a statute was found unconstitutional did not mean it had been erroneously interpreted. It also found the foreign companies' due process rights were not violated by an unconstitutional "bait and switch."


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Norris


No. 3-01-0521


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 994; 767 N.E.2d 904; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 250; 263 Ill. Dec. 178



April 9, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 14, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 9th Judicial Circuit, Fulton County, Illinois. No. 98--CF--122. Honorable Stephen R. Bordner, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The 9th Judicial Circuit Court, Fulton County (Illinois), accepted the defendant's fully-negotiated agreement with the State to plead guilty, and found defendant guilty of one count of aggravated criminal sexual abuse and one count of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. It then sentenced him and denied his subsequent post-trial motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated criminal sexual abuse and two counts of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. Pursuant to a fully-negotiated agreement, defendant pled guilty to aggravated criminal sexual abuse and one count of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child. The other predatory criminal sexual assault count was dismissed. Prior to accepting defendant's guilty pleas, the trial court informed defendant of the nature of the charges against him and the possible penalties provided by law. It did not admonish him that he was subject, when his sentences expired, to civil commitment proceedings under the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 205/0.01 et seq. (1998), and the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/1 et seq. (1998). After defendant's pleas were accepted and he was sentenced in part under an amended truth-in-sentencing law, the appellate court found civil commitment under the named acts was a collateral consequence of defendant's guilty pleas about which the trial court was not required to admonish the defendant. It also found the amended truth-in-sentencing law was not constitutionally defective.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Douglas


No. 3--01--0226


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 978; 768 N.E.2d 766; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 249; 263 Ill. Dec. 685



April 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 14, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 98--CF--1047. Honrable Michael E. Brandt, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the 10th Judicial Circuit Court, Peoria County, Illinois, to unlawful possession with intent to deliver less than one gram of cocaine, and was sentenced to eight years' imprisonment, based on a prior conviction. His postconviction petition was summarily dismissed, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted the enhancement of his sentence had to be submitted to a trier of fact and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held the application of these requirements to any fact increasing defendant's penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum did not apply to his extended term sentence based on his prior conviction, under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3.22(b)(1) (2000). The trial court was thus authorized to summarily dismiss his petition without a hearing, and the statute which allowed the trial court to do this, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-2.1(a)(2) (2000), enacted through Ill. Pub. Act 83-942 (Nov. 23, 1983), did not violate the single subject clause of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d), because all the sections of that act were naturally and logically connected to criminal justice.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1662 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Poole v. Clausen (in Re Estate of Poole)


No. 3-00-0724


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 964; 767 N.E.2d 855; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 242; 263 Ill. Dec. 129



April 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 14, 2002.
Appeal granted by Poole v. Clausen (In re Estate of Poole), 201 Ill. 2d 569, 786 N.E.2d 184, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1142 (2002)
Affirmed by Poole v. Clausen (In re Estate of Poole), 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1492 (Ill., Oct. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 10th Judicial Circuit, Putnam County, Illinois. No. 98-P-17. Honorable Stuart Borden Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In response to appellee grandmother's petition for letters of administration, the circuit court appointed her administrator and directed the letters be issued. The grandmother petitioned for an order allowing her to execute settlement documents and distribute to heirs at law. The Circuit Court for the 10th Judicial Circuit, Putnam County, Illinois, denied appellant father's petition to revoke the letters. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The case arose after the death of the father's unborn illegitimate child. On appeal, the father argued the trial court erred in determining that he had no interest, standing, or priority to request removal of the grandmother as administrator of the child's estate. The appellate court concluded that under 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3 (1998), the father, a biological parent, had preference over the grandmother for letters of administration. The grandmother argued, however, that the father was not an eligible parent. The appellate court held that the father was an eligible parent after determining that he resided with the mother before and throughout the pregnancy, provided financial and emotion support to the mother, and, through her, to the unborn child, and held himself out as the father. The court also noted that the right to bring the wrongful death action was not the grandmother's right, but that the action could have been brought by the child's father. Thus, the court held that a determination had to be made as to whether the father was the biological father of the child, with such a right.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

 

1663 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


In re O.R.


No. 2-01-1084


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 955; 767 N.E.2d 872; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 244; 263 Ill. Dec. 146



April 3, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 97-JA-133. Honorable Thomas E. Mueller, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), respondent mother challenged a judgment finding her to be an unfit parent and terminating her parental rights to her son.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/1(D)(t) was narrowly tailored to attain the legislative goal of protecting children from abuse by identifying as unfit those mothers who harmed their children by using drugs during pregnancy and who previously gave birth to a child who was adjudicated neglected due to that child being born with a controlled substance in his or her system. The mother had not carried her burden of clearly establishing that the statute violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, the Illinois Equal Protection Clause. 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 50/1(D)(t) provided a narrowly tailored means of identifying parents who pose a danger to their children's health and safety. The statute was narrowly tailored to meet the compelling state interest of protecting a child from abuse and the legislature used the least restrictive means consistent with the attainment of its goal. Mother had not carried her burden of clearly establishing a due process violation under Ill. Const. art. I, § 2.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1664 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


El-Amin v. Dempsey


No. 1-01-2173


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 800; 768 N.E.2d 344; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 208; 263 Ill. Dec. 584



March 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 L 734. Honorable Michael J. Hogan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's certified questions were answered in the affirmative.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From the Circuit Court of Cook County, plaintiff mother filed this medical malpractice action seeking recovery of damages for the death of her infant son. The court granted defendant doctor's motion to certify a question of law for interlocutory appeal regarding the discoverability of mother's prenatal care records.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that a medical malpractice defendant was entitled to obtain medical records pertaining to the prenatal care rendered to decedent's mother during the term of her pregnancy with decedent, despite the mother's invocation of the physician-patient privilege and a right to privacy, where: (1) the mother was both the plaintiff who filed the wrongful death cause of action on behalf of the decedent's estate and a beneficiary to the decedent's estate; and (2) where the decedent's death was alleged to have resulted 16 days after the decedent's birth, as a result of doctor's allegedly negligent care rendered in the first three days of the decedent's life. Filing a medical malpractice lawsuit on behalf of a child waived the physician-patient privilege for records when the child was in utero. A mother's medical records for the period when the infant plaintiff was in utero were discoverable. Here, once mother's child's medical condition was placed at issue in the lawsuit, the physician-patient privilege was waived, as to his prenatal medical records, or, in other words, to the only relevant existing medical records, those pertaining to mother.


OUTCOME: The trial court's certified question was answered in the affirmative.

 

1665 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Henderson


No. 1-99-2555


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 810; 768 N.E.2d 222; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 214; 263 Ill. Dec. 462



March 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Henderson, 788 N.E.2d 731, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 496 (Ill., 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Henderson v. Ill., 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6424 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Joseph M. Macellaio, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of two counts of reckless homicide and one count of driving on a revoked license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's speeding car hit the back of another car. That car then blew up, killing the driver. A police officer spoke with defendant and noticed signs he was under the influence of alcohol. A sample of his blood showed his blood-alcohol concentration exceeded .10 percent. The trial court gave a jury instruction stating that if the jury found defendant's blood alcohol level was .10 percent or more, it could presume, but was not required to presume, that defendant was under the influence of alcohol. After defendant was convicted of reckless homicide for operating a vehicle with a blood-alcohol level of .10 percent or more and operating a vehicle while impaired, the appellate court found the statute under which the jury instruction was given, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3(c) (1996), was not unconstitutional. It found the statute did not contain an impermissible mandatory presumption, but allowed the jury to presume a defendant with a .10 percent or more blood alcohol level was under the influence. It also found photographic evidence was admissible to show the cause of death, but further found that one of the two convictions had to be vacated since only one death occurred.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for reckless homicide based on defendant operating a motor vehicle in a reckless manner was vacated, but the judgment of conviction for reckless homicide based on an excessive blood alcohol concentration as defined by statutory law was affirmed. The remainder of the trial court's judgment and the resulting sentence was affirmed.

People v. Marsh


No. 1-00-1646


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 639; 768 N.E.2d 108; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 228; 263 Ill. Dec. 348



March 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael B. Bolan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed but defendant-appellant's sentence was modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) sentencing him after a jury convicted him of failure to report an address change in violation of the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act. He challenged the statutory penalties on constitutional grounds and his own sentence as an abuse of discretion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's long-past sex offense conviction made him subject to the reporting requirements of the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/6, when he was arrested for something else. The law imposed a two-year reporting requirement on him, but he forgot to report an address change when he moved in temporarily with a neighbor. The appeals court held that the penalty provisions of the statute, codified at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/10, did not violate the due process guarantee of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, the guarantee against double jeopardy, or the proportionate sentences guarantee of Ill. Const. art. I, § 11, because the penalties related closely to the statutory purpose. The four-year enhanced-term sentence imposed on defendant was an abuse of discretion, however, because it was manifestly unjust in the circumstances of his offense, and he should also have been required to pay a mandatory $ 500 fine.


OUTCOME: The court modified the penalty to shorten defendant's sentence and impose a mandatory fine, and affirmed the remainder of the judgment.

People v. Likar


No. 1-01-0453


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 654; 768 N.E.2d 150; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 230; 263 Ill. Dec. 390



March 29, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Daniel J. Kelley, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and order of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) finding him guilty after a bench trial of criminal trespass in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/21-3 and sentencing him to a year of supervision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and his neighbor had a tense relationship before he wrote to an Illinois state licensing agency to complain that the neighbor's wife was conducting an illegal day care center on their premises. The neighbor claimed to have warned defendant to stay off the property. Defendant received a response to his letter to the licensing agency, and, while standing in the neighbor's driveway, sought to show it to the neighbor, who refused to speak to him. When the empty envelope fell or blew onto the neighbor's lawn and defendant sought to retrieve it, the neighbor initiated a criminal trespass complaint. The appeals court held that the various subsections of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/21-3 simply explained various ways criminal trespass could occur, so no one subsection had to be identified in the indictment. The evidence did not support defendant's 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/21-3(f) defense of entry for emergency purposes, because an empty envelope was not valuable property and defendant had other ways of saving it. Furthermore, defendant was already wrongfully on the property, in the driveway.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and order.

People v. Mena


No. 1-98-1326


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 579; 768 N.E.2d 160; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 231; 263 Ill. Dec. 400



March 29, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 22, 2002. Vacated, Appeal denied: People v. Mena, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 28 (Ill. Feb. 5, 2003).
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Mena, 329 Ill. App. 3d 12, 768 N.E.2d 177, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 211 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Mena, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 28 (Ill., Feb. 5, 2003)
Different results reached on reconsideration by, Remanded by People v. Mena, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 312 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Ralph Reyna, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed but defendant-appellant's sentence was modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of first degree murder. The trial court imposed an extended-term sentence. Defendant appealed the conviction and the sentence imposed. The appeal was initially dismissed for want of prosecution. Defendant moved for post-conviction relief, which was denied. The appellate court vacated the dismissal of the direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held the trial court did not err in declining to give a jury instruction on second degree murder. Defendant had the burden of proving there was at least some evidence of serious provocation. The provocation had to be proportionate to the manner in which the accused retaliated. There was evidence that the victim drove his car across the center line to ram the front of defendant's car. Defendant said that in response he grabbed a jack and ran to the victim's car, where he found the victim lying unresponsive. He dragged the victim from the car and struck his head with such force that he fractured the base of the victim's skull. The appellate court held the response was disproportionate. However, the appellate court held the trial court erred in sentencing defendant. The jury's verdict, without any additional finding of fact, authorized the trial court to sentence defendant to a term of between 20 and 60 years in prison. The appellate court held the sentence imposed deprived defendant of the right to a jury determination of a fact crucial for setting the range of appropriate sentences the trial court had the authority to impose.


OUTCOME: The appellate court modified the sentence to a term of 60 years, and the judgment was affirmed as modified.

People v. Brunt


No. 1-00-2744


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 202



March 27, 2002, Decided  
August 14, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [*1] Rehearing Denied August 6, 2002. Released for Publication August 12, 2002.
Modified and rehearing denied by People v. Brunt, 332 Ill. App. 3d 974, 775 N.E.2d 11, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 712, 266 Ill. Dec. 449 (Ill. App. Ct., 2002)
Appeal denied by People v. Brunt, 202 Ill. 2d 620, 787 N.E.2d 160, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1997, 272 Ill. Dec. 345 (2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Dennis Porter, Judge Presiding.
People v. Brunt, 302 Ill. App. 3d 1089, 746 N.E.2d 908, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 1642, 254 Ill. Dec. 151 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) dismissing without a hearing his petition for post-conviction relief from his convictions and sentences for murder, attempted murder, and armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: A single incident gave rise to defendant's convictions of felony murder, armed robbery on which the felony murder conviction was predicated, and attempted murder. Nearly a year after his conviction, defendant petitioned for post-conviction relief. The appeals court held that under the plain language of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122(c), defendant's petition had to be filed within six months of the deadline for filing a petition for leave to appeal to the state's high court. Since he did not file within that time, his petition was properly dismissed without a hearing. The appeals court nonetheless considered the issues raised by defendant, holding that imposition of consecutive sentences upon him did not violate the rule of Apprendi, that certain provisions in the post-conviction relief statute were not unconstitutional, and that defendant's conviction and sentence for armed robbery should be vacated because they were encompassed in the felony murder conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of defendant's post-conviction relief petition, but vacated his conviction and sentence for armed robbery.

Poullette v. Silverstein


No. 1-01-0263


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 791; 767 N.E.2d 477; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 189; 263 Ill. Dec. 26



March 21, 2002, Decided  
March 21, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected April 9, 2002. Released for Publication May 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No.99 L 9199. Honorable David R. Donnersberger, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff beneficiary brought an action against defendant attorney for legal practice in the preparation of a will and trust for the beneficiary's mother. The attorney filed a motion to dismiss the action as untimely under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-214.3(d) (1994). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the motion. The beneficiary appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the beneficiary contended that the circuit court misinterpreted 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-241.3(d), and that the statute was unconstitutional as applied by the court. The appellate court held that the circuit court properly applied the statute. The appellate court noted that while the effect on the beneficiary was to shorten the period of time in which she had to filed her claim, it could neither restrict nor enlarge the meaning of the unambiguous statute. In addition, the court noted that the fact that a repose provision barred the action before it was discovered was an accidental rather than a necessary consequence. As to the constitutionality issued, the appellate court found that any distinction drawn by the statute was rationally related to a legitimate governmental purpose, and therefore, the statute was not unconstitutional. The court concluded that the statute reflected, inter alia, a policy of law intended to balance several different interests, provided a claimant with a reasonable time after the decedent's death to pursue a cause of action, and balanced the defendant's right to be free of stale claims.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1671 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Austin


No. 1-99-3224


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 798; 767 N.E.2d 433; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 168; 262 Ill. Dec. 973



March 15, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 27, 2002. Released for Publication May 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, vacated in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) that convicted him after trial to the bench of three counts each of attempted murder, armed violence, and aggravated battery and sentenced him to consecutive terms of imprisonment on the first two groups of offenses.


OVERVIEW: Three eyewitnesses identified defendant as the person who shot and wounded several people in the course of a gang fight. Although their identification evidence was inconsistent in some respects, the appeals court upheld the trial court's credibility determination, including its finding that the witnesses' delay in coming forward was attributable to fear of reprisals. Since the trial was to the court, references to defendant's gang moniker were not prejudicial. Defendant's armed violence convictions, and the sentences imposed thereon, had to be vacated, because those offenses were too closely related to attempted first-degree murder, but the appeals court upheld (although it held that they could not be consecutive to defendant's sentence on an unrelated conviction) the imposition of consecutive sentences for attempted murder because the trial court's determination that a victim's bodily injuries were severe within the meaning of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a) was entitled to deference.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the armed violence convictions but affirmed the others; it also ordered resentencing to avoid stacking of sentences with a prior sentence, but upheld the imposition of consecutive sentences as to the attempted murder convictions.

People v. Ullrich


No. 1-00-1855


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 811; 767 N.E.2d 411; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 169; 262 Ill. Dec. 951



March 15, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Honorable Peter A. Flynn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was served with a notice stating that his driver's license was suspended for refusing to submit to chemical testing, following his arrest for driving under the influence of alcohol, along with other charges. He filed a petition to rescind the summary suspension. Following a hearing, the petition was denied, by order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which also denied his motion for reconsideration. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: At his suspension hearing, defendant and his girlfriend testified defendant had not been driving when he was arrested for drunk driving. The police officers did not testify, but an officer's reports were received into evidence, over defendant's objections. Based upon the reports, the suspension was upheld by the trial court. The appellate court found that defendant presented a prima facie case for rescission of the suspension. Although the admission of the police officer's reports raised constitutional concerns, the fact that defendant could subpoena the officers generally provided an adequate opportunity for cross-examination, such that the statute allowing the officer's report to be received into evidence, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-118.1 (2000), was constitutional. However, in the instant case there was no showing that the motorist was informed of his right to subpoena the officers or the consequences of failing to exercise his right. There was no showing of a knowing and intelligent waiver of the right to subpoena the officers. As such, the trial court erred in denying the petition to rescind the summary suspension based on the officer's official reports.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1673 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Reece v. Bd. of Educ.


No. 1-00-4040


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 773; 767 N.E.2d 395; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 167; 262 Ill. Dec. 935



March 14, 2002, Decided  
March 14, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 9, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00-CH-5481. Honorable Robert V. Boharic, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendants-appellees' motion for summary judgment and deinal of plaintiffs-appellants' motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens sued defendants, board and others, alleging that 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-3.25g was unconstitutional and sought to enjoin the disbursement of public funds to the board until it complied with the statutory requirement of daily physical education. All parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizens argued that (1) the physical education curriculum was protected from waiver by 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/34-8.14(3) (1996)); (2) 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-3.25g (1996) was unconstitutional because it modified existing law without following procedural constitutional formalities; (3) 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-3.25g (1996) constituted an unconstitutional legislative veto; and (4) 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-3.25g (1996) was an impermissible delegation of legislative authority to school boards. The appellate court held (1) the physical education curriculum was not protected by 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/34-8.14(3) (1996) because it was not specifically excluded, (2) 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-3.25g (1996) was not unconstitutional because it was modified in accordance with all procedural requirements for passage of a bill, (3) it had no jurisdiction to address the veto argument, and (4) there was no impermissible delegation of legislative authority since the legislature did not delegate its general legislative powers to school districts, and the school districts could only petition for a waiver. Thus, the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendants was not in error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1674 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Palmer


No. 2-00-0641


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 348; 766 N.E.2d 296; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 164; 262 Ill. Dec. 676



March 12, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 00-CF-114. Honorable Barbara C. Gilleran-Johnson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, vacated, in part, and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the enhanced-term sentencing part of a judgment of the Lake County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting her on guilty plea of armed violence premised on aggravated battery, arguing that the sentence violated the rule of Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted having stabbed an elderly drinking companion more than 50 times, and, pursuant to a plea agreement, pled guilty to armed violence. At plea entry, the trial court mentioned the possibility of an increased sentence pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-2 based on any past record defendant might have, but neither the trial court nor defendant mentioned the possibility of sentencing enhancement based on the heinousness of the offense or the victim's age. The appeals court held that the trial court's action in thereafter imposing an enhanced sentence based on those factors violated the constitutional rule of Apprendi, which required that other than the fact of a prior conviction, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum had to be submitted to a jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant never waived her right to have those issues submitted to a jury, so they could not be used for sentence enhancement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated the sentence and remanded for resentencing within normal sentencing ranges.

People v. Coleman


1-99-2714


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 688; 767 N.E.2d 388; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 159; 262 Ill. Dec. 928



March 11, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication May 9, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Coleman, 199 Ill. 2d 562, 775 N.E.2d 4, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 738, 266 Ill. Dec. 442 (2002)
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Coleman, 206 Ill. 2d 627, 799 N.E.2d 677, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 2298, 278 Ill. Dec. 812 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 9541. The Honorable Lawrence P. Fox, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's conviction was affirmed, his sentence was vactated, and cause was remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of two counts of first degree murder. The trial court, after determining that defendant's crime was exceptionally brutal and heinous in nature, sentenced defendant to a term of natural life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of killing his estranged wife. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in admitting evidence that his wife intended to divorce him and leave the state. The appellate court held that other circumstantial evidence was sufficient to establish a basis to infer that defendant was aware of her plan, and made the evidence of the wife's intentions relevant both to suggest defendant's motive and to rebut his claim of self-defense. Defendant failed to show plain error when trial court sustained an objection to a question defense counsel asked and when the trial court failed to instruct the jury sua sponte on the lesser mitigated offense of second degree murder. Defendant failed to preserve the objections in a motion for new trial and as he failed in showing the necessity of plain error review, these issues were waived. Under Apprendi, other than a prior conviction, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum needed to be submitted to a jury, and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(b) fell within the prohibition of Apprendi. The natural life sentence imposed was improper.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed, the sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded for resentencing.

People v. Davis


No. 3-00-0621


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 411; 766 N.E.2d 277; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 160; 262 Ill. Dec. 657



March 8, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 12, 2002. As Amended June 30, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit Will County, Illinois. No. 99-CF-486. Honorable Herman Haase, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and reversed, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence by a jury in the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, for aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated discharge of a firearm, after a conviction for aggravated battery with a firearm in a first trial was vacated.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the joinder of the aggravated discharge of a firearm after defendant's conviction for aggravated battery with a firearm in a first trial was vacated violated the mandatory joinder provisions of the Criminal Code of 1961, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1-1 et seq. (2000). Since the indictment made no attempt to differentiate between one pull of the trigger and another, the State was required to prosecute all of the offenses arising out of defendant's single act of firing the gun at the three victims in a single prosecution, and the State was precluded from amending the indictment after the first conviction was vacated. Defendant's conviction for aggravated battery with a firearm was affirmed because the statute creating the offense did not violate the single subject rule. The statute that enacted the offense was naturally and logically related to a single subject, crime. Thus, defendant failed to rebut the presumed constitutionality of the statute.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part and reversed in part.
