People v. Thompson


No. 2-00-0938


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 360; 765 N.E.2d 1209; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 161; 262 Ill. Dec. 601



March 8, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied April 10, 2002. Released for Publication April 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99--CF--2583. Honorable George J. Bakalis, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: From the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), defendant charged by indictment with aggravated driving under the influence of alcohol, and sentenced on a Class 4 felony, timely appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that defendant suffered no violation of his rights or of due process when his prior commissions of driving under the influence (DUI) were found to be the functional equivalent of "convictions" for sentencing. Based on a review of caselaw, under the facts presented, 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 11/501(d)(1)(A), (d)(2), as applied to the defendant, merely provide an enhanced penalty based on the commission of prior crimes. Both of defendant's prior commissions of DUI were the functional equivalent of the "convictions". The defendant's prior disposition of supervision for the commission of one prior DUI in 1983 and a sentence of probation for another DUI conviction in 1985 were the incidents at issue. They were not elements of the crime that needed to be proved to the trier of fact beyond a reasonable doubt. Rather, they were factors in aggravation that had to be proved at sentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

People v. Brooks


No. 3-01-0073


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


328 Ill. App. 3d 424; 765 N.E.2d 1160; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 149; 262 Ill. Dec. 552



March 5, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit. Peoria County, Illinois, No. 91--CF--144. Honorable Donald Courson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's life sentence was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to first degree murder and was sentenced to natural life in prison. Defendant's direct appeal was dismissed for failure to prosecute. Defendant's petition for postconviction relief was dismissed without an evidentiary hearing. Defendant's second petition for postconviction relief was dismissed as untimely. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his sentence violated the constitutional rule set forth in Apprendi and should be vacated. Defendant's primary argument was that the brutal and heinous nature of the crime was not proven beyond a reasonable doubt and therefore, Apprendi should control. The appellate court held, however, that the trial court did not sentence defendant based solely on a factor that was not alleged in the indictment or proven to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. The court noted that first degree murder while committing the forcible felony of robbery was plainly charged in the indictment. Further, the State presented evidence of the crime in open court, and the trial court found there was an adequate factual basis for the plea. Finally, the appellate court found defendant's guilty plea was a knowing admission of guilt of the criminal acts charged and all the material facts alleged. Thus, defendant was sentenced according to the statute for the offense to which he knowingly pled guilty.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

People v. W.B. (In re J.B.)


No. 1-99-3075


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 175; 765 N.E.2d 1093; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 131; 262 Ill. Dec. 485



February 26, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 12, 2002.
Appeal granted by In re J.B., 199 Ill. 2d 555, 775 N.E.2d 2, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 672 (2002)
Vacated by, Appeal dismissed by People v. Wanda B. (In re J.B.), 2003 Ill. LEXIS 771 (Ill., Apr. 24, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Lynne Kawamoto, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of petitioner-appellee's motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted petitioner State summary judgment, declaring respondent mother was an unfit parent of her two minor children under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. § 50/1(D)(q) (1998). The mother appealed. The mother argued that § 1(D)(q)'s 1998 amendment to create a statutory presumption of unfitness could not be applied retroactively to her 1992 aggravated battery conviction.


OVERVIEW: The mother hit the older minor with a cord, and after her guilty plea was convicted of aggravated battery. The mother did not consistently take her required medications for her psychiatric problems. The older minor was in a foster home when the mother delivered the younger minor. The younger minor was adjudicated at risk, based in part upon the mother's conviction for her striking the older minor and the mother's inability and unwillingness to care for the younger minor. The trial court then granted the State's petitions that the mother was an unfit parent to both minors. The appeals court upheld the State's arguments based upon § 1(D)(q). The mother's claim to raise her own child was a liberty interest but not a vested right. Section 1(D)(q) did not violate the Due Process or Equal Protection Clauses under a heightened protection strict scrutiny analysis. Section 1(D)(q) presumed that the mother was unfit, since she was convicted of a crime. Abuse of any child (not limited to the child for whom termination was sought), was a per se (not rebuttable) factor to establish parental unfitness, and could be applied retroactively to effect an overriding State interest.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

Valdovinos v. Luna-Manalac Med. Ctr.

APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION

February 21, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 29, 2002.
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Valdovinos v. Tomita, 2009 Ill. App. LEXIS 765 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Aug. 4, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John V. Virgilio and Susan Zwick, Judges Presiding.
Valdovinos v. Tomita, 188 Ill. 2d 585, 729 N.E.2d 505, 2000 Ill. LEXIS 363, 246 Ill. Dec. 132 (2000)
Valdovinos v. Luna-Manalac Med. Ctr., 307 Ill. App. 3d 528, 718 N.E.2d 612, 1999 Ill. App. LEXIS 620, 241 Ill. Dec. 41 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1999)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of plaintiffs-appellees' motion to voluntarily dismiss action without prejudice and order requiring that plaintiffs pay expenses of defendants-appellants/cross-appellees Luna and Manalac were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant health care providers appealed an order of the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) granting the motion of plaintiff representatives of a severely disabled child to dismiss their complaint without prejudice; the child's representatives cross-appealed an order that they pay many of the health care providers' litigation costs.


OVERVIEW: By the time the mother and trust (representatives) representing a severely disabled boy moved to voluntarily dismiss their negligence actions against the health care providers and a drug manufacturer (providers), 10 years had already been spent in discovery and motions practice. Because the trial had not yet begun at the time of the motion, and because the trial court had allowed the providers sufficient time to respond to the motion despite the representatives' failure to give adequate notice, and because the providers were awarded costs, the representatives were entitled to dismissal as a matter of right under 735 Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 219(e), for the award of costs to go beyond court costs, to include many of the providers' litigation expenses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Braman


No. 3-00-0755


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


327 Ill. App. 3d 1091; 765 N.E.2d 500; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 129; 262 Ill. Dec. 363



February 21, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication April 1, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 98-CF-280. Honorable Brain Nemenoff, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by indictment with the felony of aggravated driving under the influence of alcohol (DUI). The indictment alleged that defendant had two prior DUI convictions. A jury in the Circuit Court of Tazewell County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of the offense tried. The trial court then sentenced defendant to two years of probation and six months of work release. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The fact of defendant's two prior DUI convictions was not submitted to the jury. At the sentencing hearing, the State offered defendant's two prior DUI violations into evidence, which enhanced the offense from a Class A misdemeanor to a Class 4 felony. On appeal, defendant argued that (1) his conviction for felony DUI should have been reduced to misdemeanor DUI because the State presented no evidence to the jury that he had two prior DUI violations, and 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501(d)(1)(A) was unconstitutional pursuant to Apprendi. The appellate court held that the aggravated DUI terminology used in 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501 simply referred to an aggravated or enhanced sentence for a third or subsequent DUI. 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-501(d)(1)(A) was a recidivist sentencing statute for repeat DUI offenders. Apprendi was not violated when an offender was sentenced to an extended-term sentence based upon prior convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Kidd


No. 1-00-1492


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


327 Ill. App. 3d 973; 765 N.E.2d 488; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 114; 262 Ill. Dec. 351



February 20, 2002, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 19, 2002. Released for Publication March 29, 2002.
Appeal denied by People v. Kidd, 199 Ill. 2d 569, 775 N.E.2d 6, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 815 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Kidd v. Walls, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 5580 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 22091. Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.
People v. Kidd, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1482 (Ill. App. Ct., Dec. 26, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of defendant-appellant's post-conviction petition was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed denial, by the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), of post-conviction relief from that portion of a judgment convicting him on guilty plea of murder and robbery that sentenced him to an extended prison term.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to several grave felonies, and received a 70-year extended sentence, after being advised that the State of Illinois was seeking the death penalty and that the trial court was disposed to sentence him to up to 120 years. After he pled guilty, the Apprendi case announced the federal constitutional rule that any fact, other than a prior conviction, used to extend a defendant's sentence beyond a statutory maximum required a jury finding beyond reasonable doubt. Defendant's failure to preserve a constitutional issue would not have precluded review even if Apprendi had been decided earlier. In conflict with other Illinois appeals courts, the instant court applied this constitutional rule in cases of guilty pleas. Defendant's sentence did not violate Apprendi, however, because the trial court explicitly found defendant death penalty-eligible and then decided to impose an extended sentence by reason of heinousness. Death was the maximum sentence, so the rule was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of the petition.

El Sauz v. Daley


No. 1-00-3721


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 508; 765 N.E.2d 1052; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 117; 262 Ill. Dec. 444



February 20, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Rehearing Denied March 26, 2002. Released for Publication April 12, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 00 CH 5214. Honorable Julia Nowicki Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendants-appellees' motion to dismiss complaint for lack of jurisdiction was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff liquor retailer appealed dismissal for lack of jurisdiction by the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) of its challenge to the action of defendants, local liquor control commission, license appeal commission, and named officials in suspending the business's liquor license.


OVERVIEW: A liquor retailer in Chicago, Illinois, had its license suspended by the local liquor commission. Pursuant to 235 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/7-10, which applied specifically to liquor license review processes in Chicago only, the retailer was not permitted to challenge the decision, because it had failed to seek reconsideration of the initial decision within 20 days, and this lapse deprived a local reviewing agency, and subsequently a trial court, of jurisdiction to consider the retailer's appeal. The argument that the retailer's lawyer did not receive timely notice of the suspension failed because it was reasonable, and not a denial of due process or equal protection, to use ordinary mail notice within the city, and the lawyer should have arranged for mail to be monitored while he was out of town.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Torres


NO. 5-00-0315


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


327 Ill. App. 3d 1106; 764 N.E.2d 1206; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 112; 262 Ill. Dec. 89



February 15, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 00-CF-15. Honorable Patrick J. Hitpas, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, vacated, in part, and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Marion County Circuit Court (Illinois) convicting him on guilty verdict of residential burglary and from that portion of the sentencing order directing the corrections department to withhold 50 percent of his in-prison earnings until court costs were covered.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and another entered a family's burned-out mobile home and defendant stole some clothing before he and his friend left, afraid of being seen. The appeals court upheld defendant's conviction of residential burglary in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/19-3, instead of the less serious offense of burglary, because when the family left the mobile home that evening, they attempted to secure it and intended to return, although they never did move back in. The existence of two potential offenses arising out of the same conduct was not unconstitutional because they were mutually exclusive; no defendant could be convicted of both as a consequence of a single act. The trial court had, however, exceeded its authority in directing that half of defendant's earnings in prison be withheld until court costs had been repaid, so that portion of the sentencing order was vacated, but a direction that defendant pay court costs within six months after release was allowed to stand.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence, except that it vacated the portion of the sentencing order that directed that court costs be withheld from prison earnings. It remanded with directions to correct the sentencing order.

Hawthorne v. Vill. of Olympia Fields


No. 1-01-0447


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 301; 765 N.E.2d 475; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 94; 262 Ill. Dec. 338



February 8, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected February 15, 2002. Released for Publication March 29, 2002.
Appeal granted by Hawthorne v. Vill. of Olympia Fields, 199 Ill. 2d 554, 775 N.E.2d 2, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 662 (2002)
Affirmed by Hawthorne v. Vill.of Olympia Fields, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 767 (Ill., Apr. 17, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE DOROTHY KIRIE KINNAIRD, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of plaintiff-appellee's motion for partial summary judgment was affirmed, and defendants-appellees' motion to stay was denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant non-home rule municipality denied plaintiff owner variances to operate her home day care facility using a non-resident employee after determining her facility was not a home occupation permitted in R-1, R-2, and R-3 residential zones. A Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) judgment granted the owner's partial summary judgment motion in her declaratory and injunctive relief suit. The municipality appealed and moved to stay.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court determined that: (1) the municipality's zoning ordinance excluding commercial day care businesses in homes was not valid; (2) the municipality was partially pre-empted by Illinois law from regulating home day care to the extent regulations conflicted with the Child Care Act of 1969, 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1 et seq. (1998), and could not effectively exclude them through zoning. The appeals court summarized the reasons for child-care licensing. The operator was licensed and subject to regulation by the Illinois Department of Children and Family Services to provide home care. The non-home rule municipality only could exercise powers, including zoning regulations, specifically granted to it, and not reserved by, Illinois. Illinois policy mandated that home care be allowed and not excluded, notwithstanding the municipality's goal of neighborhood tranquility. The allowance of day care facilities in non-residential zones was not a substitute for the requirement to allow home care in residential zones. The appeals court compared other cases involving licensed occupations that had been effectively excluded by municipality regulations.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment and denied the motion to stay.

In re C.J.


Nos. 1-99-1005, 1-99-1006


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


328 Ill. App. 3d 103; 764 N.E.2d 1153; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 96; 262 Ill. Dec. 36



February 8, 2002, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 29, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 JD 12893. The Honorable Edward N. Pietrucha, Presiding Judge.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) judgment adjudicated that respondent minor was delinquent after he was arrested and detained by petitioner State for unlawful use and unlawful possession of a firearm. The minor appealed, contending that the pretrial detention provision of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, particularly 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-501 (1998), violated the United States and Illinois Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The minor was first arrested on possession of controlled substance. The State filed for adjudication of wardship on that charge but the proceedings were not finalized before the minor was arrested on the firearm charges. The appeals court noted that no judge had signed a detention order on the controlled substance charges. The minor did not have standing to contest constitutionality of the detention statute for the controlled substance charges but did for the firearm charges. The appeals court summarized the reasons for the differences between the constitutional protections for criminal defendants and the due process protections for juvenile defendants in the non-adversarial civil proceedings. The principal distinguishing factors were related to the primary goal of rehabilitating a juvenile. Therefore, the juvenile did not have to be afforded criminal protections under Ill. Const. art. I, § 7 (1990) and U.S. Const. amends. IV, VI (rights to preliminary hearing, effective counsel, and probable cause). 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/5-501 (1998) satisfied any U.S. Const. amend. IV probable cause requirements. There also was probable cause to detain defendant on the firearm charges.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Arguello


1-00-3418


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


327 Ill. App. 3d 984; 765 N.E.2d 98; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 77; 262 Ill. Dec. 272



February 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 29, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edward M. Fiala, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendant-appellee's motion to suppress evidence was reversed and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of cannabis and a controlled substance. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence and quash his arrest. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The vehicle driven by defendant was stopped and searched by police because of defendant's violation of Chicago's sound-device restriction ordinance, Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code § 11-4-1115 (1996) (ordinance). Defendant was charged with criminal offenses after he was found in possession of illegal drugs. In granting the motion to suppress, the trial court held that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that a regulation that was content neutral and was a place and manner type of regulation was subject to an intermediate level of scrutiny, while a strict scrutiny test was applied if the ordinance or statute was content-based. The ordinance was content neutral and was a constitutionally permitted time and place regulation. It was narrowly tailored to serve an important governmental interest and it allowed open ample alternative channels for communication of protected speech. Preserving quiet was a significant governmental interest and noise from a vehicle could be regulated. The trial court erred in ruling the ordinance unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting the motion to suppress was reversed and the case was remanded.

People v. Brown


NO. 4-99-0735


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


327 Ill. App. 3d 816; 764 N.E.2d 562; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 88; 261 Ill. Dec. 947



February 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 11, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 99CF254. Honorable Donald D. Bernardi, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed and cause was remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of unlawful use or possession of a weapon by a felon, in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/24-1.1(a) (1998), after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) and was sentenced to an extended term of six years, six months in prison, and ordered to pay $ 415 in court costs. He appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with unlawful use or possession of a weapon by a felon, domestic battery, and endangering the life or health of a child after his former girlfriend complained to police that he refused to leave her apartment, pushed her while she was holding her child, and was keeping a handgun in her apartment. Police obtained a key from the girlfriend's roommate and used it to enter the apartment. When they did so, they found defendant asleep, woke him, ordered him to dress, and asked him questions. They also searched the apartment and found a handgun. The appellate court held that (1) defendant had no standing to challenge the search because he had been asked to leave the apartment before the search occurred and, as such, was no longer a guest in the apartment; (2) defendant was not in custody when police initially questioned him and answers he gave to their questions were admissible even though police did not read Miranda rights to defendant until they found the handgun and arrested him; (3) the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction for use or possession of a weapon by a felon; but (4) the trial court incorrectly calculated court costs.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction but remanded the case with directions that the trial court correct its sentencing order to reflect a credit for public defender fees.

People v. Bell


No. 3-00-0423


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


327 Ill. App. 3d 238; 764 N.E.2d 551; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 100; 261 Ill. Dec. 936



February 6, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 21, 2002.
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Bell, 2007 Ill. App. LEXIS 3295 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., May 4, 2007)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Bell v. Walls, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 73612 (C.D. Ill., Aug. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 99--CF--255. Honorable Donald Courson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and vacated, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of home invasion, aggravated battery, and unlawful possession of a firearm by a felon. The Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, sentenced defendant to 25 years' imprisonment for home invasion and 5 years' imprisonment for the firearm conviction to be served concurrently. Defendant was not sentenced for aggravated battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he was the same person named in a certified copy of a 1992 conviction for attempted armed robbery. The appellate court noted that defendant did not object to the State's introduction of the certified copy of conviction. On the contrary, defendant accepted the judge's suggested manner of handling this evidence. Thus, on appeal, defendant could not contend the trial court was in error by doing what he asked. Defendant also argued the truth-in-sentencing provision of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(iii) violated his due process and jury trial rights under Apprendi. The appellate court concluded that since the maximum penalty under the statute was not increased, the truth-in-sentencing provision was not unconstitutional under Apprendi. Finally, defendant contended his aggravated battery conviction should have been vacated under the one-act, one-crime principles. Although the trial judge did not use the term, "one-act, one-crime," he did say that he would not impose a sentence for the defendant's aggravated battery conviction because it was based on the same physical act as the home invasion conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's aggravated battery conviction was vacated. The judgment was otherwise affirmed.

People v. Carney


No. 1-98-4677


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


327 Ill. App. 3d 998; 765 N.E.2d 1028; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 70; 262 Ill. Dec. 420



January 31, 2002, Decided  
March 7, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified upon Denial of Rehearing March 7, 2002. Released for Publication March 29, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97-CR-29458. Honorable Colleen McSweeney-Moore, Judge Presiding.

Original Opinion of November 13, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Ill. App. LEXIS 877.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After reversal by the Supreme Court of Illinois of the instant court's holding that the imposition of consecutive sentences on defendant for armed robbery and murder pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4 violated the rule of Apprendi, the court considered defendant's additional constitutional challenges to the consecutive sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant murdered the victim in the course of committing armed robbery, and was sentenced to consecutive sentences for each offense. His argument that his consecutive sentences without jury findings supporting them violated the constitutional rule of Apprendi had been rejected by the high court, but two appellate issues remained: whether the scheme violated due process and whether it constituted impermissible double sentence enhancement. The intermediate court found no constitutional impropriety. The armed robbery was a triggering offense within the meaning of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4 and it led to the serious injury, that is, the death of the victim. The sentences themselves were separate sentences, imposed for discrete offenses (since it was perfectly possible to commit armed robbery without physically hurting anyone), not two enhancements of a single sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's consecutive sentencing scheme.

 

1691 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fields


No. 1-00-0287


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


331 Ill. App. 3d 323; 772 N.E.2d 742; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 64; 265 Ill. Dec. 371



January 30, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied June 24, 2002. Opinion Modified June 28, 2002. Released for Publication July 2, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Fields v. Illinois, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 1617 (U.S. Feb. 24, 2003).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 CR 7911. Honorable Lon Shultz, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's dismissal of defendant-appellant's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), dismissing his petition for relief, pursuant to the Postconviction Hearing Act (the Act), 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (West 1998).


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the defendant had not waived his right to postconviction relief, as he could have raised his ineffectiveness of counsel argument on direct appeal. But the defendant had been examined and declared fit for trial. His counsel was not ineffective for failing to investigate the defendant's psychiatric records after he was released. Besides access to the records would not have changed this case, as no bona fide doubt existed as to the defendant's fitness to stand trial. The defendant failed to set forth the gist of a constitutional claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. The record contradicted the defendant's allegations that he was heavily medicated at the time of his guilty plea and that his attorney coerced him into pleading guilty. Summary dismissal of his petition was proper. The defendant received the required admonishments and made a quintessential waiver of his Apprendi-based sentencing objection by pleading guilty. See 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. Ann. 5/122-1 et seq. (West 1998). 1983 Ill. Laws 83 did not violate the single subject rule.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was affirmed.

 

1692 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wallace


No. 1-00-0331


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 20



January 18, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 CR 9785. Honorable Stanley J. Sacks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of aggravated possession of a stolen motor vehicle. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to eight years' imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: In response to defendants assignments of error, the appellate court held (1) since defendant failed to preserve the issue of impeachment of a witness by prior silence for review and the evidence was not closely balanced, the plain error doctrine did not apply, (2) the trial court's restriction of defendant's cross-examination of the officer was erroneous, however, the error was harmless since the evidence in the case overwhelmingly supported the conviction, (3) the prosecutor's commends regarding the impact of the car theft did not rise to the level of plain error, (4) since defendant had a prior burglary conviction, he was ineligible for treatment under treatment alternatives for special clients, (5) the sentencing statute was not unconstitutional since Apprendi made an exemption for recidivism, and (6) defendant was not entitled to a hybrid form of representation where he filed a motion pro se but claimed denial of his right to counsel when the court ruled on his pro se motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1693 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Reichert v. Court of Claims of Ill.


NO. 5-01-0222


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


327 Ill. App. 3d 390; 763 N.E.2d 402; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 39; 261 Ill. Dec. 432



January 18, 2002, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Pope County. No. 00-MR-4. Honorable Donald Lowery, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was reversed, transfer of venue was ordered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant university sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Pope County (Illinois) that denied its motion to transfer venue of a personal injury case instituted by appellee injured party.


OVERVIEW: The injured party filed a petition for a writ of certiorari in the circuit court, seeking the review of a decision of the court of claims that held that his damages were limited to the statutory maximum of $ 100,000. On appeal, the university argued that the cause of action was one for a writ of certiorari and that the cause of action arose in Sangamon County, where the proceedings and decisions of the court of claims sought to be reviewed occurred. According to the university, all transactions, and all parts thereof, between the injured party and the court of claims took place in Sangamon County. The petition for writ of certiorari did not seek the review of any facts or issues in the underlying personal injury lawsuit but only sought a determination as to whether the court of claims' decision violated the injured party's due process rights. None of the issues involved in the underlying cause of action were involved in the certiorari action. The proper venue for the certiorari action did not lie in Pope County, but in Sangamon County, where the principal office of the court of claims was located.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and venue was transferred to another county.

People v. Love


NO. 4-00-0942


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


327 Ill. App. 3d 313; 763 N.E.2d 829; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 40; 261 Ill. Dec. 580



January 16, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 14, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Livingston County. No. 00CF199. Honorable Harold J. Frobish, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court, Livingston County (Illinois), entered a final judgment of conviction after a jury found defendant guilty of aggravated battery in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-4(b)(6)(2000). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a prison inmate. A correctional officer opened his cell door. Defendant stepped outside and spit in the officer's face. As a result, the State charged him with aggravated battery. Before defendant's trial and out of the jury's presence, the trial court addressed at a hearing the issue of defendant's propensity to spit. It heard evidence about his history of misconduct, including the spitting. It also learned he had two convictions and other charges pending against him. Defendant told the trial court he would not spit in the courtroom. The trial court ordered him to wear a mask at trial. Both parties agreed it would be best not to explain the mask to the jury, but one witness identified defendant as the person wearing the mask. Defendant was convicted. His sentence was made consecutive to other sentences against him. After judgment was entered, the appellate court found: (1) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in ordering him to wear the mask, (2) he was not denied a fair trial when he was identified as the person wearing the mask, (3) he did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel, and (4) the consecutive sentencing was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Reeves


NO. 4-00-0317


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 1083; 762 N.E.2d 1124; 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 14; 261 Ill. Dec. 197



January 14, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 99CF1631. Honorable Michael Q. Jones, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Conviction Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of drug paraphernalia pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 600/2(d) by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), claiming the trial court erred in denying his motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that defendant was convicted for possession of a homemade crack pipe, a glass tube with a steel wool pad as a filtering agent. The presence of cocaine on the crack pipe supported the jury's finding that defendant intended to use the crack pipe to ingest or inhale drugs. However, the State did not show that the pipe had been marketed for use in growing, producing, storing, or ingesting drugs as required by § 2(d). Therefore, the trial court's denial of defendant's motion for judgment notwithstanding the verdict was in error.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed.

People v. Vasquez


No. 1-99-1888


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


327 Ill. App. 3d 580; 763 N.E.2d 779; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1501; 261 Ill. Dec. 530



December 31, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Rehearing Denied February 20, 2002. Released for Publication March 8, 2002.
Rehearing denied by, 02/20/2002
Appeal denied by People v. Vasquez, 199 Ill. 2d 576, 775 N.E.2d 8, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 891, 266 Ill. Dec. 446 (2002)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Appeal after remand at, Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Vasquez, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1949, 2012 IL App (1st) 103205U (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Colleen McSweeney-Moore, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder, armed robbery, and aggravated battery. A jury found defendant guilty of armed robbery and acquitted him of the other charges. The State moved to have defendant sentenced as an adult. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the motion and sentenced defendant to 30 years in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the sentencing statute under which he was charged as an adult was unconstitutional, the trial court abused its discretion in failing to take into account all statutory factors enumerated in the sentencing statute, and his sentence was disparate to that of his codefendants. The appellate court held that defendant's constitutional claim was waived on review since he conceded the issue. The appellate court next found that the trial court properly evaluated and applied the statutory sentencing factors. Thus, there was no abuse of discretion. Finally, as to defendant's argument that his sentence should have been reduced or his cause remanded due to the disparity of his sentence and his codefendants' sentences, the court found no error. The court noted that although it was the maximum nonextended sentence allowable, defendant's sentence was within the statutorily permissible range. In addition, the record established that the codefendants entered into voluntary negotiated guilty pleas, whereby they pled guilty to the offenses of first degree murder and armed robbery, while defendant declined the plea agreement and chose to proceed to trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Jesse C. (in Re D.P.)


No. 1-00-0529


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


327 Ill. App. 3d 153; 763 N.E.2d 351; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1487; 261 Ill. Dec. 381



December 28, 2001, Decided  
December 28, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Donna Cervini, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of respondent-appellant's motion for continuance was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State filed an action against respondents, mother and father, seeking an order declaring that their son was neglected and abused. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) denied the father's motions to continue the hearing, adjudicated the child a ward of the state, and appointed the Illinois Department of Children and Family Services as the child's guardian. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: Criminal charges were filed against a father who allegedly shook his infant son and struck the child in the face. Before those charges were resolved, the State filed a petition for adjudication of wardship against the father and the child's mother. The father moved to postpone action on the State's petition until after the criminal charges he was facing were resolved but the trial court denied that motion, held a hearing on the State's petition, and adjudicated the child a ward of the State. The appellate court held that the fact the father was facing criminal charges did not, by itself, outweigh the factors that supported the trial court's decision to proceed with the juvenile case, the trial court acted within its discretion by denying the father's motions for a continuance, and the trial court's action did not force the father to choose between losing his parental rights or waiving his right not to incriminate himself.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Guzzo v. Snyder


No. 3-01-0002


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 1058; 762 N.E.2d 663; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1492; 261 Ill. Dec. 94



December 28, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Rehearing Denied February 14, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Honorable Charles P. O'Connor Judge, Presiding. No. 2000--MR--289.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of petition for writ of habeas corpus was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, director of the department of corrections and the warden of a correctional center, challenged appellee inmate's habeas corpus award, from the Circuit Court for the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the director of the department of corrections abused his discretion under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3 in establishing an unwritten policy denying good-time credit to inmates charged with or convicted of domestic battery. Because the refusal of the inmate's good-time credit was based on an unwritten policy that excluded inmates with domestic battery arrests from eligibility, the director abused his discretion when he refused to award good-time credit based on an unwritten policy, outside the scope of his authority. Because the director did not offer any other standard to deny good-time credit, the court assumed that but for the unwritten policy the inmate would have been entitled to good-time credit. Because it was necessary for the trial court to order the director to exercise his discretion and grant inmate good-time credit before releasing him, he was not entitled to habeas corpus relief. The inmate was entitled to immediate discharge from custody under mandamus.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

1699 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kidd


No. 1-00-1492


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1482



December 26, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS DECISION IS NOT FINAL UNTIL EXPIRATION OF THE 21 DAY PETITION FOR REHEARING PERIOD.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 22091. Honorable James B. Linn, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's denial of defendant-appellant's post-conviction petition was affirmed and defendant-appellant's sentence was modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with first degree murder and armed robbery. Defendant waived a jury trial and entered a guilty plea. Defendant was sentenced to an extended term of 70 years' imprisonment based on the trial judge's finding that mitigating factors precluding imposition of the death penalty. Defendant filed a motion for reconsideration. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily dismissed the motion. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant argued his extended-term sentence was unconstitutional under Apprendi. The State argued defendant's failure to raise an Apprendi challenge to his sentence in his postconviction petition waived the challenge. The appellate court held that because the element used to enhance defendant's sentence was never charged in the indictment, defendant could not be said to have waived his right to have the jury determine that element beyond a reasonable doubt. Therefore, defendant's plea of guilty did not waive his right to have a sentencing factor, except for a prior conviction, which extended his sentence beyond the maximum allowed by statute and which was not charged in the indictment, determined beyond a reasonable doubt, and Apprendi applied. The State next argued that the 70-year sentence imposed was not beyond the prescribed statutory maximum. The appellate court held that the maximum sentence defendant could receive was 60 years since he was never charged with brutal and heinous behavior, and since defendant was sentenced to a term of years, the statutory maximum for murder in Illinois was 60 years.


OUTCOME: Denial of defendant's postconviction petition was affirmed. The extended-term sentence of 70 years' imprisonment was modified to 60 years' imprisonment.

People v. Nicholas K. (In re Nicholas K.)


No. 2-00-0968


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 497; 761 N.E.2d 352; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1497; 260 Ill. Dec. 508



December 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 18, 2002.
Appeal granted by In re Nicholas K., 198 Ill. 2d 615, 770 N.E.2d 219, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 428, 264 Ill. Dec. 325 (2002)
Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Nicholas K. (In re Nicholas K.), 799 N.E.2d 1045, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 1395, 279 Ill. Dec. 242 (Ill. App. Ct., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 98--JD--329. Honorable Thomas E. Mueller, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment requiring respondent-appellant to register as a juvenile sex offender was reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) respondent child challenged the court's order that required him to register as a juvenile sex offender.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the sex offender registration statute, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq., did not require juveniles to register as sex offenders. Although the statute contained a definition of a juvenile sex offender, it did not explicitly require juvenile sex offenders to register. Under rules of statutory construction, the lower court erred by reading into 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/1 et seq. a requirement that children register. Sex offenders and juvenile sex offenders were defined as separate classes, but only sex offenders were required to register. Moreover, requiring a delinquent juvenile to register as a sex offender was inconsistent with the purposes of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1 et seq. In the absence of a clearer expression of its intention, the court would not assume that the legislature intended to authorize the release of information about a minor and his offense when the same information could not be released under 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1 et seq.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was reversed.

Alarm Detection Sys. v. Vill. of Hinsdale


No. 2-00-1393


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 372; 761 N.E.2d 782; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1496; 260 Ill. Dec. 599; 2002-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P73,554



December 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 10, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99-CH-1362. Honorable Bonnie M. Wheaton, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendant-appellee's motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff alarm company sought a permanent injunction preventing defendant village from enforcing an ordinance that required owners of commercial buildings to connect their fire alarm systems directly to the village's fire board for monitoring. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) granted summary judgment in favor of the village. The alarm company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that a municipality had the authority under 65 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/11-8-2, 11-30-4 (1998) to amend national building or fire codes or draft its own codes as it determined necessary to protect the public safety and welfare. Accordingly, the village had the authority to enact the instant ordinance requiring all fire alarm systems in new and existing commercial buildings be tied directly to the village's fire board. The appellate court noted that there was a reasonable basis for the determination by the village that public safety required the application of the ordinance to existing buildings. In addition, the appellate court held that the ordinance was not a de facto regulation on fire alarm companies, nor was it a violation of the Illinois Antitrust Act, 740 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1 et seq. (1998). Finally, the appellate court concluded that although the alarm company failed to raise the issue prior to its appeal, the ordinance was not an unconstitutional infringement upon its right to contract, but rather was a reasonable legislative judgment tailored toward the improvement of the public welfare and safety.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Sample


No. 1-99-2204


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


326 Ill. App. 3d 914; 761 N.E.2d 1199; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1461; 260 Ill. Dec. 643



December 18, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication February 13, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Sample v. Illinois, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7087 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Appeal denied by People v. Sample, 198 Ill. 2d 629, 770 N.E.2d 224, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 586, 264 Ill. Dec. 330 (2002)
Writ of certiorari denied Sample v. Illinois, 537 U.S. 910, 123 S. Ct. 253, 154 L. Ed. 2d 189, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 7087 (2002)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Sample, 381 Ill. App. 3d 1140, 966 N.E.2d 605, 2008 Ill. App. LEXIS 2663, 359 Ill. Dec. 284 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2008)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Sample, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 3047 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 14, 2010)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Sample v. Chandler, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 119513 (N.D. Ill., Aug. 23, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edward Fiala, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's convictions and sentence were affirmed, clerk was ordered to ament mittimus to reflect 999 days served.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of four counts of first degree murder, one count of armed robbery, and one count of home invasion, after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County(Illinois) and he was sentenced to consecutive sentences of 35 years imprisonment for first degree murder, 6 years imprisonment for armed robbery, and 6 years imprisonment for home invasion. He appealed his convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree murder, armed robbery, and home invasion after co-defendants told police they entered a house with defendant to commit a robbery and that defendant killed a person inside the house during the robbery. During his opening statement at trial, the prosecutor described the conversations that police had with the co-defendants and, when he questioned the officers who conducted the investigation, the prosecutor asked them to recount what the co-defendants had told them about the defendant's actions. Defense counsel did not object to the prosecutor's opening statement or the police officers' testimony and, at the close of trial, a jury returned a general verdict finding defendant guilty of all charges. The appellate court held that: (1) the prosecutor's conduct breached the investigative process exception to the hearsay rule, but, as there was other evidence of defendant's guilt, the violation was harmless error; (2) the trial court properly sentenced defendant to consecutive sentences even though the crimes arose from a single course of conduct; but (3) defendant was not given proper credit against his sentence for time already served.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder, armed robbery, and home invasion, and sentenced him to consecutive terms of imprisonment for those offenses, but it also directed the clerk of the trial court to amend the mittimus to reflect that defendant was entitled to 999 days of credit for time served.

Hous. Auth. v. Keys


No. 3-00-0902


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 577; 761 N.E.2d 338; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1457; 260 Ill. Dec. 494


May 17, 2001, Submitted  
December 14, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit Will County, Illinois. No. 00-LM-915. Honorable Raymond A. Bolden Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment in favor of defendant-appellee was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff housing authority appealed from a Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit Will County (Illinois) holding that public housing tenants could not be evicted for the criminal activities of guests or family members over whom they had no control, after housing authority brought a forcible entry and detainer action against defendant tenant to evict her from her residence.


OVERVIEW: Where the tenant was a patient in the hospital when a crime occurred, had no knowledge of its commission, and had no restraining influence over the criminals at the time they committed the crime, the trial court's finding they were not "under tenant's control" was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. The fact the one of the criminals was named on the tenant's lease did not warrant her eviction. The lease was ambiguous, and its terms had to be construed against the housing authority as the drafter of the lease. The tenant had to exercise control over household members and guests as well as other persons who engaged in criminal activity in order to allow the tenant's eviction. It appeared that the eviction of innocent tenants was not part of the congressional scheme for housing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

1705 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hale


NO. 5-99-0700


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 455; 762 N.E.2d 59; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1474; 260 Ill. Dec. 793



December 14, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Edwards County. No. 98-CF-13. Honorable Terry H. Gamber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder, aggravated battery with a firearm, armed violence, attempted murder, and aggravated vehicular hijacking. A jury found the murder qualified for the death penalty. A judge in the Circuit Court of Edwards County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to life for the murder and 30-year consecutive prison terms for each of the other crimes. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued his convictions should be overturned and he should be granted a new trial, or alternatively that his life sentence was unconstitutional. Defendant alleged the trial court erred in allowing the submission of other-crimes evidence to the jury because such evidence infected his trial with a prejudice that compelled reversal of his convictions. The appellate court noted that the State possessed overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. The appellate court held that the probative value of the other-crimes evidence was compelling, and under such a circumstance, it was within the trial judge's discretion to admit the evidence, even though the State's other evidence may well have carried the day without it. The appellate court also noted that while the other-crimes evidence demonstrated a penchant for killing and stealing, it had the kind of probative value necessary to outweigh the prejudice to defendant. Finally, the appellate court held that since the life sentence was established as the maximum sentence in lieu of death, the life sentence was imposed in accordance with the procedural safeguards of a jury trial, and there was no constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The convictions for first-degree murder, aggravated vehicular hijacking, and attempted murder, and sentences imposed, were affirmed. The convictions for aggravated battery with a firearm and armed violence were vacated.

People v. Cabrera


No. 3-00-0049


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 555; 764 N.E.2d 532; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 925; 261 Ill. Dec. 917



December 12, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Withdrawn from the Bound Volume January 16, 2002. Modified on Denial of Rehearing January 16, 2002. Released for Publication January 16, 2002.
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Cabrera, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 3880 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., July 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 89--CF--665. Honorable Rodney Lechwar, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Cabrera, 294 Ill. App. 3d 1119, 721 N.E.2d 860, 1998 Ill. App. LEXIS 1770, 242 Ill. Dec. 581 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed. The conviction was affirmed. Defendant filed a postconviction petition. The State moved to dismiss the petition. The court granted a partial dismissal and held an evidentiary hearing on the remaining portion. The Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial District, Will County, Illinois, dismissed the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) his sentence was unconstitutional under Apprendi, (2) he was denied due process when Illinois Department of Corrections (DOC) personnel coerced an exculpatory witness not to testify; and (3) the court should have held an evidentiary hearing on the dismissed portion of his petition, which alleged that his trial attorneys were ineffective for failing to call two exculpatory witnesses. The appellate court held that there was no error in sentencing defendant to life because such an imposition could be made based on that fact that the murdered individual was a DOC employee or that defendant previously had been convicted of murder in another state. The court also held that because the exculpatory witness's testimony was unsubstantiated and not credible, there was no violation of defendant's constitutional rights with respect to denial of the witness's testimony. Finally, the appellate court concluded it could not say, as a matter of law, that defense counsel's decision not to call certain witnesses was a matter of trial strategy. The court remanded the matter for an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and the case was remanded.

 

1708 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Morissette v. Briley


No. 3-01-0193


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 590; 761 N.E.2d 333; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 926; 260 Ill. Dec. 489



December 12, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication January 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois, No. 00-MR-587. Honorable Charles P. Connor, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery, and was sentenced to life imprisonment under the Habitual Criminal Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 et seq. (1983). Defendant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, and the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois), granted the State's 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-615 motion to dismiss. Defendant appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the Act was unconstitutional under the Apprendi doctrine. A writ of habeas corpus was available to obtain the release of a prisoner where some occurrence after the prisoner's conviction entitled him to release. In Apprendi, the Supreme Court held that, except for a prior conviction, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the statutory maximum had to be submitted to the finder of fact and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held that defendant met all of the conditions for a mandatory natural life sentence under the Act. The appellate court held that the Act did not violate the rule of Apprendi. The Apprendi decision made clear that it did not consider recidivism to be a fact that fell within its holding. Because the Act was not unconstitutional under Apprendi, defendant was not entitled to release from prison. Taking the facts in the light most favorable to the State, the appellate court held that defendant did not allege facts in his petition that would compel the trial court to grant him habeas corpus relief. Therefore, the trial court properly granted the State's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1709 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lee


No. 3-00-0664


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 882; 762 N.E.2d 18; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 907; 260 Ill. Dec. 752



December 7, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal granted by People v. Lee, 198 Ill. 2d 625, 770 N.E.2d 222, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 542 (2002)
Reversed by People v. Lee, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1420 (Ill., Aug. 21, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County, Illinois. No. 88-CF-235. Honorable Michael E. Brandt Judge, Presiding.
People v. Lee, 292 Ill. App. 3d 941, 688 N.E.2d 673, 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 802 (Ill. App. Ct. 3d Dist., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was vacated, defendant-appellant's sentence was modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Tazewell County (Illinois) judgment dismissed as frivolous defendant's successive post-conviction petition. Defendant appealed and argued that (1) 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-2.1 ( 2000) was unconstitutional; and (2) his 80-year extended term sentence violated the constitutional rule set forth in Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's 1989 first degree murder conviction had been affirmed, and dismissal by the trial court of defendant's 1994 first post-conviction relief petition had been affirmed. The appeals court had previously held that 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-2.1 (2000), enacted under 1983 Ill. Laws 942, did not violate the single subject clause of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) (1970). The appeals court then determined that Apprendi could be applied retroactively as falling within the second Teague exception as a core due process right. Apprendi held that as a matter of due process, any facts, other than a prior conviction, that increased the penalty for an offense beyond the statutory maximum had to be submitted to the jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant timely filed, under 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1(c) (2000), the instant second post-conviction relief petition two months after the United States Supreme Court decided Apprendi in June 2000. The Apprendi due process claim could not have been presented in the earlier proceeding. Accordingly, the appeals court refused to apply the procedural limits of waiver and res judicata to bar defendant's successive petition.


OUTCOME: The appeals court found that the imposition of defendant's extended term sentence of 80 years was unconstitutional. The appeals court, therefore, vacated the judgment of the circuit court and modified defendant's sentence to the maximum possible sentence for first degree murder under the applicable statute, which was 60 years in prison.

People v. Rivera

December 5, 2001, Filed

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing March 21, 2002. Released for Publication October 25, 2002.
Modified and rehearing denied by, 03/21/2002
Appeal denied by People v. Rivera, 201 Ill. 2d 604, 786 N.E.2d 196, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 1054, 271 Ill. Dec. 938 (Oct. 2, 2002)
Related proceeding at Rivera v. Mueller, 596 F. Supp. 2d 1163, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 9308 (N.D. Ill., Feb. 2, 2009)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by People v. Rivera, 2011 IL App (2d) 091060, 962 N.E.2d 53, 2011 Ill. App. LEXIS 1248, 356 Ill. Dec. 709 (Dec. 9, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 92--CF--2751. Honorable Christopher C. Starck, Judge, Presiding.
People v. Rivera, 284 Ill. App. 3d 1134, 708 N.E.2d 1282, 1996 Ill. App. LEXIS 4674, 237 Ill. Dec. 242 (Ill. App. Ct. 2d Dist., Nov. 19, 1996)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder. Defendant appealed. The conviction was reversed and the case was remanded. Defendant filed a motion to authorize funding for an expert witness. The motion was denied. Defendant was retried. A jury convicted defendant of murder. Defendant filed a motion for a new trial. The motion was denied. Defendant was sentenced in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois) to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his right to present a meaningful defense was violated when the trial court barred him from presenting expert testimony regarding the phenomenon of false confessions. The appellate court held that the trial court properly excluded the testimony because the fact that people in stressful situations may falsely confess was not a concept beyond the understanding of ordinary citizens and within the comprehension of the jury. Defendant next argued that the trial court improperly allowed the State to elicit an opinion from a witness that defendant killed a victim. The appellate court noted that although the testimony reflected the witness's opinion, the jury was free to accept or reject that opinion. Defendant next argued that the trial court coerced a verdict from the jury. The appellate court noted that the record reflected that the foreperson informed the deputy that after review of testimony they could ultimately reach a verdict. Thus, there was no error in the trial court's communication to the jury. The court next determined that defendant's motion for a continuance was properly denied based on the circumstances surrounding the request.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Barnes v. Chi. Hous. Auth.


No. 1-00-2856


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


326 Ill. App. 3d 710; 761 N.E.2d 283; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 895; 260 Ill. Dec. 439



December 3, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 15, 2002. Released for Publication January 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 L 9046. The Honorable Diane Joan Larsen and Sophia H. Hall, Judges Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment dismissing plaintiffs-appellees' third amended complaint and granting defendant-appellant's motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband, wife, and minor daughter, appealed judgments by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing their negligence complaint against defendant housing authority and the grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant management company based on governmental immunity factors.


OVERVIEW: While the father was visiting his wife and daughter at a public housing development, he saw the daughter beaten by gang members and was also shot by one of them. Plaintiffs sued the housing authority and the management company for failure to provide adequate security. The trial court found that both entities were immune from liability. The appellate court reviewed the various sections of the state tort immunity act and agreed. The housing authority was not only immune from liability for negligence, it was also immune from liability for willful and wanton acts. The "voluntary undertaking" doctrine did not supercede its statutory immunity. The management company was also immune since it was created as part of a federal program, was engaged in governmental activities, and was entirely government funded. The plaintiffs did not establish their alleged constitutional violations.


OUTCOME: The judgments were affirmed.

Gelb v. Air Con Refrigeration & Heating

People v. Manos


No. 1-00-2816


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


326 Ill. App. 3d 698; 761 N.E.2d 208; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 883; 260 Ill. Dec. 364



November 26, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 14, 2002. Released for Publication January 22, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 00 CH 1859. The Hon. Lester D. Foreman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court order affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants dentists refused to produce patient appointment books and two patients' files named in a subpoena duces tecum. Plaintiff department filed a complaint to enforce the subpoena. The dentists answered, asserting the physician-patient privilege. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted the department's motion. The dentists appealed.


OVERVIEW: The dentists contended on appeal that summary judgment was improper because issues of material fact existed; dentists were considered surgeons under Illinois law, and therefore covered by the physician-patient privilege; and the material requested by the department fell under the physician-patient privilege. Upon review, the appellate court concluded that no issues of material fact existed which precluded summary judgment. Further, the failure of the dentists to offer facts to rebut the department's assertion that they were under an investigation was fatal to their argument that summary judgment on this basis was improper. The appellate court found that the issuance of the subpoena alone was sufficient for the circuit court to conclude that the documents were needed, and that there was a sufficient basis for the circuit court to conclude that the purpose of the investigation was to protect the public from risk of harm from the dentists. As to privilege, the appellate court held that the dentists were surgeons, and therefore covered by the physician-patient privilege. The court held that the patient files were protected, but the appointment book records were not privileged.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed in part, reversed in part, and the case was remanded.

May 21, 2001, Assigned; June 20, 2001, Submitted  
November 19, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 24, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Phillips v. Illinois, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6108 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).
Writ of certiorari denied Phillips v. Illinois, 537 U.S. 829, 154 L. Ed. 2d 43, 123 S. Ct. 126, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6108 (2002)
Vacated by, Remanded by People v. Phillips, 208 Ill. 2d 550, 804 N.E.2d 1066, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 385, 281 Ill. Dec. 771 (2004)

DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's convictions and sentence were affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her controlled substance conviction and sentence by the Circuit Court of the 14th Judicial Circuit Henry County, Illinois, claiming that the admission of lab reports violated her constitutional right to confrontation and that her mandatory prison sentence violated Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's vehicle was stopped by the police after it veered off the roadway. After she was placed under arrest for driving with a suspended license, her vehicle was searched and bags of a white substance were discovered. Defendant's signed, written statement and a lab report proving the substance was cocaine were admitted at trial. The appellate court held that not only did defendant fail to object to the admission of the lab reports at trial, she stipulated to them. Therefore, they were properly admitted into evidence pursuant to the stipulation rather than the unconstitutional statutory provisions of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/115-15. Because she was sentenced under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3(c)(2)(D), the amount of cocaine found was a sentencing factor and not an element of the crime. Therefore, the judge could make the finding and impose the mandatory minimum sentence.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

People v. Pittman


1-00-2224


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


326 Ill. App. 3d 297; 761 N.E.2d 171; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 844; 260 Ill. Dec. 327



November 8, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 5, 2001. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 13, 2001. Released for Publication January 4, 2002. Writ of certiorari denied: Pittman v. Illinois, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 6676 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable John J. Wasilewski, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's dismissal of defendant-appellee's petition for post-conviction relief was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicted defendant of two counts of armed robbery. The trial court imposed concurrent extended term sentences of 50 years. The convictions and sentences were affirmed on direct appeal. Defendant then filed a pro se petition seeking post-conviction or habeas corpus relief. The trial court summarily dismissed the petition. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, under Apprendi, he was entitled to relief because former Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-5-3.2(b)(1), 1005-8-2 (1981) (now codified at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1), 5-8-2), pursuant to which his extended term sentences were imposed, were unconstitutional as they allowed a sentence beyond the statutory maximum upon the finding of facts not submitted to the jury for proof beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held that the Apprendi Court exempted prior convictions from the category of sentence enhancing facts which had to be submitted to a jury for proof beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant also argued that the extended term sentence violated his right to a jury trial under the Illinois constitution. The appellate court found that a prior conviction did not relate to the commission of the offense with which an accused was charged and that a prior conviction was the result of proceedings in which defendant had the right to a trial by jury and the State was required to establish his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. These safeguards mitigated constitutional concerns regarding due process rights and jury trial guarantees.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Ligons

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his enhanced and extended-term sentence for theft by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois), claiming it was unconstitutional pursuant to Apprendi and that he was entitled to one additional day of credit for time served.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of theft. The trial court took judicial notice of his prior theft conviction and enhanced the conviction from a misdemeanor to a felony. He was sentenced to an extended term in prison, but was given credit for time served. Defendant was entitled to one day of credit for each day (or portion thereof) that he spent in custody prior to sentencing.
