1717 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Scullark


No. 1-99-1722


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 876; 759 N.E.2d 565; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 814; 259 Ill. Dec. 785



October 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 24, 2001. Released for Publication December 10, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Stanley Sacks, Judge Presiding.

People v. Scullark, 1-99-1722, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 134 (Mar. 13, 2001, Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., Gordon, J)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of murder and aggravated kidnapping, for which he was sentenced to natural life imprisonment. Thereafter, defendant filed a post conviction petition. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) summarily dismissed the petition on the ground that it was time-barred. Defendant then filed a motion to reconsider, which was denied. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not ask to amend his petition, but did claim in his motion to reconsider that he was free from culpable neglect in failing to file on time. Defendant alleged that he was placed in segregation for six months and was denied access to his legal materials until after the deadline. The appellate court held that defendant could be excused from failing to file in a timely manner if he showed that he was not culpably negligent. A post conviction petition did not need to include allegations of lack of culpable negligence, but could be later amended to include them. Defendant should not have been summarily deprived pursuit of post-conviction relief simply because he neglected to label his motion correctly. The trial court erred in not considering the motion for reconsideration as a motion to amend the pleadings. If defendant had been placed in segregation through no fault of his own or otherwise prevented from filing his petition for a period of time after the deadline, his failure to file in a timely manner was not culpable negligence. However, defendant's Apprendi issue was stricken, as Apprendi could not be applied retroactively to cases pending on collateral review.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The case was remanded in order to afford defendant an opportunity to amend his petition. The attempt to raise Apprendi issues through the post-conviction appeal was stricken.

Arnett v. Snyder


NO. 4-00-0895


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


331 Ill. App. 3d 518; 769 N.E.2d 943; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 819; 264 Ill. Dec. 106



October 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Sangamon County. No. 99MR407. Honorable Thomas R. Appleton, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendant-appellee's motion for summary judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmates appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) granting defendant Director of the Illinois Department of Corrections' motion for summary judgment, where the inmates sought to enjoin a discipline policy utilized by the director.


OVERVIEW: The prison warden established controlled-feeding status, whereby inmates received "meal loaf" as a punishment for certain misconduct relating to food. Meal loaf consisted of a combination of regular food items prepared in a loaf served only with water. At the most, the punishment was imposed for six days at a time with a one day break. The inmates claimed that controlled-feeding status violated former 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-8-7(b)(1) and the Eighth Amendment. The appellate court affirmed. Former § 3-8-7(b)(1) only prohibited the denial to inmates of nutritionally adequate food for disciplinary reasons. Because the meal loaf was nutritionally adequate, it did not violate former § 3-8-7(b)(1). The policy did not violate the Eighth Amendment, because the Eighth Amendment only required that the food be adequate to maintain health; it did not need to be tasty or aesthetically pleasing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Newell Co. v. Petersen


No. 2-99-1232


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 661; 758 N.E.2d 903; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 836; 259 Ill. Dec. 495


January 31, 2001, Assigned; May 22, 2001, Submitted  
October 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 29, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of McHenry County. No. 97-LA-245. Honorable Michael J. Sullivan, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered, cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, chairman of the holding company, holding company, and acquired company filed an interlocutory appeal of the order of the Circuit Court of McHenry County (Illinois) denying their motion to dismiss plaintiff shareholder's complaint, alleging, among other things, the chairman's improper purchase of stock from the other management shareholders and the contravention of the shareholder's agreement.


OVERVIEW: The holding company was a Delaware corporation with its principal place of business in Illinois. The holding company's shareholders' agreement contained a choice of law provision choosing Nebraska law. When the stock purchases made by the holding company chairman occurred, leading to this action, none of the parties were residents of Illinois. However, the chairman thereafter became an Illinois resident. The subject of this appeal was whether the Illinois borrowing statute for limitations periods, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-210, was applicable to this case and whether the Delaware limitations period governed the shareholder agreement. The appellate court found that 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/13-210 was applicable to this case, although none of the parties was an Illinois resident when the cause of action accrued, because the chairman later became a resident before the limitations period of the jurisdiction in which the cause of action accrued expired. The Delaware limitations period governed the shareholder agreement, because Delaware, as the state of the holding company's incorporation, had an overriding interest in regulating the internal affairs of the holding company.


OUTCOME: The appellate court found that the Illinois borrowing statute for limitations period was applicable and a Delaware limitations period applied to the shareholder agreement. The case was remanded.

 

1720 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Purcell


No. 2-01-1053


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 551; 758 N.E.2d 895; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 837; 259 Ill. Dec. 487



October 30, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 29, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 01--CF--1783. Honorable Rosemary Collins, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's order denying defendant-appellant's motion for pretrial bail and finding bail statute constitutional was vacated, cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, accused of murdering his wife, appealed an order of the Winnebago County Circuit Court (Illinois) denying bail. He challenged the constitutionality of 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/110-4(b), and also argued that the trial court abused its discretion in denying his request.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, charged with murdering his wife, faced a possible sentence of life imprisonment under Illinois law. His request for pretrial release on bail was denied pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/110-4, which precluded bail where the proof of a defendant's guilt was evident or the presumption of guilt was great. The trial court held that defendant had failed to satisfy his statutory burden that he did not fall under that prohibition. The appeals court, after surveying case law from many jurisdictions, determined that the portion of the statute that imposed a burden of proof on defendant violated his due process right, under Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, to a presumption of innocence. Once that part of the statute was severed, however, the rest of the statute simply tracked Ill. Const. art. I, § 9, and could be upheld.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order denying bail and remanded for a new proceeding at which the State was to bear the burden of proof.

Mitchell v. Banary (In re M.J.)


1-00-0590


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 826; 759 N.E.2d 121; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 813; 259 Ill. Dec. 641



October 29, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehehearing Denied November 29, 2001; Released for Publication December 10, 2001. As Corrected November 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99 D 079287. The Honorable Gay Lloyd Lott, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's grant of defendant-appellee's motion to dismiss was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed a judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissing her complaint to establish defendant boyfriend's paternity of her children, conceived by artificial insemination, and to impose support obligations.


OVERVIEW: The mother and her boyfriend had a 10-year relationship. During that time, the mother was artificially inseminated, conceived, and delivered twins. The boyfriend provided financial assistance and decided with the mother that the sperm was to be from a Caucasian donor so that the offspring would appear to be a product of their relationship. The mother terminated the relationship when she discovered that the boyfriend was already married. She sued for paternity and support. The trial court granted the boyfriend's motions to dismiss. The appellate court held that the boyfriend's oral promise to support the children was unenforceable. 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 40/3(a) (act) required written consent to an insemination procedure. The act did not discriminate against children born through artificial insemination to unmarried women.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1722 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lee


NO. 5-99-0166


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 643; 759 N.E.2d 930; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 824; 259 Ill. Dec. 869



October 26, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Review or Rehearing granted by: People v. Lee, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 1478 (Ill. App. Ct. Sept. 12, 2001).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 98-CF-370. Honorable Donald Lowery, Judge, presiding.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of July 20, 2001, Previously Reported at: 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 587.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury of capital murder, residential burglary, robbery, and theft over $ 10,000. After a death penalty sentencing hearing, the jury did not impose the death penalty. The Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois), entered judgment and imposed a life sentence for the murder, concurrent 7-year terms for the robbery and theft, and a 15-year consecutive sentence for the residential burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the State's peremptory challenge of the sole African-American juror, asserting the removal was racially motivated. The State gave three race-neutral reasons for the challenge. The appellate court found the record supported the State's tendered reasons to challenge the juror, and there was no deprivation of the right to equal protection of the law. The use of defendant's prior fingerprint card did not cause undue prejudice, as the State made no mention of the fact that defendant was under arrest when the inked prints were made, and there were many potential explanations for a government agency to have a person's fingerprints on file. Also, since they were necessary to establish identity, it was not necessarily error to admit them into evidence. As for the sentencing, since a jury determined beyond a reasonable doubt those facts that exposed defendant to a life term, the sentence was proper. The claim challenging the validity of the consecutive sentences was also rejected, as the sentences defendant received were within the statutory range, and Apprendi considerations did not apply to consecutive sentences.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. McGee


No. 3-00-0670


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 165; 761 N.E.2d 741; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 812; 260 Ill. Dec. 558



October 26, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 3, 2001. Released for Publication December 3, 2001.
Modified and rehearing denied by, 12/03/2001
Appeal denied by People v. McGee, 198 Ill. 2d 626, 770 N.E.2d 223, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 551, 264 Ill. Dec. 329 (2002)
Appeal denied by People v. McGee, 221 Ill. 2d 660, 857 N.E.2d 679, 2006 Ill. LEXIS 1285, 306 Ill. Dec. 280 (2006)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. McGee, 2014 IL App (3d) 120291-U, 2014 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 485 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit. Will County, Illinois. No. 99--CF--81. Honorable Stephen White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit Will County (Illinois) of aggravated criminal sexual assault, aggravated vehicular hijacking, and aggravated battery. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim's vehicle was parked in the driveway when she was assaulted in a residence and her keys were taken. Defendant then fled in the victim's vehicle, leaving her behind. The appellate court held that the term "immediate presence," as the term applied to the vehicular hijacking statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/18-3(a), meant that the vehicle was within the immediate control of the alleged victim at the time of the occurrence. In this instance, the victim's car was in the driveway outside the residence in which she was assaulted and her keys were taken. Consequently, the vehicle was not taken from the immediate presence of the victim as required by the vehicular hijacking statute. Under these circumstances, the State failed to meet its burden of proof and a rational trier of fact could not have found that the elements of aggravated vehicular hijacking were proven beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated vehicular hijacking was reversed and the sentence was vacated.

People v. Barbara R. (In re T.B.)


No. 3-01-0178


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 566; 758 N.E.2d 489; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 807; 259 Ill. Dec. 366



October 24, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois. No. 98-JA-154. Honorable Jerelyn D. Maher Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed an order by the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit, Peoria County, Illinois, upholding petitioner State's change of the permanency goal for her children from "return home" to "substitute care" pursuant to 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-28(3).


OVERVIEW: The State filed a juvenile petition asking that the court find the mother's children neglected because of a history of domestic violence and drug abuse. The State subsequently filed a supplemental juvenile petition alleging violations of the previous court order. The trial court ordered that the children be placed in shelter care and found the mother to be unfit. She was ordered to complete a variety of tasks and attend permanency reviews. The court ordered a permanency goal of "return home" for the children. It later changed the permanency review order to "substitute care." The mother appealed. The appellate court held that the permanency review orders were not final orders. The statute stated that such an order was immediately appealable. However, only the state supreme court, not the legislature, could provide for appeals from judgments other than final judgments.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.

People v. Johnson


NO. 5-99-0637


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


333 Ill. App. 3d 935; 776 N.E.2d 238; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 809; 267 Ill. Dec. 101



October 23, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County. No. 98-CF-511. Honorable David W. Watt, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the imposition of an extended sentence for his conviction of attempted murder and aggravated assault, by the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), claiming a violation of his constitutional rights pursuant to Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder and aggravated assault after he donned a ski mask to conceal his identity and savagely assaulted a complete stranger. The trial judge imposed an enhanced sentence after finding that the effort at murder was accompanied by exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty. The appellate court found that the trial judge was applying the law, as it then existed, in a correct manner. However, since that time the United State Supreme Court made its ruling in Apprendi. Therefore, the enhancement of defendant's sentence beyond the statutory maximum of 30 years was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed as modified to a 30-year determinate term of imprisonment.

 

1726 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Ret. Bd.


No. 1-00-1549


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


329 Ill. App. 3d 589; 771 N.E.2d 431; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 795; 264 Ill. Dec. 727



October 15, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Modified Upon Denial of Rehearing May 20, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 92 CH 4216. The Honorable Bernetta Bush, Thomas A. Hett, Dorothy K. Kinnaird, Mary Jane Theis, Judges Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On October 1, 1998, the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered an order granting in part and denying in part plaintiff officers' motion for summary judgment in their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights action. On April 11, 2000, the trial court entered an order denying the officers' amended motion for clarification and reconsideration of the October 1, 1998, order. The officers appealed. Defendant board cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the officers alleged that: (1) the trial court erred in refusing to adopt a construction of 1989 Ill. Laws 272 that would increase their pension benefits for service after age 63 and thereby avoid an unconstitutional interpretation; and (2) the trial court erred by not limiting the application of its ruling to only the officers whose benefits had been reduced. The appellate court held, first, that the board's conclusion that the three percent annual increases would accrue after age 63, but would not be paid until the officers actually retired, was consistent with the general rule that pension acts were to be liberally construed in favor of a pensioner's rights. Second, the application of 1989 Ill. Laws 272 unconstitutionally diminished the officers' benefits without due process of law, because they were not afforded a predeprivation hearing, as was required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 5-189 (1989). Third, the officers were not entitled to service credit for years where they made no corresponding contribution. Finally, Ill. Const. art. XIII, § 5, did not provide that a person had a vested right in any beneficial changes in a pension system.


OUTCOME: The October 1, 1998, order granting in part and denying in part the motion for summary judgment was affirmed with respect to plaintiffs whose benefits were diminished but reversed with respect to those whose benefits increased. The cause was remanded with directions.

People v. Wilder


No. 1-99-1425


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 987; 760 N.E.2d 496; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 789; 260 Ill. Dec. 79



October 12, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 10, 2001. As Amended October 17, 2001.
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Wilder, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 302 (Ill. App. Ct., Mar. 31, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CR 00265. Honorable Lawrence Fox, Judge Presiding.

 People v. Wilder, 321 Ill. App. 3d 608, 749 N.E.2d 357, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 193.

 People v. Wilder, 195 Ill. 2d 596, 749 N.E.2d 984, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 869.
People v. Wilder, 321 Ill. App. 3d 608, 749 N.E.2d 357, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 193, 255 Ill. Dec. 256 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2001)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) judgment, after a jury trial, convicted and sentenced defendant as follows: an aggregate 60-year sentence: 45 years for first degree murder, 15 years for armed robbery and 15 years for aggravated kidnapping, with the 15-year sentences concurrent to each other and consecutive to the 45-year sentence. Defendant appealed after denial of his motions for new trial and to reconsider his sentence.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court affirmed the trial court's exercise of discretion (1) to allow evidence of defendant's gang affiliation, noting, in part, that testimony regarding gang hierarchy was relevant and admissible to explain an otherwise inexplicable act and to establish an "advancement within the ranks" motive for the crime; and (2) to not allow defendant a 30-day continuance to find non-prison trial clothing for his 450 pound frame since defendant had three years to find clothing and was able to find clothing a day after denial of his motion. The appeals court reviewed 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a), (b) (1994). The trial court imposed consecutive sentences after its finding consecutive sentences were necessary to protect the public from further criminal conduct. Upon remand, the trial court was to determine whether (1) the offenses were part of a single course of conduct, and, if so, apply § 5/5-8-4(a) consecutive sentencing only if all three components of § 5/5-8-4(a) were met; and (2) if the offenses were not part of a single course of conduct, apply § 5/5-8-4(b) consecutive sentencing if it determined such sentencing was necessary to protect the public.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment of conviction, but reversed and vacated the consecutive sentences and remanded for further consistent proceedings, which included resentencing.

 

1728 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pomykala


No. 3-99-0715


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 390; 759 N.E.2d 916; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 784; 259 Ill. Dec. 855



October 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication December 13, 2001. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing December 31, 2001. Rehearing Denied December 13, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 99--CF--249. Honorable Stephen White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant-appellant's conviction for reckless homicide was vacated, trial court's judgment was reversed, and cause was remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois), defendant was convicted of two counts of reckless homicide. The trial court vacated one count and sentenced defendant to a term of 14 years' imprisonment on the remaining count. The trial court also ordered that half of defendant's monthly income be withheld for application to costs. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the reckless homicide statute and the accompanying jury instructions mandated a presumption of recklessness that relieved the State of its burden of proving recklessness beyond a reasonable doubt, and other errors. The charges arose from an incident in which defendant caused a fatal auto accident while intoxicated. Defendant claimed that his brakes malfunctioned. 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/9-3(b) stated that in cases involving reckless homicide, being under the influence of alcohol or any other drug or drugs at the time of the alleged violation would be presumed to be evidence of a reckless act unless disproved by evidence to the contrary. A mandatory presumption was one in which the finder of fact had to presume certain facts and was not free to reject the proffered presumption. All mandatory presumptions violated defendant's due process rights under both the Illinois and United States Constitutions. The court held the statute and jury instructions in question created a mandatory presumption which compelled the jury to presume that defendant was acting recklessly, thus effectively removing the burden of proving that element from the State.


OUTCOME: The reckless homicide conviction was reversed and remanded.

 

1729 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Birkett v. City of Chicago


Nos. 2-00-0615 & 2-00-0715 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 196; 758 N.E.2d 25; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 791; 259 Ill. Dec. 180



October 10, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 14, 2001. Released for Publication November 14, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99-L-957. Honorable James W. Jerz, Judge, Presiding. Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 97-L-1042. Honorable Rodney W. Equi and James W. Jerz, Judges, Presiding.

 People ex rel. Birkett v. City of Chicago, 184 Ill. 2d 521, 705 N.E.2d 48, 1998 Ill. LEXIS 1916 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a religious organization and the people, appealed from decisions of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) dismissing their suits for nuisance arising out operation of the airport owned by appellee, a city. The trial court dismissed the suits based on the city's immunity under the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1-101. The appeals were consolidated.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act), 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1-101, gave the city immunity from liability for nuisance, as a tort. The Act applied only to tort actions and did not bar actions for constitutional violations. Sections 1-204, 2-201, of the Act, codified at 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 10/1-204, 10/2-201, were not unconstitutionally vague. Finding immunity was proper even where no specific employee of the city was identified as causing the injury, because a municipal corporation can act only through the actions of its agents and officials. The nuisance alleged resulted from the airport's existence, location, and the manner in which the runways are laid out. These could only result from acts of discretion by city agents in policy-making positions. Therefore, the city's actions were discretionary in nature. Dismissal of the claims for nuisance was affirmed. However, as the Act did not protect the city from claims for injunctive relief, the trial court's orders were modified to dismissal of the claims without prejudice to afford the parties the opportunity to seek equitable relief.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgments were affirmed, but modified to dismissal of the claims without prejudice. The matters were remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this opinion.

People v. Watkins


Nos. 2-00-0643, 2-00-0644 cons.


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 13; 757 N.E.2d 117; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 794; 258 Ill. Dec. 732



October 10, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 30, 2001. Rehearing Denied October 19, 2001. Released for Publication October 19, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. Nos. 98--CF--1246, 99--CF--749. Honorable Ronald B. Mehling, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) used evidence that defendant had one prior conviction to elevate two charges of misdemeanor retail theft to felonies. After defendant pled guilty to both felonies, the court sentenced him to consecutive three-year terms in prison. Defendant filed a motion to vacate his pleas and also asked the court to reconsider its sentence, and he appealed after the court denied both motions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of misdemeanor retail theft after he stole merchandise valued at $ 22 from one store and merchandise valued at less than $ 150 from another store. The trial court accepted evidence that defendant had a 1993 conviction, and pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/16A-10(b) (1998), it used that conviction to elevate both offenses to Class 4 felonies. After hearing evidence that defendant had a drug problem, was HIV positive, and had an extensive criminal history, the trial court ordered defendant to serve the maximum period of confinement authorized for each offense and that he serve his sentences consecutively. The appellate court held that (1) the trial court was allowed to use defendant's 1993 conviction to enhance both charges because those charges were separate and factually distinct; (2) the trial court was required to impose consecutive sentences once the charges were enhanced because defendant committed his second offense while he was out of jail on bond awaiting trial for his first offense; and (3) defendant was not sentenced in violation of the United States Supreme Court's Apprendi opinion.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1731 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wade


No. 3-00-0487


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


326 Ill. App. 3d 396; 760 N.E.2d 491; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 892; 260 Ill. Dec. 74


June 7, 2001, Submitted  
October 10, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified November 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 98-CF-486. Honorable Clark Erickson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed, in part, and vacated, in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty, in the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois) to one count each of predatory criminal sexual assault of a child and child pornography. He was sentenced to consecutive prison terms of 15 and 7 years, respectively. Those terms were subsequently reduced to 12 and 5 years. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that his prison sentences should have been modified to run concurrently and that his aggregate sentence was unconstitutionally increased without proof beyond a reasonable doubt that the two offenses were committed as part of a single course of conduct. Prior to imposing sentence, the trial court had determined that the offenses were committed during a single incident. The appellate court held that the mandatory consecutive sentencing provisions of 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4 did not increase punishment exceeding the statutory maximum for each discrete offense, but only controlled how multiple sentences were served. Accordingly, sentences imposed pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4 did not violate the rule of Apprendi. Since the trial court determined that the two offenses were committed during a single course of conduct, it properly imposed mandatory consecutive sentences. However, the trial court proceedings in ordering forfeiture of a computer and digital camera were error as no forfeiture complaint was filed and no forfeiture hearing was held. The State's first mention of forfeiture did not come until the prosecutor's sentencing recommendation.


OUTCOME: The order of forfeiture was vacated, and the remainder of the judgment was affirmed.

People v. Knippenberg


No. 3-00-0101


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 251; 757 N.E.2d 667; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 779; 258 Ill. Dec. 978


July 19, 2001, Submitted  
October 4, 2001, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 10th Judicial Circuit. Peoria County, Illinois. No. 98-CF-1124. Honorable Donald C. Courson, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court which convicted defendant of six counts of theft in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/16(a)(2)(a) (West 1998), dispersing charitable trust funds without authority and for his personal benefit in violation of 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 460/19 (West 1998), and failure to register as a professional fund raiser in violation of 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 460/6(a) (West 1998).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that: (1) the prosecution, conviction, and sentencing for each of the offenses he was convicted of were void and erroneous; (2) he was unconstitutionally sentenced to consecutive terms of imprisonment; and (3) he was denied the effective assistance of counsel. The appellate court found that nothing in the plain language of 225 Ill. Comp. Stat. 460/19 (West 1998) indicated an intent to change the concurrent power of the attorney general and the state's attorney to prosecute criminal violations. Further, the appellate court found that there was sufficient evidence to prove defendant guilty of this offense beyond a reasonable doubt. Finally, the appellate court found that defendant was properly sentenced to consecutive terms of imprisonment, and that under the holding in Apprendi, defendant's sentence was not increased merely by sentencing him to consecutive terms.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Newbolds


NO. 5-01-0162


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 192; 757 N.E.2d 664; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 772; 258 Ill. Dec. 975



October 2, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by People v. Newbolds, 197 Ill. 2d 576, 763 N.E.2d 775, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1611, 261 Ill. Dec. 526 (2001)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Newbolds, 352 Ill. App. 3d 678, 816 N.E.2d 1114, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 1202, 287 Ill. Dec. 903 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2004)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Newbolds, 2006 Ill. App. LEXIS 198 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., Mar. 20, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 98-CF-460. Honorable Ronald Eckiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois) convicted defendant of home invasion. The trial court found the victim of the crime suffered great bodily harm, and the court ordered defendant to serve 85 percent of his sentence, pursuant to section 3-6-3(a)(2)(iii) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(iii). Defendant moved to reconsider, the trial court denied the motion, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the statutory provision under which he was required to serve 85 percent of his term of imprisonment is unconstitutional under the Apprendi doctrine. The Apprendi doctrine stated that other than the fact of a prior conviction, any fact that increased the penalty for a crime beyond the prescribed statutory maximum must be submitted to a jury and proved beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court held that 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(iii) did not violate the Apprendi doctrine. Whether defendant served all or part of the term of imprisonment to which he was sentenced, that term would not be in excess of the prescribed maximum penalty for home invasion. The Apprendi doctrine did not constrain the legislature's ability to define the manner in which a sentence imposed within the statutory range must be served. The statutory scheme under which defendant was required to serve a minimum portion of his term of imprisonment neither altered the maximum penalty for the crime committed nor created a separate offense calling for a separate penalty, it only limited the sentencing court's discretion in selecting a penalty within the range already available to it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Turner


NO. 5-00-0445


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 185; 757 N.E.2d 658; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 773; 258 Ill. Dec. 969



October 2, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Massac County. No. 00-CF-24. Honorable Terry J. Foster, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Massac County (Illinois) convicting defendant of aggravated criminal sexual assault. On appeal, defendant claimed that he was improperly convicted twice for the same conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to predatory criminal sexual assault of a child in 1996. After serving his prison sentence, defendant was arrested on the same conduct, and he was convicted of aggravated sexual assault. The State argued that because predatory criminal sexual assault had been invalidated by the Illinois Supreme Court, and it was treated as if the law never existed, defendant's original conviction and the sentence he served were to be treated as if they never occurred. The appellate court reversed. Although the law was to be treated as if it had never existed, defendant's conviction and time served in prison existed and could not be treated otherwise. Double jeopardy prohibited the State from prosecuting defendant on the same conduct twice.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded.

People v. Bryant


No. 1-00-2218


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 448; 758 N.E.2d 430; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 758; 259 Ill. Dec. 307



September 28, 2001, Decided  
September 28, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 27, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Bryant, 205 Ill. 2d 596, 803 N.E.2d 486, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1522, 281 Ill. Dec. 82 (2003)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by People v. Bryant, 362 Ill. App. 3d 1231, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 5206 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied United States ex rel. Bryant v. Acevedo, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 179675 (N.D. Ill., Dec. 19, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98-CR-30071. Honorable Timothy Chambers, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence for attempted first-degree murder and aggravated battery by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), claiming self-defense, that the State failed to tender evidence, and that the sentence was excessive.


OVERVIEW: Defendant severely beat and stabbed his wife. He claimed she started the dispute. He was convicted and sentenced following a bench trial. The appellate court held that the evidence negated his claim of self-defense. Any rational trier of fact could have found him guilty. Defendant failed to show any bad faith by the State when it could not produce the briefcase or its contents. The briefcase was considered lost or destroyed. Any evidence therein would have been speculative and uncorroborated. The trial court found that the offense was exceptionally brutal and heinous and indicative of wanton cruelty, meriting an extended-term sentence. However, the sentence exceeded the maximum and had to be reduced pursuant to Apprendi. The error was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing.

 

1736 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Lewis


No. 1-99-3950


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 435; 758 N.E.2d 438; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 759; 259 Ill. Dec. 315



September 28, 2001, Decided  
September 28, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication November 27, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Lewis, 198 Ill. 2d 602, 766 N.E.2d 243, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 124 (2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Dismissed by United States ex rel. Kirk v. Terhune, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 5936 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 88-CR-9683. Honorable Daniel J. Kelley, Judge Presiding.
People v. Lewis, 165 Ill. 2d 305, 651 N.E.2d 72, 1995 Ill. LEXIS 9 (1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On remand from the Illinois Supreme Court, defendant appealed his life sentence by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) based upon his prior murder conviction in California and his existing conviction for murder in Illinois pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and armed robbery and was sentenced to death. The state supreme court vacated his death sentence and remanded for a new sentencing hearing. On remand, he was sentenced to a mandatory term of natural life imprisonment due to a prior murder conviction in California. He contended that the sentence was improper because his prior conviction was for second-degree murder, not first-degree murder as required by Illinois. The appellate court held that para. 1005-8-1 did not distinguish between first- and second-degree murder. It reviewed the laws of both states and found that they were similar. The similarity was not found in the statutory labels, but in the shared mental state requirements needed to support a conviction. The mental state required for second-degree murder in California was equivalent to that required for first-degree murder in Illinois.


OUTCOME: The sentence was affirmed.

 

1737 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fender


NO. 5-00-0227


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


325 Ill. App. 3d 168; 757 N.E.2d 645; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 775; 258 Ill. Dec. 956



September 27, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Clay County. No. 99-CF-12. Honorable Patrick L. Duke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery after a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Clay County (Illinois) and he was sentenced to 16 years' imprisonment. Before it sentenced defendant, the trial court found that his victim had suffered great bodily harm, and as a result, the court ordered defendant to serve 85 percent of the 16-year sentence it imposed. Defendant appealed his conviction and sentence.


OVERVIEW: During a robbery, defendant hit a convenience store clerk with his gun, cutting her head and breaking her finger. At trial, defendant's girlfriend, testified that defendant threatened to kill her and her child if she talked to police. Another witness (defendant's cellmate) testified that defendant kind of made an offer to pay someone to kill his girlfriend and her child. The appellate court held that (1) defendant waived his right to argue on appeal that testimony provided by his girlfriend and cellmate was inadmissible evidence of uncharged misconduct because his counsel did not object to that testimony at trial or raise the issue in a posttrial motion; (2) because the record showed that defense counsel did not object to the girlfriend's testimony or the cellmate's testimony as a trial strategy, defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel; and (3) 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(iii) (1998), which required the trial judge to order that defendant serve 85 percent of his sentence because the judge found that defendant's victim suffered great bodily harm, did not violate the United States Supreme Court's Apprendi holding.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

1738 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Owner-Operated Indep. Drivers Ass'n v. Bower


No. 1-99-4497


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 1045; 757 N.E.2d 627; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 729; 258 Ill. Dec. 938



September 21, 2001, Decided  
September 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 31, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff truck owner-operators and their association appealed a Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois) judgment dismissing their constitutional challenge, based in the Commerce Clause, to defendant state tax official's collection of the Illinois motor fuel use tax, pursuant to 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/13a, from commercial vehicles using the Illinois Tollway.


OVERVIEW: At § 13a of the Illinois Motor Fuel Tax Law, 35 Ill. Comp. Stat. 505/13a, the legislature imposed a tax on commercial motor carriers for use, on Illinois highways, of fuel purchased outside the state. A national association of truck owner-operators, and some individual members, challenged the practice of collecting the tax from users of the Illinois Tollway as violative of the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The appeals court held that the association lacked standing to pursue the constitutional challenge, because in Illinois associations could not sue on their members' behalf unless the organization was also directly injured. It then sustained the tax as satisfying a four-prong test of constitutionality, since the owner-operators' activity had a nexus with Illinois, the tax was fairly apportioned, it did not discriminate against interstate commerce, and was fairly related to services provided by Illinois, which included more than mere tollway use.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of dismissal.

 

1739 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Edmonds


No. 1-00-1827


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 439; 757 N.E.2d 619; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 726; 258 Ill. Dec. 930



September 20, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 31, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 99-CR-15048. Honorable Mary Maxwell Thomas, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver on a public way within 1,000 feet of a school.


OVERVIEW: A police officer witnessed defendant selling drugs. Defendant met the client at the end of an alley. The client handed the defendant money. They proceeded to a vacant lot 10 to 20 feet from the end of the alley, and defendant handed drugs to the client. Defendant was arrested, and crack cocaine was found near defendant in the vacant lot. A police investigator measured the distance between where defendant was arrested to the nearest school, and it was 752 feet. In the indictment, defendant was charged with selling drugs within 1,000 feet of a school, but the indictment did not contain the citation to the portion of the criminal code that outlawed the conduct. The conviction was affirmed. Although the original indictment did not contain the citation for the offense, it sufficiently apprised defendant of the charge against him. The State was properly permitted to amend the indictment to insert the missing citation, as the defect was not material, and it did not change the elements of the offense charged. The measurement was sufficiently accurate that no reasonable doubt existed as to whether the offense occurred within 1,000 feet of a school.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1740 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Blackwell


No. 1-99-4064


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 354; 757 N.E.2d 589; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 719; 258 Ill. Dec. 900



September 18, 2001, Decided  
September 18, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 31, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Blackwell, 203 Ill. 2d 552, 788 N.E.2d 730, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 490, 273 Ill. Dec. 139 (2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Blackwell v. Illinois, 540 U.S. 889, 124 S. Ct. 273, 157 L. Ed. 2d 162, 2003 U.S. LEXIS 6413 (2003)
Related proceeding at United States ex rel. Blount v. Briley, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 44064 (N.D. Ill., Apr. 15, 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Blackwell v. McCann, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 75092 (N.D. Ill., Sept. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 97 CR 21738. Honorable Thomas M. Tucker, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), defendant was found guilty of first degree murder and attempted murder. At sentencing, the trial court imposed an extended-term sentence for the murder and determined that defendant was eligible for consecutive sentences. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot a gun into a crowd of people. One victim, age 71, was hit by a gunshot and died from it. Another victim was hit by gunshots and was severely injured. The trial court imposed an extended-term sentence for the murder on the basis that the murder victim was 71-years-old. The trial court also determined that defendant was eligible for consecutive sentences because defendant inflicted severe bodily harm on the attempted murder victim. Defendant argued that the extended-term sentence and consecutive sentences were unconstitutional under Apprendi, and that the sentences were excessive. The appellate court held that although an Apprendi violation may have occurred where the age of the victim was not submitted to a jury, such violation amounted to harmless error where, had the issue of the victim's age been submitted to a jury, a jury would have still found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt. Apprendi explicitly disclaimed any holding regarding consecutive sentencing. The record showed that the trial court did consider factors in mitigation and allowed the mitigation testimony. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1741 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Boston


No. 2-00-0201


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


324 Ill. App. 3d 557; 755 N.E.2d 1058; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 733; 258 Ill. Dec. 239



September 13, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 12, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 98--CF--0165. Honorable Philip L. DiMarzio, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) convicted defendant of armed robbery. The trial court adjudged defendant a habitual criminal and sentenced him to life imprisonment. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with robbing a bookstore at knifepoint. Defendant argued that (1) the trial court erred in admitting into evidence a knife found near the crime scene, and (2) the mandatory life sentence provisions of the Habitual Criminal Act, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-1 et seq. (2000) were unconstitutional. The victim of the robbery testified on both direct and redirect examination that defendant used a knife in the attack and that she saw a knife. She specifically testified on redirect examination that she got a good look at the knife. Further, she identified an exhibit offered by the State as that knife. The appellate court held that the trial court properly admitted the knife. Regarding the sentencing, the maximum prison sentence for defendant's crime was 30 years, but since the trial court adjudged defendant a habitual criminal, he was sentenced to life. The appellate court held that in the context of a sentencing under the act, Apprendi did not require the fact of prior Class X convictions to be submitted to a fact finder and proven beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Reed


NO. 5-98-0777


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


324 Ill. App. 3d 671; 755 N.E.2d 1000; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 708; 258 Ill. Dec. 181



September 7, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by, 09/07/2001
Appeal denied by People v. Reed, 197 Ill. 2d 578, 763 N.E.2d 776, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1635, 261 Ill. Dec. 527 (2001)
Appeal denied by People v. Reed, 198 Ill. 2d 604, 766 N.E.2d 243, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 81, 262 Ill. Dec. 623 (2002)
Appeal denied by People v. Reed, 202 Ill. 2d 691, 787 N.E.2d 179, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 36, 272 Ill. Dec. 364 (2003)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by People v. Reed, 2012 IL App (5th) 090629-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1262 (2012)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Reed v. Duncan, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 111732 (S.D. Ill., Aug. 21, 2015)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Reed v. Hammers, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 117090 (S.D. Ill., Sept. 2, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 96-CF-1958. No. 96-CF-1959. Honorable Edward C. Ferguson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 96-CF-1958, Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded. No. 96-CF-1959, Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant brothers convicted in Madison County Circuit Court (Illinois) of murder and hijacking challenged the sufficiency of evidence and admissibility of certain evidence, and alleged prosecutorial misconduct, disparate sentencing of various participants in the scheme, and unconstitutional imposition of enhanced sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant twin brothers operated a hijacking scheme with two accomplices. After a hijacking ended in a brutal murder, one accomplice considered testifying against them, and eventually the other accomplice, courted by prosecutors, did. Despite his own checkered past, the accomplice received almost no jail time. The appeals court upheld defendants' convictions. The accomplice's uncorroborated testimony was sufficient to convict them, if the jury found him credible. The trial court's rulings on the admissibility of relevant evidence and keeping in check prosecutorial excesses were correct. The disparity in outcome for the four participants was logically related to their degrees of cooperation with the prosecution. The only issue on which defendants' appeal was successful was their constitutional challenge to the non-jury imposition of greater than maximum enhanced sentences based on the crime's brutality. The court modified one brother's sentence to the statutory maximum and remanded for resentencing of the less culpable brother.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions, but modified one defendant's first-degree murder sentence and vacated the other defendant's sentence, remanding for resentencing in accordance with its opinion.

People v. Pugh


No. 1-97-4622


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 336; 758 N.E.2d 319; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 695; 259 Ill. Dec. 196



September 4, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Rehearing Denied October 23, 2001. Released for Publication November 27, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Edwin A. Gausselin, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of sentence of Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), imposed after vacation of a death sentence previously imposed, challenging, in particular, the imposition of extended-term and consecutive sentences. He also argued that a finding of aggravating circumstances had to be made beyond a reasonable doubt.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to murder and related offenses after shooting a hostage in a hold-up. His initial death sentence was vacated by the Supreme Court of Illinois. He appealed the sentenced imposed after remand, but the appeals court affirmed. It held that trial court after remand had properly considered only the murder conviction and sentence, because that was the only judgment vacated. The trial court had supported its findings of brutality and heinousness in determining that defendant was death eligible, and because it found those factors beyond reasonable doubt, a second finding was not required when the trial court sentenced defendant to an extended term in prison instead. That term was not beyond the statutory maximum, because the maximum sentence was death. However, imposition of consecutive sentences was improper, under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-4, because it resulted in more prison time than the original sentences.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment to make the sentences run concurrently, and affirmed.

 

1744 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Lyons v. Ryan


No. 1-00-2692


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 1094; 756 N.E.2d 396; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 684; 258 Ill. Dec. 414



August 31, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 15, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ELLIS E. REID, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs state citizen and political watchdog organization sued defendants former state secretary of state (SOS), and now governor, his political committee, and certain SOS employees to, inter alia, impose a constructive trust on funds and benefits allegedly illegally received while the SOS was the SOS. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed the action. Plaintiffs appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, inter alia, alleged that defendants used the SOS's position to issue commercial drivers licenses to non-qualified drivers in exchange for political contributions. The dispositive issue was whether plaintiffs had standing to sue and thus whether the circuit court had jurisdiction. The appeals court agreed that plaintiffs did not have standing. 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/20-104(b) (that provided a private citizen could sue to recover the damages authorized by 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/20-102 to 20-104 on behalf of the affected government unit) was declared unconstitutional to the extent it purported to confer standing. Section 5/20-104(b) conflicted with the inherent powers of the state attorney general as the proper person to direct the legal affairs of the state and to sue in cases where the state was the real party in interest. The appeals court stated that the Illinois Supreme Court had consistently held that the public interest was not served by allowing certain government agencies or private persons to assume the inherent powers of the attorney general. Dismissal was properly granted, so the courts declined to consider the merits of plaintiffs' claims.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the orders.

 

1745 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mason


No. 1-99-2805


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 762; 756 N.E.2d 365; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 671; 258 Ill. Dec. 383



August 28, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 15, 2001. Certiorari Denied May 13, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3394.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 CR 4234. Honorable Joseph Urso, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court of Illinois remanded defendant's appeal of his murder and attempted murder convictions and consecutive sentences by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to the appellate court to determine if defendant's counsel was ineffective and if his sentences were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and attempted first-degree murder after a bench trial and was sentenced to consecutive terms. Trial testimony established that he was involved in a shoot-out at a liquor store where a child was killed and one of the shooters was injured. After appeals to both an appellate court and the state supreme court, the case was remanded back to the appellate court. The appellate court held that defendant's counsel was not ineffective based on the record before it. Because counsel had impeached a witness with inconsistent statements, he was not required to use the witness's earlier testimony as substantive evidence. In addition, because defendant was initially tried in a bench trial, there was no possibility of jury confusion. Defendant's sentences were each within the statutory range. Therefore, they were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The sentences and convictions as originally imposed were affirmed.

 

1746 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Stroger v. Reg'l Transp. Auth.


No. 1-00-2545


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 970; 756 N.E.2d 328; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 657; 258 Ill. Dec. 346



August 24, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 15, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE MOSHE JACOBIUS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated; case remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiffs, the president of a county board of commissioners and a registered voter, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied their motion for a preliminary injunction and granted the defendants', the regional transportation authority (RTA) and two of its divisions, motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The plaintiffs brought an action for injunctive and declaratory relief against the defendants alleging that certain provisions of the Regional Transportation Authority Act (RTA Act), 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. 3615/1.01 et seq., violated certain principles of the Illinois Constitution. On appeal, the plaintiffs argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by concluding that the "one person, one vote" guarantee embodied in Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 and Ill. Const. art. III, § 3 did not apply to appointed bodies, such as the RTA boards. Upon review, the appellate court reversed the judgment. The allegations of plaintiffs' complaint revealed that the directors were not appointed on the basis of one man-one-vote as required under 70 Ill. Comp. Stat. 3615/3.01(h) (1998). In light of traditional statutory construction, which ascribed meaning to all provisions of a statute, the appellate court found the trial court's analysis insufficient to dispose of the plaintiffs' action on a motion to dismiss for failure to state a cause of action.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and the case was remanded.

People v. Peacock


No. 1-98-3552


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 749; 756 N.E.2d 261; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 648; 258 Ill. Dec. 279



August 21, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 15, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Peacock, 788 N.E.2d 733, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 489 (Ill., 2003)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Peacock v. Ill., 2003 U.S. LEXIS 5928 (U.S., Oct. 6, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Richard L. Samuels, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of first degree murder, aggravated vehicular hijacking, armed robbery, and aggravated kidnapping.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and a co-conspirator car jacked the victim's car, and the co-conspirator shot the victim twice and left him to die. The victim was 60 years old. Defendant waived a jury trial, but the next day he attempted to withdraw the waiver when he changed his mind. The trial court denied the withdrawal. Defendant was sentenced to an extended term of 80 years for the murder based on findings that the offense was accompanied by heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty, and it was committed against a person 60 years of age or older. The appellate court affirmed. Defendant waived the issue as to whether he was improperly denied a jury trial, because he did not raise the issue in a posttrial motion. The issue was not subject to plain error review. Although the age of the victim was not presented to the trier of fact as part of the indictment and subjected to proof beyond a reasonable doubt, any error was harmless, because a jury would have found defendant guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of killing a 60 year old man.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1748 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fuller


No. 1-00-1485


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 728; 756 N.E.2d 255; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 646; 258 Ill. Dec. 273



August 20, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 15, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. 99 CR 4496. The Honorable Mary Ellen Coghlan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, convicted of aggravated kidnapping, appealed his sex offender adjudication under § 2(B)(1.5) of the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act, codified at 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/2(B)(1.5), challenging the statute's constitutionality. He also argued that a legislative enactment amending several statutes violated the single-subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated kidnapping after stealing a van that contained two children. Under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 150/2(B)(1.5) of the Illinois Sex Offender Registration Act aggravated kidnapping of children by a non-parent subjected him to registration as a sex offender. The appeals court held that the statute as applied did not violate defendant's due process rights, because it survived rational basis scrutiny. Inclusion of kidnapping, a common precursor to sexual violence against children, was rationally related to the statute's purpose of preventing violence against children. The statute, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 152/120, that made aggravated kidnapping a Class X felony, for which a long prison term could be imposed, was not invalid by reason of its enactment in 1989 Ill. Laws 707, which amended several different statutes. The single-subject rule of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) was not violated because all the provisions dealt with criminal law.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Tittlebach (In re Tittlebach)


No. 2-99-1266


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


324 Ill. App. 3d 6; 754 N.E.2d 484; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 664; 257 Ill. Dec. 826



August 17, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 13, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Tittlebach, 198 Ill. 2d 606, 766 N.E.2d 244, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 25, 262 Ill. Dec. 624 (2002)
Petition for relief denied by People v. Tittelbach (In re Tittelbach), 2013 IL App (2d) 120463-U, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 382 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 99--MR--285. Honorable John W. Darrah, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) which determined he was a sexually violent person pursuant to the Sexually Violent Persons Commitment Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/1 et seq. (1998).


OVERVIEW: The State filed a petition requesting that defendant be evaluated and adjudicated a sexually violent person and committed to the care and custody of the Department of Human Services pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 207/15 (1998). At the hearing, the State presented expert testimony that there was a substantial probability defendant would commit a sexually violent act in the future. The appellate court held defendant had not demonstrated the trial court abused its discretion in failing to continue the dispositional hearing to obtain more information on suitable placement as the trial court clearly indicated that it had sufficient information to make its decision. It also held the trial court did not err in finding he was not an appropriate candidate for conditional release. Given the testimony of the three expert witnesses, the nature and circumstances of defendant's behavior, his prior and present mental condition, and what arrangements were available to ensure he had access to and would participate in necessary treatment, the trial court did not err in committing him to institutional care.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

In re Mehring


NO. 5-00-0057


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


324 Ill. App. 3d 262; 755 N.E.2d 109; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 640; 258 Ill. Dec. 28



August 13, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 96-D-905. Honorable Barbara Crowder, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother of the subject child appealed an order of Madison County Circuit Court (Illinois) finding her in contempt (and awarding attorney fees) for noncompliance with its previous order awarding appellee grandmother visitation rights. She challenged the constitutionality of 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(1).


OVERVIEW: A grandmother obtained an order allowing visitation with her granddaughter pursuant to 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/607(b)(1), and maintained a successful contempt proceeding with an award of attorney fees when her former daughter-in-law refused to comply with it. Although the trial court erred in failing to rule on the grandmother's fitness, the mother waived that error by failing to appeal it. The mother's subsequent contempt for the order was evident on the record, and the fee award was not an abuse of discretion. The mother's constitutional challenges failed. The best interests standard was not unconstitutionally vague, because other Illinois statutes listed many factors for consideration in applying it. There was also no denial of due process protections of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Ill. Const. art. I, § 2, because the statute was narrowly drawn to reach only situations in which the State had a compelling interest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

1751 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Hurst v. Capital Cities Media, Inc.


NO. 5-99-0194


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 812; 754 N.E.2d 429; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 633; 257 Ill. Dec. 771



August 7, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County. No. 96-L-103. Honorable P. J. O'Neill, Judge, presiding.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of April 24, 2001, Previously Reported at: 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 294.



DISPOSITION: Certified questions answered; judgment entered; orders affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant media corporation appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court, Madison County (Illinois) which certified two issues for the court of appeals in an effort to expedite a cause of action for false light.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff citizen filed an action for false light after he was identified in a newspaper article as having been questioned in a recent rape case. The citizen twice voluntarily dismissed his case, and twice refiled it. The corporation moved to dismiss the claim on the grounds that the citizen's claim violated the single-refiling rule. After significant argument, the trial court certified the question for consideration by the appellate court. The appellate court was also asked to consider whether identification of the citizen as a suspect in a criminal case in newspaper articles could be innocently construed as true so as to bar a false light cause of action. The appellate court found that nothing in the article charged the citizen with the commission of a crime. The appellate court found further that the article did not state that the citizen was questioned as a suspect, nor did it imply a sinister motive to the interview. Finally, the appellate court found that the citizen's claim was barred because the state supreme court declared the statute allowing multiple re-filing of pleadings unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court answered the certified questions, and entered judgment in favor of the media corporation.

People v. McLaughlin


Nos. 1-99-3612, 1-00-0117, consolidated


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 909; 755 N.E.2d 82; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 623; 258 Ill. Dec. 1



August 3, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 27, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. McLaughlin, 197 Ill. 2d 575, 763 N.E.2d 775, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1722 (2001)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by, in part, Motion denied by, in part, Count dismissed at United States ex rel. McLaughlin v. Bowen, 2003 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 16210 (N.D. Ill., Sept. 4, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 CR 27838. Honorable Edward M. Fiala, Jr., Judge Presiding.
People v. McLaughlin, 287 Ill. App. 3d 1114, 710 N.E.2d 570, 1997 Ill. App. LEXIS 2374 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 1997)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prisoner filed a petition, pursuant to the Illinois Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1, for post-conviction relief, and a petition, pursuant to § 2-1401 of the Illinois Code of Civil Procedure, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-1401, for post-judgment relief. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed both petitions, and the defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On February 15, 1996, a jury convicted the defendant of murder and, on April 25, 1997, his conviction was affirmed on appeal. On October 8, 1998, defendant filed a petition for post-conviction relief, and he attached an affidavit from an eyewitness who testified against him at trial, but who recanted. The trial court dismissed the petition as untimely, and defendant appealed and also filed a petition for post-judgment relief, which was also dismissed. The appellate court held that (1) there was a rational basis for the different periods the legislature adopted in 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1(c) for filing a post-conviction relief petition, and defendant's petition was untimely; (2) because defendant's petition for post-judgment relief was filed more than two years after he was convicted and he offered no proof that supported his claim that potentially exonerating evidence was fraudulently concealed, that petition was untimely; and (3) defendant failed to make a case necessary for using 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/116-3 to extend the statute of limitations for seeking either post-conviction or post-judgment relief.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

People v. Lindsey


NO. 4-99-0014


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


324 Ill. App. 3d 193; 753 N.E.2d 1270; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 627; 257 Ill. Dec. 644



August 3, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication September 7, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 98CF1094. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified and remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a Champaign County Circuit Court (Illinois) judgment on verdict convicting him of weapons offenses. He argued counsel ineffectiveness in failing to stipulate to prior convictions and in failing to move to vacate the unlawful use conviction, due process violations, and that one felony offense was really a misdemeanor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of unlawful possession of weapons by a convicted felon and unlawful weapons use. The appeals court held, first, that his trial counsel had not been ineffective in failing to stipulate to defendant's prior convictions before the jury heard about them, because at that time, the State of Illinois was not required to accept stipulations which, in any case, defendant had not offered. Counsel was also not ineffective in failing to move to vacate the unlawful use conviction, because it was not a lesser-included offense of unlawful possession. There was no plain error in allowing jurors to find defendant guilty under an accountability theory, because he could also have been convicted under a constructive possession theory. Finally, the statute making unlawful use a felony instead of a misdemeanor was an amendment to a statute that had later been held unconstitutional. Therefore, a shorter sentence was required.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed most aspects of the judgment, but modified it to reduce defendant's felony conviction of unlawful weapons use to a misdemeanor, appropriately modified his sentence on that offense, and remanded for issuance of an amended judgment of sentence in accordance with its instructions.
