In re Curtis B.


No. 1-99-2683


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 393; 758 N.E.2d 312; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 613; 259 Ill. Dec. 189



August 2, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Rehearing Denied November 7, 2001. Released for Publication November 27, 2001.
Appeal granted by, Sub nomine at People v. Leola B. (In re Curtis B.), 196 Ill. 2d 542, 763 N.E.2d 318, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1339, 261 Ill. Dec. 348 (2001)
Rehearing denied by, 11/07/2001
Reversed by, Cause remanded by, Sub nomine at People v. Leola B (In re Curtis B.), 203 Ill. 2d 53, 784 N.E.2d 219, 2002 Ill. LEXIS 624, 271 Ill. Dec. 1 (2002)
Different results reached on reconsideration by, On remand at In re C.B., 335 Ill. App. 3d 1180, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 5377 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois Child Protection Division. No. 95 JA 1105. Honorable Cheryl Starks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois Child Protection Division order changed the permanency goal for respondent mother's son to substitute care pending court determination on termination of parental rights pursuant to 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-28(3) (1998) of the Juvenile Court Act. The mother appealed. Petitioner State moved to dismiss the appeal for lack of appellate jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: The sole issue presented in the appeal was whether 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-28(3) (1998) of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, which provided for immediate appeals from permanency orders as a matter of right pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 304(b)(1) violated the separation of powers clause found in Ill. Const. art. II, § 1 (1970). A circuit court's order setting a permanency goal was not final because it did not finally determine a right or status of a party but instead looked at the anticipated future status of the child. The portion of 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-28(3) that allowed a party to immediately appeal a nonfinal permanency order was unconstitutional because it unduly encroached upon the exclusive power of the Supreme Court of Illinois to regulate matters of appellate practice and procedure.


OUTCOME: The appeals court granted the motion to dismiss.

People v. Herring


No. 1-00-1353


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 458; 754 N.E.2d 385; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 598; 257 Ill. Dec. 727



July 27, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 7, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable MARY ELLEN COGHLAN, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) defendant was convicted of two counts of home invasion and four counts of aggravated criminal sexual assault. He was sentenced to six years in prison for each aggravated criminal sexual assault, with the terms to run consecutively, and one year in prison for home invasion, to run concurrently. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant, who had attacked a woman in her apartment, argued that the State did not prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he committed the second of the four charged sexual offenses because the victim's testimony as to the second alleged sexual offense did not prove the element of penetration. Under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-12(f) (1998), "penetration" did not require physical penetration but merely contact. The victim testified that defendant exposed both her sexual organ and his own and, then, while she was face up and he was on top of her with his knees on either side of her, he tried to put his penis in her while he was choking her. The appellate court held that based on such testimony a rational trier of fact could have found that the elements of aggravated criminal sexual assault, including sexual penetration by way of contact, were proven beyond a reasonable doubt. Defendant also argued that Apprendi required his sentences to run concurrently because he was not afforded a jury determination of the aggravating factors used to enhance his sentence. The appellate court found no sentencing error because Apprendi did not apply to consecutive sentences.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

People v. Langston


No. 1-00-1421


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


342 Ill. App. 3d 1100; 791 N.E.2d 1; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 575; 274 Ill. Dec. 205



July 24, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 7, 2001.
Subsequent appeal at People v. Langston, 351 Ill. App. 3d 1168, 2004 Ill. App. LEXIS 5059 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 95 CR 16791. Honorable Themis Karnezis Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) which denied defendant's motion to reconsider the dismissal of his post-conviction relief petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and was sentenced to prison. The trial court dismissed defendant's post-conviction petition and denied his motion for reconsideration. On appeal, defendant argued he was not culpably negligent in filing his post-conviction petition late because of his reliance on his counsel's advice. The State responded that defendant's petition was properly dismissed because defendant's assertions that he was not culpably negligent were insufficient as a matter of law under Rissley, in which the court rejected reliance on advice of counsel as a sufficient excuse to negate culpable negligence for delay in filing. The appellate court agreed with the State. The appellate court determined that defendant's post-conviction petition was untimely filed pursuant to 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1(c). Further, the court noted that under Rissley, a petitioner was responsible for the errors of his counsel which resulted in a late filing. Accordingly, a petitioner could not claim that he was not culpably negligent because his petition was filed late due to his counsel's mistakes rather than his personal mistakes.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

People v. Landrum


NO. 5-00-0392


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 664; 755 N.E.2d 18; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 589; 257 Ill. Dec. 916



July 20, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Washington County. No. 99-CF-81. Honorable Lloyd A. Karmeier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant entered an open plea of guilty to one count of obstructing justice, a violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/31(4)(a) (1998), and he was sentenced by the Circuit Court of Washington County (Illinois) to an extended, four-year term of imprisonment, which was to run consecutively to sentences he was already serving. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: A trial court sentenced defendant to an extended five-year term in prison, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-2 (1998) and 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3.2(b)(1) (1998), after he pled guilty to obstructing justice and, pursuant to 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(b) (1998), the court ordered defendant to serve his sentence after he completed a sentence he was already serving. The trial court reduced the length of defendant's sentence to four years after hearing defendant's motion to reconsider his sentence, but reiterated its order that defendant serve his sentences consecutively. The appellate court held that (1) the only true factual inquiry involved in § 5-5-3.2(b)(1) was whether defendant had a prior conviction of at least the same or similar class felony within the previous 10 years and, because defendant's prior conviction was not an essential element of the underlying offense and was unrelated to that offense, the imposition of an extended term sentence was not unconstitutional; and (2) the imposition of a discretionary consecutive sentence under § 5-8-4(b) did not violate defendant's rights to due process and a trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

People v. Owen


NO. 5-00-0277


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 653; 752 N.E.2d 1269; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 570; 257 Ill. Dec. 89



July 18, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Effingham County. No. 00-DT-18. Honorable Richard H. Brummer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Effingham County (Illinois) entered a statutory summary suspension pursuant to 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/2-118.1 (2000), entered in conjunction with charges of driving under the influence of alcohol and drugs. The trial court denied defendant's motion to rescind the suspension. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A sheriff's deputy observed defendant driving over the speed limit and running off the side of the road and then back onto the road. By the time the deputy caught up with and stopped defendant, they had crossed over the line into a different county. The deputy noticed that defendant smelled of alcohol. When defendant got out of the car, the deputy saw a bag sticking out of defendant's pants at the waist, which defendant admitted contained drugs. After arriving at the county correctional facility with the deputy, defendant refused a field sobriety test and blood testing. The deputy cited defendant for, inter alia, driving under the influence of drugs and alcohol. The deputy failed to notify officials of the other county of the arrest of defendant. Defendant argued this failure invalidated his arrest and entitled him to a rescission of his statutory summary suspension. Although the deputy was obligated to notify the officials of the other county of the arrest pursuant to 725 Ill. Com. Stat. 5/107-4(a-7)(2000), the court held that an otherwise valid arrest could not be invalidated for a lack of notice of that arrest to another law enforcement agency.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

People v. Cochran


No. 2-00-0059


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 669; 753 N.E.2d 1155; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 593; 257 Ill. Dec. 529


March 21, 2001, Assigned; June 28, 2001, Submitted  
July 18, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 99--CF--1216. Honorable K. Craig Peterson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a Winnebago County Circuit Court (Illinois) judgment convicting him of offenses involving possession of a look-alike substance, arguing 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/404(b), 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/407(b)(3), and 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3(c)(2)(D) violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 due process guarantees and challenging sufficiency of the evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of possessing a look-alike substance in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/404(b), an offense for which fines were potentially higher than for offenses involving controlled substances, within 1,000 feet of a school, which called for heightened penalties under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/407(b)(3). This offense was not probationable under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3(c)(2)(D). Despite this potential for greater punishment, the appeals court held that these statutes did not violate the due process guarantees of Ill. Const. art. I, § 2. An earlier version of the statute creating the look-alike substance offense articulated two constitutionally permissible rationales for the penalties, and these rationales continued to justify successor statutes' application, and application of related statutes, to defendant. Defendant's challenge to sufficiency of the evidence was meritless; looked at in the context of drug transactions, the evidence was more than adequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Milwaukee Safeguard Ins. Co. v. Selcke


1-00-1973, 1-00-1979 CONSOLIDATED


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 344; 754 N.E.2d 349; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 564; 257 Ill. Dec. 691



July 17, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 27, 2001. Released for Publication September 7, 2001. Certiorari Denied May 13, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 3521.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 93 L 50663, etc., (consolidated). The Honorable Alexander P. White, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, insurance companies, sued defendants, insurance director and state treasurer, alleging they were subject to an unconstitutional tax. Earlier, the Illinois Supreme Court affirmed that the tax was unconstitutional and remanded the case. On remand, the defendants asserted the pass-on defense. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) ruled that the pass-on defense applied and certified four questions for interlocutory appeal.


OVERVIEW: Insurance companies did business in Illinois but were incorporated in other states. The suit challenged a tax that was imposed on foreign insurers. At trial after the initial remand, defendants for the first time raised the pass-on defense, which stated that in order to be entitled to a tax refund, the insurance companies were required to show that they bore the burden of the tax and did not pass it on to their policyholders, thereby receiving a windfall. The certified questions were: (1) whether the pass-on defense applied as a matter of law, (2) whether the plaintiffs had the burden of establishing that they bore the burden of the tax and did not receive a windfall, (3) whether defendants waived the issue of windfall, and (4) whether further proceedings were required with respect to the amount of the windfall. The appellate court found that there was a general policy against unjust enrichment through the refund of illegal taxes and the proper party to recover a tax illegally exacted was the person actually bearing the burden of the tax. The pass on defense applied, and was a refund issue properly considered, and initially raised, at the remedy phase of an action.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed. The certified questions were answered as follows: (1) The "pass-on defense" applied, (2) since the pass-on defense was raised by the defendants, the insurance companies had the burden of establishing that there was no windfall, (3) the issue of windfall was remedial and thus not waived, and (4) further proceedings were appropriate with respect to determining the amount of windfall.

Forest Pres. Dist. v. Loren & Gisela Brown Family Trust


No. 2-00-0289


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 686; 753 N.E.2d 1110; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 568; 257 Ill. Dec. 484



July 17, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 30, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County. No. 98--ED--17. Honorable Hollis L. Webster, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff forest preserve district filed a complaint for condemnation of land against defendants, a family trust, a corporation, and unknown others. The trust filed a traverse and a motion to dismiss. The Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) struck portions of the traverse and the motion to dismiss but granted the defendants' motion for summary judgment on the condemnation action and the parties cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: A forest preserve district passed an ordinance which authorized the district's executive director, his staff, and the district's attorneys to enter into negotiations for the acquisition of property owned by a family trust. When negotiations failed, the district passed a second ordinance which authorized the executive director, his staff, and the district's attorneys to "take necessary steps, either by negotiation or condemnation," to acquire the land. The appellate court held that, because it did not vest the district's staff with the power to determine the political propriety of condemning the property, but merely authorized the staff to effectuate an already approved condemnation action or to negotiate further with the property owner within definite guidelines set by the district, the second ordinance was not an improper delegation of the power of eminent domain.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the trial court's judgment granting summary judgment on the defendants' traverse and motion to dismiss and it remanded the case for further proceedings.

People v. Rhoades

OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the first degree murder of a 14 year old girl. At the grand jury hearing the evidence showed defendant had kidnapped, raped and tortured at least two other women, one of whom escaped. The other was discovered by a trooper chained to the sleeper of defendant's truck. The victim's body was found with bailing wire wrapped around her neck. People v. Owens


No. 2-00-0574


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 222; 753 N.E.2d 513; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 557; 257 Ill. Dec. 318


October 18, 2000, Assigned; March 7, 2001, Submitted  
July 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 9, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County. No. 98--CF--1378. Honorable George Bridges, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; restitution order vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The defendant was convicted of making a false report of a vehicle theft but acquitted of insurance fraud after a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois). The trial court sentenced the defendant to 6 months imprisonment and 30 months of probation, and ordered him to pay $ 19,468 in restitution, and the defendant appealed his conviction and the restitution order.


OVERVIEW: The defendant was charged with making a false report and insurance fraud after he reported the theft of a vehicle to police and allegedly filed a claim for loss with his insurance company. Evidence showed that he obtained paper title to an automobile owned by someone else, that he registered and insured the vehicle, that he reported the vehicle stolen, and that his insurance company received a claim for theft and issued a check in the defendant's name. The trial court acquitted the defendant of insurance fraud because the prosecution failed to prove that the defendant submitted the claim to his insurance company or that he cashed the company's check. The appellate court held that (1) the legislature supplied knowledge, and not criminal knowledge (i.e., knowledge plus criminal purpose), as the mental state for a violation of 625 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/4-103(a)(6); (2) the evidence was sufficient to uphold the defendant's conviction for false reporting; but (3) the trial court improperly ordered the defendant to pay restitution under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-6 because the defendant was convicted of violating the Illinois Vehicle Code, and not the Illinois Criminal Code.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the defendant's conviction for making a false report of vehicle theft but it reversed and vacated the trial court's restitution order.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County (Illinois) granting petitioner grandparents visitation rights to their grandchildren.

Section 607(b)(1) did not satisfy strict scrutiny, because the mother was fit to parent, the mother did not seek to terminate visitation, and the trial court failed to give special weight to the mother's determination of her children's best interests.

People v. Garry


NO. 4-00-0205


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 292; 752 N.E.2d 1244; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 550; 257 Ill. Dec. 64



July 6, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 6, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Garry, 196 Ill. 2d 552, 763 N.E.2d 322, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1405, 261 Ill. Dec. 352 (Oct. 3, 2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied United States ex rel. Garry v. McCann, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 10079 (N.D. Ill., Feb. 13, 2007)
Related proceeding at, Petition dismissed by People v. Garry, 2017 IL App (4th) 150373, 2017 Ill. App. LEXIS 540 (Aug. 22, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Macon County. No. 99CF940. Honorable Theodore E. Paine, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) convicted defendant of home invasion, armed robbery, and armed violence, 720 Ill. Comp. Stats. 5/12-11, 18-2(a), 33A-2. The trial court sentenced him to 45 years in prison for armed violence, 25 years for home invasion, and 25 years for armed robbery, with all sentences to run concurrently. The trial court denied defendant's motion to reconsider, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that he inflicted great bodily harm upon the victim, that the truth-in-sentencing provision in 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(iii) was unconstitutional pursuant to the Apprendi doctrine, and other errors. The victim testified that after breaking into her house, the defendant tried to intimidate her into giving him money or drugs. Defendant then beat the victim with a gun, and choked her. The victim was treated for lacerations, and suffered bruises. The victim testified that she had scars and damage to one of her hands from the beating. The court held this provided sufficient evidence to support the finding that defendant inflicted great bodily harm under 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-4(a). The appellate court held that the Apprendi doctrine did not render 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/3-6-3(a)(2)(iii) unconstitutional. The trial court's finding that defendant's conduct leading to his convictions resulted in great bodily harm did not increase the maximum penalty. Instead, the finding of great bodily harm simply had an impact upon the amount of time by which defendant could decrease his sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1766 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Schlemm v. Cowen


NO. 4-00-0689


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 318; 752 N.E.2d 647; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 548; 256 Ill. Dec. 767



July 5, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 5, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Menard County. Nos. 78CF17, 78CF18. Honorable M. Carol Pope, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Menard County (Illinois) denied petitioner prisoner's pro-se petition for a writ of habeas corpus, 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-101 through 10-137, alleging that his imprisonment was unlawful and seeking his release. The prisoner appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was convicted on two counts of murder and two counts of concealment of homicide, and was sentenced to consecutive sentences. The prisoner argued that the consecutive sentences were unlawful. The appellate court held that a writ of habeas corpus could not be used to review proceedings that dd not exhibit one of the defects set forth in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-124, even though the alleged error involved a denial of constitutional rights. The appellate court held that the prisoner's claimed errors were not subject to review under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-124. The prisoner did not raise any issue regarding jurisdiction or allege any postconviction event that would entitle him to release. The prisoner's claims that his consecutive sentences were unconstitutional or were otherwise imposed in error were not cognizable under 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-124. The appellate court further held that the trial court properly addressed the habeas corpus petition as a postconviction petition under the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 through 122-8.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1767 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Griffin v. Goldenhersh


NO. 5-00-0109


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 398; 752 N.E.2d 1232; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 539; 257 Ill. Dec. 52



July 3, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 98L554. Honorable Lloyd A. Cueto, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Questions answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client, who had his murder conviction overturned, sued defendant law firm which represented him in his murder trial 17 years earlier for malpractice. The law firm filed an interlocutory appeal on the issues of whether the statute of limitations and/or the statute of repose barred the client's action as well as whether the statute of repose was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The client was charged with a multiple homicide. The law firm represented him along with another defendant, claiming there was no conflict of interest. The client was convicted. After years of appeals, it was determined a conflict of interest did exist in the law firm's representation of the client. The client's conviction was overturned. Approximately 20 months after his release the client filed suit. The appellate court held the statute of limitations did not begin to run until the client's conviction was overturned since the damages were speculative until a final mandate was issued. However, the client's suit was barred by the six year statute of repose. Since, the repose statute was enacted after the alleged malpractice and the period would have expired prior to the statute's enactment, the client had six years from the date the repose statute was enacted in which to file suit. The repose statute was constitutional as there was a legitimate state interest in limiting the time in which suits could be brought.


OUTCOME: The certified questions were answered. The client's suit was barred by the statute of repose.

People v. Chaney


No. 1-99-1925


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 322; 753 N.E.2d 447; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 518; 257 Ill. Dec. 252



June 29, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 28, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 94 CR 12081. The Honorable Thomas F. Dwyer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions and consecutive sentences for aggravated sexual assault and armed robbery in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), claiming court error in allowing the victim to testify of her prior failure to identify and in imposing consecutive sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated criminal sexual assault and armed robbery after he and another person raped the victim multiple times. He was sentenced to consecutive prison terms for the sexual assault convictions. On appeal, the appellate court held that although the victim impermissibly testified of her prior failure to identify defendant, the error was harmless. In any event, defendant failed to object to the testimony and other witnesses had independently identified him. His conviction of aggravated criminal sexual assault fell within the second of the named exceptions to the consecutive sentencing bar in 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a), thereby triggering the imposition of consecutive sentences. Section 5-8-4(a) had previously been declared constitutional.


OUTCOME: The convictions and consecutive sentences were affirmed.

People v. Ephraim


No. 1-99-0836, 1-99-1267 (consolidated)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIFTH DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 1097; 753 N.E.2d 486; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 528; 257 Ill. Dec. 291



June 29, 2001, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois. 96 CR 15350. Honorable Stuart Palmer, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions of attempted first-degree murder and aggravated battery with a firearm and the imposition of consecutive sentences in the Circuit Court of Cook County, Illinois, claiming court error.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions of attempted first-degree murder and aggravated battery with a firearm after two children were injured by shots he fired from his car while chasing a rival gang member's car. The appellate court held that the trial court properly rejected his contention that two jurors should have been excused for cause. The jurors indicated they could keep an open mind and were not confused about the burden of proof. Minor equivocations were rehabilitated. Because defendant's intent to kill the rival gang member was clearly established, that intent was transferable to the injured victims. The trial court did not have to hold a hearing on the alleged ineffectiveness of counsel when there was no clear basis for the allegation. Each of defendant's individual sentences was within the statutory range established by the legislature and was proper under the Apprendi standard.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed in part and vacated in part.

 

1770 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Beyer v. Parkis


No. 1-99-1676


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


324 Ill. App. 3d 305; 753 N.E.2d 1032; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 538; 257 Ill. Dec. 406



June 29, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 21, 2001. Released for Publication August 28, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 91 D 4461. Honorable James J. Gavin Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; contempt order vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered an order, which: (1) granted appellee wife's petition for interim attorney's fees under § 501(c-1) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution Act, 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/501(c-1); and (2) held appellant husband in civil contempt and subjected him to a term of incarceration for refusing to pay $ 19,000 in attorney's fees to the wife, in violation of the court order. The husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the husband contended that the circuit court was without statutory authority to award interim attorney's fees under 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/501(c-1), because 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/501(c-1) applied exclusively to pre-dissolution decree proceedings. In the alternative, the husband contended that the application of 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/501(c-1) was unconstitutional, and that the wife's petition for interim attorney's fees was insufficient to support an interim fee award. The appellate court held, first, that the plain language of 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/501(c-1) was unambiguous, and that the legislature intended 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/501(c-1) to apply in post-decree proceedings. Second, because 750 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/501(c-1) did not foreclose the opportunity of an evidentiary hearing, but still allowed for a hearing where good cause was shown, it did not violate procedural due process. Finally, it was not an abuse of discretion for the circuit court to grant the interim fee award to the wife, in view of the uncontradicted representations concerning the husband's ability to pay.


OUTCOME: The order compelling the husband to pay interim attorney's fees was affirmed. The order of contempt against the husband was vacated.

 

1771 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Tye


No. 1-98-4342


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 872; 753 N.E.2d 324; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 488; 257 Ill. Dec. 129



June 26, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 28, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Michael B. Bolan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction of murder and death sentence were affirmed. He then petitioned for postconviction relief claiming ineffective assistance of counsel. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed defendant's petition regarding the guilt-innocence phase without an evidentiary hearing, but held a new sentencing hearing and sentenced him to life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that where a defendant took a direct appeal, the judgment of the reviewing court was res judicata as to all issues actually decided by the court, and any other claims that could have been presented, if not presented, were waived. The waiver rule could have been relaxed where the evidentiary basis for the ineffective assistance of counsel claim was outside the record or was newly discovered, but the record contained information upon which a claim of ineffective assistance of counsel could have been made on direct appeal. Thus, that claim was waived. In any event, defendant failed to show either that his representation fell below a standard of reasonableness, or that the claimed ineffective assistance so harmed him that the result would have been different. There was nothing to indicate that a motion to suppress filed would have been successful, so it could not be said that defendant was harmed by the failure to file such a motion. Defendant waived his claims of error regarding sentencing by failing to file a written motion following his resentencing. The lower court did not abuse its discretion in imposing sentence, so there was no plain error.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Tate


No. 1-99-1279


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 905; 753 N.E.2d 347; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 493; 257 Ill. Dec. 152



June 26, 2001, Decided  
June 26, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 28, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 00187. Honorable Stanley Sacks, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's sentence and conviction vacated. Judgment of the trial court reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of possession of heroin, cocaine, cannabis, and unlawful use of a weapon. On appeal, defendant challenged, among other things, the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that when police officers searched defendant's home, they failed to comply with the knock and announce rule. In so doing, the police found incriminating evidence. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress based on the officers' failure to knock and announce, finding that the evidence seized would have been admissible under the independent source and inevitable discovery exceptions to the exclusionary rule. The appellate court reversed. It was irrelevant that the information supporting the warrant was known before the illegal entry was made. The otherwise valid search warrant was executed in violation of the Fourth Amendment, and the violation was directly connected to the illegal entry. As a result, the independent source and inevitable discovery exceptions did not apply as exceptions to the knock and announce rule.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1773 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pickens


NO. 5-00-0533


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 429; 752 N.E.2d 1195; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 512; 257 Ill. Dec. 15



June 26, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 99-CF-8. Honorable Richard A. Aguirre, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and a partner robbed a used-car dealership and shot two people. A jury in the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) found defendant guilty of armed robbery, two counts of aggravated battery, and two counts of attempted murder. Upon finding that defendant was a habitual criminal, the trial court imposed life duration as punishment pursuant to 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/33B-1. Defendant appealed his sentence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, defendant argued that § 33B-1, which empowered the trial judge to impose life imprisonment based on the fact that defendant had two prior convictions of a certain classification, was unconstitutional. He argued that, pursuant to the rule of Apprendi, the facts that mandated his punishment had to be alleged in the charging instrument and submitted to the jury. Specifically, he argued that § 33B-1 was unconstitutional because a State officer rather than the jury determined that the requisite prior convictions existed and because that finding was not made under a reasonable doubt standard. The appellate court found that § 33B-1 was not unconstitutional because, under the rule of Apprendi, the fact of a prior conviction was not the type of fact that had to be proved to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt in order to increase the penalty for a crime beyond the usual statutory maximum. Accordingly, defendant's prior convictions, which were not elements of the later crimes, did not have to be alleged in the charging document, submitted to the jury, or proven beyond a reasonable doubt in order to be the basis for enhancing his punishment. The sentence was valid.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the judgment.

 

1774 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kenya C. (In re K.C.)


No. 1-99-0508


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 839; 753 N.E.2d 314; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 479; 257 Ill. Dec. 119



June 25, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 28, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 96 JA 866. The Hon. Carol P. McCarthy, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered an order granting appellee State's petitions to adjudicate appellant disabled mother's minor child a ward of the court, to terminate the disabled mother's parental rights to the child, and to appoint a guardian with the power to consent to the child's adoption. The disabled mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The disabled mother was adjudicated disabled under the Illinois Probate Act of 1975, 755 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1 et seq. The probate court appointed a plenary guardian over her person. She later gave birth to a child. At the subsequent hearings, the juvenile court judge chose to proceed despite being advised that the plenary guardian was neither named in the petitions nor served with notice of the motions. The appellate court held that the order adjudicating the child a ward of the court was void for lack of jurisdiction. The plenary guardian was a necessary party to the proceedings under 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-22, however, he was neither named in the wardship petition nor served notice of the proceedings. Therefore, the disabled mother was deprived of due process in the exercise of her rights under 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/1-5(1). Due process dictated that the plenary guardian was equally a necessary party to the termination proceedings, and he was neither named as a party in, nor served notice of, those proceedings. Therefore, the order terminating parental rights and appointing a guardian with the power to consent to the child's adoption was also void.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed.

People v. Vida


No. 1-99-2922


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SIXTH DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 554; 752 N.E.2d 614; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 491; 256 Ill. Dec. 734



June 22, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 13, 2001.
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Vida, 202 Ill. 2d 696, 783 N.E.2d 31, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 27, 270 Ill. Dec. 456 (Feb. 5, 2003)
Later proceeding at People v. Vida, 339 Ill. App. 3d 115, 790 N.E.2d 64, 2003 Ill. App. LEXIS 555, 273 Ill. Dec. 922 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., May 2, 2003)
Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by People v. Vida, 357 Ill. App. 3d 1088, 895 N.E.2d 696, 2005 Ill. App. LEXIS 3524, 324 Ill. Dec. 201 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., June 30, 2005)
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, Certificate of appealability denied Vida v. Hutchinson, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 111840 (N.D. Ill., July 18, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Frank De Boni, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Trial court's judgment was affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) convicting defendant of first degree murder and sentencing him to 100 years in prison, finding that his acts were exceptionally brutal, heinous, and indicative of wanton cruelty.


OVERVIEW: As a result of the brutality of the murder committed by defendant, he was sentenced to 100 years in prison. Although first degree murder carried a sentence of 20 to 60 years in prison under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(a) (1998), a court was permitted to sentence a defendant to 60 to 100 years in prison if the offense was exceptionally brutal or heinous indicative of wanton cruelty. 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-2(a)(1), 5-5-3.2(b) (1998). Defendant claimed that his 100 year sentence was unconstitutional, because the sentence was beyond the statutory maximum, requiring the trial court to submit to the jury the question of whether the murder was exceptionally brutal. The trial court was not required to submit the exceptionally brutal question to the jury, because the maximum sentence in a first degree murder case was natural life in prison. In addition, the statute used to impose an extended-term sentence upon defendant involved a consideration of the evidence regarding the particular offense in question after he was tried on the elements of that offense. Therefore, no new evidence was considered by the trial court in sentencing defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Pulgar


No. 1-99-1779


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FOURTH DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 1001; 752 N.E.2d 585; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 457; 256 Ill. Dec. 705



June 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 13, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE CIRCUIT COURT OF COOK COUNTY. HONORABLE ROBERT BERTUCCI, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for aggravated battery and commission of a hate crime in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), claiming the State used perjured testimony, did not prove his guilt, violated the one-act-one-crime doctrine, and his sentences violated Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery and a hate crime after he and another yelled racial slurs at the victim and hit him with their car. He was sentenced to consecutive prison terms. His motion for a new trial was denied, and he appealed. The appellate court held that even though no probable cause was found for the hate crime at the preliminary hearing, the State could subsequently seek and obtain an indictment for it. Since the testimony at the preliminary hearing was not knowingly false, it was not perjured. The State was not obligated to tell the grand jury that the testimony was hearsay. Since both charges resulted from defendant's act of hitting the victim with his car, the lesser charge had to be vacated. The evidence at trial sufficiently supported and proved the charges against him. Consecutive sentencing was proper since defendant had prior unrelated convictions.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for aggravated battery was affirmed and his conviction and sentence for the commission of a hate crime was vacated.

Reagan v. Searcy


NO. 5-00-0056


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 393; 751 N.E.2d 606; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 467; 256 Ill. Dec. 216



June 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by Reagan v. Searcy, 196 Ill. 2d 562, 763 N.E.2d 325, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1350, 261 Ill. Dec. 355 (2001)
Related proceeding at Reagan v. State Farm Ins. Co., 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 5, 2013 IL App (5th) 110251U (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County. No. 99-CH-726. Honorable Patrick M. Young, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) entered a judgment granting appellee patient's motions to dismiss appellant administrator's petition for a rule to show cause as to why the patient and his healthcare providers should not be held in contempt for their refusals to produce the patient's medical records in an arbitration proceeding concerning underinsured motorist insurance coverage. The administrator appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient and the decedent were involved in an automobile collision. The decedent died of the injuries he sustained in the accident. The decedent's estate was being administered by the administrator. The issue in the pending arbitration proceeding (proceeding) between the administrator and the patient's liability insurer was the patient's sobriety at the time of the accident. The administrator contended that the patient's medical records should be discoverable in the proceeding. The appellate court held that the physician-patient privilege (privilege) was not waived, and that the patient's medical records were not available to the administrator. The proceeding did not fall within the exception to the privilege set forth in 735 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/8-802(4), because it was not brought by the patient, his representative, or his beneficiary. The patient, who was not a party in the proceeding, did not waive the privilege merely because he previously made a claim against the decedent's estate. The patient's medical records were protected by the privilege even though the result was to bar information about the patient's sobriety at the time of the accident.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

People v. Carillo


NO. 5-99-0512


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


323 Ill. App. 3d 367; 751 N.E.2d 1243; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 468; 256 Ill. Dec. 406



June 21, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Johnson County. No. 98-CF-207. Honorable James R. Williamson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of bringing an item of contraband into a penal institution, a Class 1 felony and a violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/31A-1.1 (1996), after trial in the Circuit Court of Johnson County (Illinois), and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove to a correctional facility to visit an inmate and he followed a guard's instructions when he parked his car on facility grounds. Defendant locked his car and was walking towards the visitors' entrance when a guard asked if he could search defendant's car. Defendant gave his consent to search and the guard discovered a paper bag in the back of defendant's car with four unopened cans of beer inside the bag. The appellate court noted a prior precedent that equated bringing items of contraband into a prison with bringing those items onto prison grounds, but also noted that the legislature had greatly expanded the list of items identified as contraband and had amended the definition of "penal institution" since that case was decided, and held that, as amended, the statute used to convict defendant did not prohibit possession of contraband in areas not dedicated to captivity. The court also held that a broader reading of the statute would present a serious question of constitutionality because most people of common intelligence would not think to empty items that are routinely kept in a car, but which are defined as contraband under the statute.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant circulator appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) reversing a decision of the Illinois State Board of Elections (board) that overruled plaintiff objector's opposition to circulator's nominating petitions.


OVERVIEW: Objector initiated a proceeding before the board by objecting to the nominating petitions of circulator. The circuit court reversed the board's decision, and circulator appealed. The Illinois Supreme Court found 10 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/10-4 constitutional. People v. Avant


NO. 4-00-0183


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 459



June 20, 2001, Decided  
June 20, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

 [*1] THIS OPINION WAS WITHDRAWN BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion withdrawn, Opinion replaced: People v. Avant, 331 Ill. App. 3d 144, 771 N.E.2d 420, 2002 Ill. App. LEXIS 827, 264 Ill. Dec. 716 (Ill. App. Ct. 2002).


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 99CF701. Honorable Thomas J. Difanis, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of a controlled substance in the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), and argued that: (1) the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence; and (2) his conviction should be reversed because it was based, in part, on a police laboratory report admitted into evidence pursuant to a statute which the Supreme Court of Illinois declared unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by an officer walking the same section of a street several days in a row in a high drug activity area. The officer stopped defendant and asked if he had any illegal substances and defendant handed over a bag of crack cocaine. At the time he approached defendant, the officer had not observed defendant committing a crime and defendant did not appear about to commit a crime. Defendant argued that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence because it was obtained in an illegal seizure in violation of the Fourth Amendment. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motion to suppress because the officer had observed defendant's behavior for two to three days and knew the area to be a high drug-trafficking area. The officer's suspicion that defendant had committed, was committing, or was about to commit a crime, specifically, trafficking in unlawful drugs, was reasonable. Defendant argued that the appellate court should reverse his conviction because the only evidence that he possessed drugs was a lab report. Defendant forfeited this argument by failing to challenge the admissibility of the lab report at trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Bradley (In re C.B.)


NO. 4-01-0008


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 1011; 750 N.E.2d 1271; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 464; 255 Ill. Dec. 886



June 14, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 18, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of Champaign County. No. 99JA91. Honorable Holly F. Clemons, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father appealed from a permanency review goal in favor of petitioner State by the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Father appealed a permanency review goal for his child, who had been adjudged dependent and neglected, to remain at home with the child's mother as not being authorized by statute and as being against the manifest weight of the evidence. The appellate court held that § 2-28(3) of the Juvenile Court Act, codified at 705 Ill. Comp. Stat. 405/2-28(3), which made permanency review orders immediately appealable, was unconstitutional because it violated the separation-of-powers clause of Ill. Const. art. II, § 1, and dismissed the appeal.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.

People v. Rohlfs


NO. 4-99-0048


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 965; 752 N.E.2d 499; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 465; 256 Ill. Dec. 619



June 14, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 18, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 98CF574. Honorable G. Michael Prall, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for theft by deception and attempted theft by deception before the Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois). Defendant asserted error in the admission of certain evidence, the sufficiency of evidence, and fees and costs imposed at sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who was in jail at the time of the crimes, was convicted as a result of calling elderly women from jail, pretending to be a relative, and asking them to wire him money. At trial evidence of three other prison telephone scams with the same modus operandi were admitted. The appellate court held the other crimes were overwhelmingly similar to the crimes for which defendant was charged and there was a resulting logical inference that the same person committed both the charged and uncharged offenses. Therefore, the probative value of the evidence outweighed the risk of unfair prejudice. The appellate court also held the evidence was not so unreasonable, improbable, or unsatisfactory as to leave doubt of defendant's guilt. The appellate court did vacate the reimbursement order, as no appointed-counsel hearing had been held, and it vacated the $ 20 fine imposed by the clerk. Finally, it affirmed his extended-term sentence, finding that although the jury was not asked to rule on whether the victim was over 60, since the witness testified she was 93 the error was harmless. In addition, defendant's sentence was predicated upon a prior offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Walls

OVERVIEW: Following his conviction, defendant was sentenced to 50 years imprisonment. On appeal, defendant contended that (1) he was denied due process because the State failed to tender material prior to trial relating to the victim's immigration status and any pending investigations by Immigration and Naturalization Services; (2) defendant's trial counsel was ineffective for failing to uncover the victim's immigration file prior to trial; (3) the trial court erred in sentencing defendant to consecutive sentences because 730 Ill. People v. Nor


No. 1-99-1374


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 449; 752 N.E.2d 468; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 426; 256 Ill. Dec. 588



June 11, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication August 13, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. Honorable Fred G. Suria, Jr., Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the imposition of consecutive sentences by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) for first degree murder of one victim and second degree murder of another victim. Defendant asserted § 5-8-4(a) of the Unified Code of Corrections, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-4(a) (1998) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The State contended defendant had waived the issue of § 5-8-4(a)'s constitutionality because he did not challenge the charging instrument prior to the conclusion of his trial or challenge his sentence in a postsentencing motion. The appellate court held a party could challenge the constitutionality of a statute at any time. It also held Apprendi concerns were not implicated by consecutive sentencing, as consecutive sentences remained discrete and therefore a determination that sentences were to be served consecutively could not run afoul of Apprendi, which only addressed sentences for individual crimes. Thus, § 5-8-4(a) of the code passed constitutional muster. Defendant's sentences which ran consecutively to each other were not transformed into a single sentence, but were discrete sentences each within the statutory range established by the legislature. None of the penalties for any of the individual sentences had been increased. Accordingly, there was no Apprendi violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Cundiff


NO. 5-99-0534


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 426; 749 N.E.2d 1090; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 413; 255 Ill. Dec. 608



June 7, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 98-CF-125. Honorable John Speroni, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his guilty but mentally ill conviction of attempted murder of a policeman and the sentence imposed by the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois), claiming failure to prove guilt, ineffective assistance of counsel, prejudicial/inflammatory evidence, and sentencing errors.


OVERVIEW: Policeman was called to defendant's home after receiving a call that defendant was threatening construction workers. Defendant stabbed policeman when policeman approached him. Defendant was a schizophrenic, but was not on medication at the time. Defendant was found fit for trial. He filed an insanity defense. He was found guilty but mentally ill. On appeal, the appellate court found sufficient evidence supporting the verdict. Defendant did not prove legally insanity. Admission of the policeman's bloody uniform was not prejudicial or inflammatory. It was relevant to show defendant's intent to kill. Counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to that relevant evidence. Medication was not a "special provision" which qualified defendant for sentencing under a different statute. Defendant's sentence was within limits of statute in effect at time of sentence.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

Welch v. Ill. Supreme Court


No. 3-00-0143


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 345; 751 N.E.2d 1187; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 406; 256 Ill. Dec. 350


January 31, 2001, Assigned  
June 4, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 10, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County. No. 98--L--66. Honorable James L. Brusatte, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sued defendants state supreme court and supreme court justice alleging breach of contract and age and sex discrimination. The Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois) granted a motion to dismiss filed by state supreme court and supreme court justice. Employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: Employee alleged that after she began work for state supreme court, her promised salary was reduced. Employee's count against supreme court justice alleged that he directed her salary reduction in furtherance of his bias against her as an older employee, a female, and as a former employee of a political rival. The appellate court held that the State Lawsuit Immunity Act, 745 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/1 et seq. (Act), provided that the court of claims was the exclusive forum for lawsuits against the state. As the alleged acts of supreme court justice arose out of his duties as a state employee, the claim against him was also governed by the Act. Although a claim of malice could have been brought in the circuit court, employee had not pled the specific facts needed to take her claim outside of the scope of sovereign immunity. Employee's age and gender discrimination claims were civil rights violations and thus preempted by the Illinois Human Rights Act, which provided an exclusive remedy before the Illinois Human Rights Commission. Finally, the trial court did not err in denying employee's request to amend her complaint, as even after the amendment no cause of action could be stated.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

People v. Caruth


No. 3-99-0757 (Consolidated with No. 3-99-0758)


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 226; 751 N.E.2d 1160; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 399; 256 Ill. Dec. 323


October 18, 2000, Submitted  
May 31, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 22, 2001. Released for Publication June 22, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. Nos. 97--CF--5224 & 97--CF--5743. Honorable Herman S. Haase, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant pled guilty to home invasion, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/12-11(a)(2). He was subsequently tried by a jury and found guilty of residential burglary and aggravated criminal sexual assault, 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/19--3, 12-14(a)(1). The Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County (Illinois) sentenced defendant to consecutive prison terms of 14, 20 and 25 years, respectively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's arraignment was conducted without objection by closed circuit television. Upon the convictions, the trial court imposed consecutive sentences totaling 59 years. The issues on appeal were whether (1) the closed circuit television arraignment procedure violated due process, (2) the trial court mistakenly believed that consecutive sentences were mandated for all three offenses, and (3) the consecutive sentence imposed for home invasion was an unconstitutional violation of Apprendi. The appellate court found that since defendant did not object to the use of the arraignment procedure, he was obligated to show plain error on appeal. The appellate court did not find that the closed circuit procedure prejudiced defendant or impaired any substantial rights, so there was no plain error. Based on review of the record, the appellate court found that the trial court imposed consecutive sentences for residential burglary and home invasion pursuant to its discretionary authority under 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5-8-4(b). Finally, the appellate court held that the consecutive sentencing provided for in 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5-8-4(b) did not violate the rule of the Apprendi case.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentences were affirmed.

People v. Murphy


NO. 5-99-0535


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 271; 752 N.E.2d 19; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 379; 256 Ill. Dec. 475



May 22, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County. No. 98-CF-47. Honorable John Speroni, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for predatory criminal sexual assault of a child and aggravated sexual abuse by the Circuit Court of Williamson County (Illinois) claiming deprivation of a fair trial due to admission of hearsay evidence and abuse of discretion in sentencing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual crimes against a child. At trial, the child's mother repeated various conversations she had with the child about the abuse. Defendant was sentenced to consecutive terms. His motion for reconsideration was denied, and he appealed. The appellate court held that the mother's testimony was cumulative. Because defendant failed to object to her testimony at trial or to raise the issue in his post-trial motion, he waived it on appeal. The child was not required to testify at the reliability hearing, only at trial. The consecutive sentences were constitutional since the trial judge made no factual determinations. In addition, 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-5 mandated consecutive sentences if one of the charges against involved sexual abuse of a child. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing since it considered mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed, except as modified to include credit for time served to reduce the sexual assault fine to zero.

People v. Ware


1-99-3893


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, SECOND DIVISION


323 Ill. App. 3d 47; 751 N.E.2d 81; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 383; 256 Ill. Dec. 28



May 22, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication July 27, 2001. Certiorari Denied March 4, 2002, Reported at: 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1412.
Appeal denied by People v. Ware, 196 Ill. 2d 561, 763 N.E.2d 325, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1166, 261 Ill. Dec. 355 (2001)
Writ of certiorari denied Ware v. Illinois, 535 U.S. 905, 122 S. Ct. 1205, 152 L. Ed. 2d 143, 2002 U.S. LEXIS 1412 (2002)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Ware, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 3688 (Ill. App. Ct. 1st Dist., July 23, 2010)
Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by People v. Ware, 2012 IL App (1st) 103021-U, 2012 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 3199 (2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 98 CR 24643. The Honorable William P. Prendergast, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed conviction of aggravated criminal assault, and sentence to life imprisonment, by Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), arguing that trial court's admission of witness's prior consistent statement was plain error, that kidnapping was not separate offense from rape, and that jury should have determined fact of his prior conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant forced his former co-worker (victim) into a secluded place and raped her. The trial court admitted victim's mother's prior statements to police. Although the content of this statement went beyond the scope of the exception for early reports of rape, the appeals court found no plain error, because there was so much corroborating evidence. Therefore, counsel was not ineffective in failing to object. The offense of forcing victim into an area where her cries could not be heard was sufficiently separate from the assault to constitute kidnapping, which was properly used to upgrade defendant's offense to aggravated criminal sexual assault. Finally, defendant's prior conviction of the same offense was properly the basis for imposing a statutory term of imprisonment for defendant's natural life because prior convictions were the exception to the rule that aggravating circumstances affecting sentences had to be found by a jury beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. There was enough corroborative evidence to negate erroneous admission of evidence, kidnapping of victim was a separate aggravating circumstance, and prior convictions were the exception to the rule that aggravating circumstances had to be proven to support sentence increases.

People v. Watson


No. 2-00-0188


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 164; 749 N.E.2d 1078; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 386; 255 Ill. Dec. 596


May 16, 2001, Submitted; February 5, 2001, Assigned  
May 22, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 21, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 99--CF--2274. Honorable Richard W. Vidal, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the circuit court of Winnebago County affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his enhanced sentence for his conviction for residential burglary in the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), on grounds that prior convictions must be proven beyond a reasonable doubt pursuant to an enhanced sentencing statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary and given an enhanced sentence based on two prior convictions. Defendant contended his enhanced sentence was unconstitutional because the state failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt the prior felony convictions that were the basis of the enhanced sentence. Defendant's presentence report showed two prior convictions for burglary. At the sentencing hearing, the prosecutor informed the court that defendant was eligible for an enhanced sentence based on those two convictions. The enhanced sentence did not violate defendant's right to due process because the state did not prove the basis for the enhancement, his prior convictions, beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court noted that prior convictions are typically undisputed matters of record and requiring the state to prove prior convictions at trial would greatly prejudice the defendant with little corresponding benefit. The presentence report was all that was necessary to establish defendant's eligibility for an enhanced sentence.


OUTCOME: The sentence of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Swift


No. 2-99-1156


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 127; 750 N.E.2d 294; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 388; 255 Ill. Dec. 713


January 31, 2001, Assigned  
May 22, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 21, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County. No. 98--CF--465. Honorable K. Craig Peterson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his sentence for murder in the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and appealed his sentence. The facts upon which the trial court relied to increase defendant's murder sentence were never charged in the first-degree murder count, nor were the extended-term facts submitted to the jury in the instructions. The trial court's finding at the sentencing hearing of exceptionally brutal and heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty extended the potential penalty for defendant's offense beyond the 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-8-1(a)(1)(a) maximum of 60 years' imprisonment. This sentencing scheme violated the Fourteenth Amendment's proscription of the deprivation of liberty without due process of law and the Sixth Amendment's right to trial by jury. Any factors which acted to extend defendant's sentence beyond the statutory maximum must have been proven beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence for murder was vacated and remanded to the trial court to conduct further hearings.

Alpha Gamma Rho Alumni v. People ex rel. Williams


NO. 4-00-0744


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FOURTH DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 310; 750 N.E.2d 282; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 478; 255 Ill. Dec. 701


April 25, 2001, Submitted  
May 21, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 21, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Circuit Court of McLean County. No. 95TX1 (30). Honorable Ronald C. Dozier, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayers, paid 1994 real-estate taxes under protest and filed objections. Part of the taxpayers' complaint alleged that 73 taxing districts accumulated improper surpluses. The Circuit Court of McLean County (Illinois) granted defendants', state and municipalities, motion to dismiss as to some funds, and approved the parties' stipulation setting forth the amount of tax to be refunded. Plaintiffs appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the taxpayers' claims alleging unlawful accumulation of surplus funds in firemen's pension funds, policemen's pension funds, the Illinois Retirement Fund, Social Security, and Medicare, and in the levies of two home-rule municipalities. The municipalities also moved to reconsider and for leave to file a motion to dismiss the motion for leave to file an amended notice of appeal. The appellate court held that the taxpayers' motion to file an amended notice of appeal was untimely. The appellate court held the trial court properly dismissed the claims of unlawful accumulation of surplus funds in police and firefighter's pension funds. General rules prohibiting unnecessary accumulation did not apply when a statute authorized accumulation, and the accumulations were justified to account for unfunded accrued liability as required state law, 40 Ill. Comp. Stats. 5/3-125, 5/4-118. The trial court also properly dismissed the claims against home-rule municipalities, because the home-rule municipalities could exercise the power to tax, and no statutory limitations on the taxing power applied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re J.F.


No. 1-99-2106


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


325 Ill. App. 3d 812; 757 N.E.2d 905; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 375; 259 Ill. Dec. 42



May 21, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 29, 2001. As Modified on Denial of Rehearing of September 10, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit court of Cook County, Child Protection Division. No. 98 JA 04092, No. 98 JA 04093, No. 98 JA 04094, No. 98 JA 04095. The Honorable Eddie Stephens, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee State filed a petition for adjudication of wardship of the appellant mother's four children. Following an adjudicatory hearing, the Circuit Court of Cook County, Child Protection Division (Illinois), found the allegations of abuse and neglect proven, and held a dispositional hearing. The trial court adjudged the children wards of the court. Mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: Mother had not been personally served with notice of the hearing and was not present, although she was in court when the hearing was scheduled and her attorney was given notice of the hearing. The petition alleged that one of the children had been born with cocaine in his system, while the evidence at the hearing showed it was in fact a different child. On appeal, mother argued that the trial court should have been reversed because: (1) there was lack of proper notice of the hearing, (2) the evidence of the drug exposed child was different than that alleged in the petition, and (3) the finding of abuse was erroneous since the relevant incident was an accident. The appellate court found that mother had been given actual notice of the hearing in the prior court proceeding and her constitutional challenge to the notice provisions had been waived. The defect in the name of the drug-exposed child had been waived as well, but neglect toward one child could be taken as evidence of an injurious environment for the child's siblings. Finally, even if the incident in question was an accident, it could have, in conjunction with other evidence, supported a finding of abuse.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

 

1794 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Renner


NO. 5-99-0520


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


321 Ill. App. 3d 1022; 748 N.E.2d 1272; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 378; 255 Ill. Dec. 202



May 18, 2001, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Christian County. No. 97-CF-254. Honorable Dennis M. Huber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to driving while license revoked, and was sentenced to probation. Plaintiff State sought to revoke probation, alleging that defendant tested positive for drugs. Defendant filed a motion in limine seeking to exclude from a probation revocation hearing the results of a urine test by means of a certified laboratory report. The Circuit Court of Christian County (Illinois) granted the motion, and plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The probation order contained a provision stating that the results of drug testing were admissible in any proceeding to revoke the probation. Defendant argued that admission of the laboratory test results was hearsay, and that the waiver she signed in the probation order was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that at a probation revocation hearing, the State had the burden of going forward with the evidence and proving the violation of probation by a preponderance of the evidence, while using only competent evidence. Hearsay evidence was not competent evidence in probation revocation proceedings. The court held that the waiver in the probation order was not provided by statute. The appellate court held that defendant did not knowingly waive her right to confront the witnesses against her at a probation revocation proceeding. The appellate court held that the waiver condition of probation was outside the range of permissible conditions, absent a voluntary and knowing waiver. Therefore, plaintiff was required to introduce the urine test results by means other than introducing any written or printed laboratory result from a certified laboratory.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Steppan


No. 1-00-0751


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, THIRD DIVISION


322 Ill. App. 3d 620; 751 N.E.2d 32; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 361; 255 Ill. Dec. 938



May 16, 2001, Date Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 28, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. No. 97 CR 822. Honorable Michael B. Bolan, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Vacated in part and affirmed in part; cause remanded with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions of aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated battery by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), claiming ineffective assistance of counsel and court errors in retroactively finding him fit to stand trial and in its sentencing procedures.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated battery with a firearm and aggravated battery. He moved for acquittal or a new trial. His counsel withdrew because he was uncooperative. Defendant alleged ineffective assistance of counsel because no fitness hearing had been requested. The trial court found defendant fit for both sentencing and trial. The appellate court agreed because defendant understood the charges against him, participated in his defense, and recalled details about the trial. Because defendant failed to raise doubts as to his fitness to stand trial, he also failed to show that trial counsel's performance was unreasonable. Charges resulting from a single act were to be sentenced according to the most serious offense. The legislature determined that armed violence was more serious than aggravated battery with a firearm by making the minimum sentence greater.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence for aggravated battery with a firearm were vacated, and his conviction for armed violence was affirmed. The case was remanded for sentencing on the armed violence conviction.
