People v. Jones


No. 3-99-0919


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 236; 749 N.E.2d 466; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 344; 255 Ill. Dec. 365


July 7, 2000, Submitted  
May 11, 2001, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Modified on Denial of Rehearing May 11, 2001. Released for Publication May 11, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 12th Judicial Circuit, Will County, Illinois. No. 99--CF--650. Honorable Amy Bertani-Tomczak, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court, Will County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of unlawful possession of a look-alike substance with intent to distribute on public housing property in violation of 720 Ill. Comp. Stat. 570/404(b), 407(b)(3).


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's conviction, defendant appealed contending (1) his trial counsel was ineffective for not challenging his arrest on probable cause grounds, (2) his conviction should be reduced to simple possession, and (3) 730 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/5-5-3(c)(8), under which he was sentenced, was unconstitutional. Defendant's conviction stemmed from a substance found in his pocket during a search incident to an arrest. The appellate court found that the defendant did not establish the prejudice required to sustain his ineffectiveness claim. The circumstances supported a finding of probable cause. As such, there was no reasonable likelihood that a motion to quash his arrest for a lack of probable cause would have been granted. Further, the evidence seized from defendant consisted of 58 small bags containing a white rocklike substance. In light of that evidence, a reduction of the defendant's conviction to simple possession was not warranted. Finally, defendant's prior convictions were reliable sentencing enhancement factors because they were entered in proceedings where he received due process protections.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

People v. Rush


NO. 5-99-0092


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIFTH DISTRICT


322 Ill. App. 3d 1014; 757 N.E.2d 88; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 903; 258 Ill. Dec. 703



May 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:

THIS OPINION WAS VACATED BY THE COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended December 4, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Rush, 196 Ill. 2d 558, 763 N.E.2d 324, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1292, 261 Ill. Dec. 354 (2001)
Vacated by, Appeal denied by People v. Rush, 796 N.E.2d 1048, 2003 Ill. LEXIS 1476, 277 Ill. Dec. 682 (Ill., 2003)
Petition denied by People v. Rush, 2004 Ill. LEXIS 564 (Ill., Mar. 24, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County. No. 95-CF-126. Honorable Patrick J. Hitpas, Judge, presiding.

Previously Reported at: 748 N.E.2d 832 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.
People v. Rush, 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 369 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., May 11, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Court of appeals' prior opinion was withdrawn and this opinion substituted. Trial court's dismissal of defendant-appellant's post-conviction petition was affirmed but defendant-appellant's sentence was modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On appeal of the denial, by the Marion County Circuit Court (Illinois), of his petition for post-conviction relief, petitioner added a claim that imposition of a greater than maximum sentence, upon the sentencing court's findings of brutality and heinousness of the murder committed, violated the constitutional rule articulated in Apprendi.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder. The longest prison sentence that could be imposed without special findings was 60 years, but the trial court imposed a 75-year sentence upon finding brutality and heinousness. While petitioner's unsuccessful post-conviction relief petition was awaiting review, he added a claim that his sentence was invalid pursuant to Apprendi, the constitutional rule that guaranteed a defendant's right to a jury determination of guilt beyond reasonable doubt of every fact (except prior convictions) that increased his penalties. In the face of divided case law in its Illinois appellate district, the court reviewing dismissal of petitioner's claims considered whether the new rule fell within the narrow exception to the general rule of non-retroactivity in collateral proceedings reserved for watershed rules of criminal procedure. It determined that Apprendi fell within the exception, and that petitioner's sentence was invalid. The court therefore modified his sentence to run 60 years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed dismissal of defendant's original claims as frivolous, but agreed that the new constitutional rule applied retroactively to petitioner, and modified his sentence to the longest sentence that could have been imposed without an enhancement.

 

1798 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Amaya


No. 2-00-0099


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, SECOND DISTRICT


321 Ill. App. 3d 923; 748 N.E.2d 1251; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 353; 255 Ill. Dec. 181



May 10, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 7, 2001.
Appeal denied by People v. Amaya, 196 Ill. 2d 547, 763 N.E.2d 320, 2001 Ill. LEXIS 1162, 261 Ill. Dec. 350 (2001)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by Amaya v. Bartley, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 77806 (N.D. Ill., Oct. 1, 2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at People v. Amaya, 2013 Ill. App. Unpub. LEXIS 7, 2013 IL App (2d) 110305U (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 98--CF--535. Honorable Donald C. Hudson, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for murder, attempted murder, and aggravated discharge of a firearm by the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) objecting to the imposition of consecutive sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder, attempted murder, and aggravated discharge of a firearm. The trial court ordered consecutive sentences. It based its decision on its findings that defendant had committed a Class X felony, the offenses were part of a single course of conduct, and defendant had inflicted severe bodily injury. Defendant appealed the denial of his motion to reconsider the sentences. The appellate court found ample evidence to support a guilty verdict. Even if there was not enough evidence for a jury instruction on accountability, the error was harmless. Because the State failed to properly apportion the gunshots into a separate count of aggravated discharge of a firearm, and because it was a less serious offense, defendant's conviction of aggravated discharge of a firearm had to be vacated. Consecutive sentences did not extend the convictions.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of aggravated discharge of a firearm was vacated. All other convictions were affirmed.

 

1799 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


People v. Sharpe


No. 3-99-0668


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, THIRD DISTRICT


321 Ill. App. 3d 994; 749 N.E.2d 432; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 337; 255 Ill. Dec. 331



May 8, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication June 8, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit, Kankakee County, Illinois. No. 97--CF--142. Honorable Daniel W. Gould, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of the 21st Judicial Circuit (Illinois), Kankakee County, which summarily dismissed defendant's pro se petition for postconviction relief as frivolous and without merit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of home invasion. The trial court dismissed defendant's petition for postconviction relief. On appeal, the appellate court noted the sole issue was whether 1983 Ill. Laws 83-942, which amended the Post-Conviction Hearing Act, 725 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/122-1 et seq. (1998), violated the single subject clause of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. IV, § 8(d) (1970). The appellate court noted that another single subject challenge to 1983 Ill. Laws 83-942 had been rejected. The appellate court noted that another appellate court had found all seven sections of 1983 Ill. Laws 83-942 concerned criminal law or the administration of criminal justice. Therefore, it ruled that all of the provisions had a natural and logical connection to a legitimate single subject-the criminal justice system. Accordingly, the appellate court concluded the prior opinion upholding the constitutionality of 1983 Ill. Laws 83-942 was soundly reasoned, and the stated subject and the separate provisions of 1983 Ill. Laws 83-942 withstood "single subject" analysis.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of defendant's postconviction petition.

 

1800 of 2788 DOCUMENTS


Hearne v. Chi. Sch. Reform Bd. of Trs. of the Bd. of Educ. for Chi.


No. 1-99-1385


APPELLATE COURT OF ILLINOIS, FIRST DISTRICT, FIRST DIVISION


322 Ill. App. 3d 467; 749 N.E.2d 411; 2001 Ill. App. LEXIS 333; 255 Ill. Dec. 310



May 7, 2001, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 6, 2001. Released for Publication June 28, 2001.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County. The Hon. Dorothy Kine Kinnaird, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Upon notice of impending discharge, plaintiff teacher sought a 105 Ill. Comp. Stat. 5/34-85 (1998) dismissal hearing, prevailed therein, but was terminated by defendant education board anyway. Plaintiff sued for administrative review, mandamus, and declaratory and injunctive relief in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois); and won remand, then reinstatement. Defendants, including State Board of Education and administrators, appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff, belatedly, paid a theatre and restaurant some field trip costs, and a police officer alleged gambling took place in his classroom. The dismissal hearing officer, which found for plaintiff, gave him due process in a hearing with cross-examination, and submitted a well-reasoned detailed 13 page report with factual findings and legal analysis. In contrast, defendant board, which found against plaintiff, produced an unsigned, undated, uncaptioned half page conclusory document with an out-of-synch certification, and did not indicate that it conferred with the hearing officer. Plaintiff won in circuit court. The appellate court held that as credibility was the determining factor, as defendant Chicago School Reform Board of Trustees of the Board of Education for the City of Chicago had final termination authority under § 5/34-85, and as defendant board had reversed all the hearing officer's credibility findings, it should have conferred with him. Although the statute was ambiguous and contained mistakes, which the appellate court corrected, the legislative intent was clear.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
